O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	You, dear children, I have completed this book, which is the last of medical knowledge, its fulfillment, and have finished it through its explanations and declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I completed this with a treatise, which is a part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And since the work of hands is closely guarded in our region and unknown everywhere, the knowledge has decayed and become obsolete, and there is nothing left of its strength but small descriptions in ancient books about what the hands have done.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this has come error and vanity, and thoughts are closed, and knowledge is distant.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	It seems to me that I want to revive this treatise by ordering it according to the method of exposition and explanation, and bringing together the forms of cauterizing instruments and other tools used in the work, with adjustments to their declarations and preparations, as is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And for the reason that no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine has declined.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And he who would intervene in this matter must be well-versed in anatomy, as Galien says, to the extent that he understands the judgment of members, their shapes and connections, and separations; and has knowledge of bones, nerves, veins, and the number of their movements, and from where they emanate.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And Hippocrates says that ignorance is death, and knowledge is life; especially in the art of healing.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you in the beginning of this book that he who is not knowledgeable about the things mentioned above, risks making errors and misleading others; as I have often seen many of those who intervene in this science without knowledge or experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a great wonder that affected the abscess of scrofula on the neck of a woman, affecting the arteries of her neck; so much blood issued forth that the woman died in the woman's hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And I saw another wonder where a stone was extracted from an elderly man's bladder, and the stone was large; it carried away with it a piece of the bladder, and the man bled internally for three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to treat him, and I saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone; I knew well that if it were cut, he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another wonder, taking care of the duke of our land who had a broken leg and a wound from the fracture; the skilled surgeons, full of ignorance, tightened the fracture over the wound with strong ties, leaving no space for the wound to heal, and left it like that; and he commanded him not to unbind it; and so it was until the leg was completely swollen and painful and came to ruin.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him, and I hurried to unbind the leg; and when I heard it dislocated, it was completely at peace and did not feel any pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But every way of corrupting it was already confirmed in that member, and could not be healed; and the corruption did not cease to spread throughout the member until the whole member was destroyed.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I saw another wonder: the abscess, which had been healed, burst open again, and then became inflamed due to the evil nature of its lordship.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For the ulcer, when it is free of melancholic humor, one should not apply iron unless the part is in a position to remove entirely what is corrupt.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And for this reason, dear child, it is necessary that you know that the art of healing is divided into two parts: that is to say, work involving danger in many ways; and I will show you in each part of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	Therefore, be careful that the foolish gaze cannot speak ill of you; take up your weapons in courage and begin with your sick gently but firmly, using the best method so that by God's grace you may be saved and happy; banish diseases filled with grief through health; put away your weapons of doubt and have faith in yourself so that you can pass from this world to the next, full of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galen says in none of his warnings: "Do not take any ill disease too seriously, lest you be called a fool.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter is about fire cautery and medicine-based cautery, and it's ordered from the head down to the feet; and about the forms of instruments, and the tools for cauterization, and everything that's necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and the use of suction cups and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and this chapter also orders and describes the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar conditions; it ordains the use of the main joint up to the point of healing, and the shapes of the instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Thus, remembering the work, it is appropriate that I describe the qualities of aid and the potential harm of each condition.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the qualities of aid and potential harm are the most extensive and subtle knowledge, and these secrets are revealed; and many wise ones have spoken of them and agreed upon them; and I will content myself with their words, as I fear lengthening this discourse.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that cautery helps universally for every complexion where it has material, whether it is hot or cold complexion: that is to say, a hot complexion with material, and a dry complexion without material.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In a hot and dry complexion, there is material, they devised no remedy but said that cautery is great help; and others said the contrary: that cautery is useless for illness coming from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is hot, and should not be treated with heat for a hot illness through warmth or dryness; and he who says the contrary states that cautery provides great help to hot and dry illnesses that come into the bodies of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of man and its moisture with the color of fire, you perceive the body is cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	Because I have found this to be true through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And in any case, no one should attempt this except he who has tried it and knows through long experience the chapter of cautery, the diversity of the dispositions of men's bodies, the causes of their ailments, the remedies and the passage of time; for other constitutions we have only fear, especially for cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all of them marvelled and agreed to the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, child, that cautery uses fire in a way that is the essence of healing, and indeed it is much gentler than cautery with burning medicines.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and it does not come from outside unless it touches the hot member, and it does not harm any other member by itself.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Burning medicines travel from one member to another, and bring diseases of great suffering without healing; but by chance, fire, because of its heat and the goodness of its substance, does not cause harm if it is used in excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And because I have found it by experience and through the long service and study that I have devoted to this art, and in accordance with the truth of things; and for this reason, I excuse the length of my words, as I do not wish to disclose the secret that lies within fire and the quality of the work, how it drives diseases from the body, as the philosopher demonstrates; consider it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, my son, that they agree on the time when cauterization should be performed and chose prayers to recite.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cauterization is appropriate at all times, because the pain causing harm is removed by the help of cauterization; especially when cauterization is for necessary and urgent pain, so that no greater evil comes to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think, dear child, as they do who are unwise; for the disease that is healed by cautery has no return, and thus it should be; but it is not like what they care for, because cautery is only a medicine that changes the complexion, dries up the humors that cause pain, and acts more quickly than other medicines because of its power and authority.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And another powerful thing is that the disease comes according to the complexion of the sick person and the place of the illness and its power; and excesses accumulate in them through the acquisition of foods and similar things, except when cautery is administered where there are few excesses and moisture, as in cautery for pain and similar conditions, and such pain does not return; but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why cautery is called the last of medicine, and that's true; but they do not believe that cautery has any value after medicine, because when we administer remedies for any disease and they do not help, then we resort to cautery, and it is effective.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Then it is clear that cautery is indeed the last of medicine, not according to the opinion of the unwise crowd.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that gold cautery instruments are more effective than iron ones, and they only spoke of fire for the quality of gold and the excellence of its substance; they said that the heat of cautery does not cause corruption, but I have tried it and found it to be true in no way for any man; and gold cautery is worth more than iron, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And even when you heat the gold instrument, you are not sure if it is heated through by the color of the gold, and as soon as it cools down; and if it is heated too much, it becomes damaged; thus there is enough hindrance.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this, we use fire cautery because we have equipped it with our tools for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Therefore, I have ordered this chapter in the beginning so that the way to find it is more clear.
dou cautere olivaire	olive cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	Cyst cautery should be applied to moisture and coldness on the head, and it is effective for conditions caused by a disease known as "soda," and due to many humors that descend from the brain to the limbs and ears, and because of frequent dreams, toothache, throat pain, and especially for diseases arising from cold, such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is such that the patient is purified by a solvent medicine that cleanses the head, either the third or fourth degree of heat, according to the virtue and endurance of the patient's condition; and then the head should be re-covered with the medicine.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then make it sit crossed in your hands, and place both of his hands on each side; after that, put the root of your palm against the root of his nose between his two fingers; and leave it there until your middle fingers meet. If blood flows, then heat up the cautery called 'olive', which has this shape:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	Mark the bone with ink, and repeatedly lower and pull your hand in turning; then gently lift your hand, and check if you see the bone emerge; and if not, repeat the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you. Afterwards, take some string and put moistened and soft cotton inside, and place it on the wound, leaving it for three days; after that, cover it with butter-moistened cotton; and leave it until the burning is gone; finally, treat the wound with the ointment called 'tetrafarmacy' as long as it remains healthy.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And they say that the older a wound is, the more it bleeds; and for this reason, one must act quickly.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they say that one should not allow the cautery to burn off any part of the bone, and then remove what is burned from the bone, and it will heal.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And another advises that one should not allow the cautery to burn for too long, and push so hard that the bone is depressed as wide as a woman's womb, so that the humors can be discharged; and the wound should be left open for a long time; afterwards, it should be cleaned and bandaged.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of cautery do not seem good to me in every case, except for those in which there is no fear; and I think I should leave them, because the joint is weakened by continuous solutions of nature, as we witness in other members; and even when the patient's joint is weak by nature, the first appearance of cauterization seems safer and more mobile to me, and from this, I act accordingly.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	from the ancient pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When chronic pain in the head comes and lasts for a long time, patients should use herbs and pills called "cough drops", and purgatives for the head and eyes, and compresses; and if one performs the cauterization we have mentioned above, it is of no avail.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care if the patient's shoulder is of strong nature and not too frozen; then cauterize it from below, as we have said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After cauterizing each corner of the shoulder near the bone, as we have said before, and cauterizing the middle part called "vasselz," which is where the suction cups are placed, hold your hand lightly so as not to see the bone. The patient feels much greater pain from this cauterization than from others, and I will speak of it later; it is important that the cauterization of the corners be more precise than that of the middle part of the shoulder, and this is its form:
dou cautere dou chief	For fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When in a part of the head there is sudden pain, and the disease extends to the oil (or possibly referring to inflammation), and the condition is purged with medicines prepared according to specific methods, and all other treatments mentioned in the division of illnesses do not help, then perform cauterization according to two methods, that is, using hot or cold applications.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cauterization with hot applications involves pricking a sweet almond, removing the shell and the flesh (or possibly referring to the nerve or tissue), and then making an incision at the place of pain in such a way that you can replace the almond under the skin; and when it is replaced, hold it firmly and tightly for twelve hours. Then loosen it and treat the wound fiercely with salt, leaving it like this for two or three days, and then apply cotton soaked in butter until the healing process begins.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the treatment with herbs, as long as it is healthy; and if you see that something similar to what I have written about burning medicines occurs, then follow the proper treatment of these burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The fire cautery is done according to this method.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the fire cautery with this tool:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "clos" because the head is shaped like a clamp with a small concave area, and in the middle there is a slight appearance; place it on the painful limb, hold your hand, and twist the fire slightly until half of the thickness of the heart is burned; then remove your hand so that the artery does not burn, which is harmful, and let an abundance of blood flow out.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After placing cotton in awe of the wound, and keeping it on the skin for three days; then he moistens it with butter, and continues to treat the wound with care until it is healed; if you wish to cauterize this migraine with a cautery called 'cultellare', be sure not to cut the artery in this migraine which is not old.
de emigraine	of migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When treating migraine as we have previously discussed regarding the divisions of illnesses, and if beneficial treatments with cauterization recommended earlier do not help, then you must heat up the cautery called 'cultellare' until it is white; sign over the suffering wound a line half an inch long, and move your hand once, so that you do not cut the artery or cause bone damage; guard against the mandible becoming mute when chewing, ensuring the nerves only focus on muteness and spasms do not affect the patient; be wary of blood clotting in the artery after it has been cut, which can be especially frightening for those unfamiliar with this procedure. Leave the task halfway done. But I will tell you how to prevent blood clots once the artery is cut, and show you in this book where it is mentioned.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that this cautery does not suffice against the illness, and the patient suffers, cauterize again with fire both as we have said, and cure the wound until it is healthy; and if you see fit, apply the cautery from our chapter on the extraction of the artery, together with a cautery having two blades; and this cautery is better than that one and more helpful.

de litargie	De litargie" translates to "on altar stone

de la cure de fistule par cautere	On the treatment of a fistula by cauterization
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have discussed regarding diseases, and your treatments do not benefit the patient, then it is necessary that you perform cauterization on it according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to place their head on a healthy surface; then, with your hands, hold their head still in such a way that it does not move or wiggle its head; afterwards, apply moist cotton soaked in wine or pear juice over the wound; after that, heat up the cauterizing iron until it is hot. Position the iron near the head, shaped like a quill, so that it touches the wound; if you see fit, point it from one side to the other, and if you prefer, make it resemble a tent; nevertheless, whatever shape it takes, this part of the process is crucial for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the fistula, open it and drain the pus and dryness; if it closes again, work on it further and remove the bowels; then place hot cautery over the affected area, holding your hand steady above the cautery near the inflamed part of the oil, so that your hand does not cause harm; and apply the cautery to the fat in the oil, and dry it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you start the cautery near the bone, that would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If that does not work, repeat the cautery one more time, and if necessary, do so again after three days; then apply moistened butter cotton to the affected area and continue treatment with a healing ointment until it is healed; and if forty days pass and it is not healed, apply a corrosive medicine as needed until the bone is exposed; and follow this according to what comes in your chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a way of cauterizing a fistula that no one from the old days spoke of.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Understand the fistula, and locate its source; then apply a subtle heat to it, thus taking on this form:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	and it makes the quantity of a drop of blood; and hold your hand with the heat firmly, and do not let the patient move at all, so that the blood does not flow to its place; and one must put on the wound clean moist cotton in order for healing or otherwise: the blood quickly leaves the fistula and heals in a marvelous way.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have mentioned, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If this does not work, it is necessary to administer heat or cold, and bring the fistula back to the body according to what is appropriate in its specific place.
des crevaices en levres	cracks in the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times, cracks appear in the lips, called "poil," especially on the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these wounds as we have mentioned in detail, and the treatment does not benefit, then use a small surgical knife according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And apply the ointment to these wounds until it reaches the bottom; afterwards, treat the area with a healing wax until it is healthy.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess forms in the throat's root or uvula, or on the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, it causes putrefaction and swelling and becomes a fistula; then treat it as we have said in detail, but it does not help. Then you must perform cautery according to the size of the fistula; after opening or perforating the fistula, keep your hand on it until the heat has reached the bottom, and do not remove it until it is completely healed; and repeat this once or twice, following the treatment we have described for wounds, until it is healthy. If it heals in this way, that is good; if not, you must expose the area and remove the corrupt bone, as you will find described in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	no movement of the joints
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and treatment with medicine is ineffective, then place the patient's painful tooth in a healthy environment; afterward, apply the hot cautery to the area from which the tooth will come, in this manner, as you would place a cane over the tooth; and apply the hot cautery firmly, holding your hand until the patient feels the heat reaching the root of the tooth; then remove your hand and repeat the cauterization according to your desire; afterward, have the patient fill his mouth with salty water and hold it for an hour and rinse thoroughly.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this way, the tooth that was moving is firmly set, the soft gums are restricted, and the moisture is dried up.
de la dolor des dens	about the pain of teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When tooth pain arises from cold, or there is a chill or fever, and the remedies of medicine are ineffective, then it requires cautery according to two methods: butter cautery and fire cautery.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Butter cautery is performed by pressing melted butter into a copper or iron spoon, then wrapping cotton around the tip and moistening it with the butter. It is applied to the aching tooth and held there until it cools; this process is repeated several times until the pain-relieving effect reaches the root of the tooth. If the butter becomes too cold, it is reheated over a hot iron until the fire reaches the gum around the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	He applies the fire cautery, making it such that you press a piece of iron or steel into it, and if it's thick enough, the fire doesn't reach the patient; afterwards, he heats the cautery, from which its shape will form, places it on the tooth, and holds his hand until the cautery cools down; do this often, as the pain will subside that very day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it is necessary that the patient fill his mouth with good butter in the heat of this cautery, and then suck on a hot coal; and this is the shape of the cautery.
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make a cautery where you wish, according to your ability; and it is the form of the bone.
des scrophules	of scrofula
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When scrofula is of cold moisture and is not obedient to medicine, then heat the cautery with this after it forms, so that it has openings for the fumes to escape from the cautery to the other part. Place the hot cautery on the abscess once or twice, as necessary, until it reaches the bottom of the abscess; if the abscess is small, apply the cautery according to its quantity, and leave it like this for three days. Then apply cotton moistened with butter until the burning is gone. After that, treat the wound with oil and bandages until it is healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	The shape of the bone:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When moisture conquers the channels of the body, especially when it arises from a cold complexion, then it is necessary that the patient be first relieved by solvent medicines; after this, they should have fire cautery at the root of the throat, and be careful not to go near the throat, and only gently apply heat.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	After this, they perform another cautery at the joint of the collarbone above the spine, and these cauteries that are called "claws" from which we have the form before; and treat the limb as we have said above until it is healed.
de la toust	Of the toast (or perhaps referring to a burned area)
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all and any illness of the pores are caused by cold moisture, and the patient has no fever or chills, and it is an old illness, make two cauterizations on the strong parts of his body; and another cauterization between the two limbs; and this cauterization called "clavile" according to the shape mentioned above.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you see, make a cauterization by pricking all the cauterization called "poins" from which the shape is as mentioned above in the illness of the ears; and the points can be up to 30, or even more inside.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After the cure, the shoulder should be treated according to what has been said above, and the cautery should be performed in three stages according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And because the cautery is lighter, make three copies of this.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	Afterward, remind the patient of his pain on his back and side; afterward, ease the pressure inside the wound with your left hand's finger; if the joint is misaligned internally, apply the heat of the fire gently where it forms.
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	And cauterize the wound as deep as it penetrates to the side, and the shape of the cautery should be four cauteries; and for this reason, cautery is made with a cautery having three prongs, so that the shape of the cauterization consists of six cauteries; and the nerve corresponds to the subtlety of a needle, and it is the form of the cautery having three prongs.
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And never should it be adjusted on this nerve, for which there are eight cauterizations.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	After applying the cauterization, place crushed silk on it; then rest the patient, and do not move the limbs for a long time until they are well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it becomes dislocated from above, small things happen poorly, then cauterize on the thick lower part of the bone, or many cauterizations in sequence.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	Because the joints are closed, and the moisture is dried and healed the patient.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When coldness and moisture in the stomach drain it of its color, causing increased catarrh, and despite usual remedies, it does not benefit, then it is necessary for the patient to rest on their back, extending their legs and arms.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	Then make III cauteries deep under the knife, each with a width equal to that of a finger, and drive in the cautery; perform two cauteries on both sides, making the shape of the cauterize marks at three angles, ensuring there is enough space between them so they do not adhere together as they heal; make sure the cauterized marks are deep enough to penetrate both parts of the heart, and the shape of the cauterize marks should be as described without any distortion.
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if you need to cauterize with a large flame in the stomach according to this form, and whoever has fear of this cautery cauterizes by poking and marking on the stomach at one point according to the amount that you see; then cauterize across all the cautery that is called 'point'.
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment of the condition that we have discussed above, as long as it is healed.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	When the liver experiences pain from a cold and moisture and excessive flatulence, as long as it is deprived of its natural condition due to superfluities; and the patient is treated as we have said in divisions, but it does not help, so it is necessary that the patient be cautious about his head; and there are three signs of cautery according to this form and figure and quantity on the liver, expelling the humors, laying or cutting the veins where the pain comes from; and there should be a distance between each cautery equal to the thickness of two fingers; and the cautery should be long in the body, without pressing too hard with your hand over all the cautery; and it should only burn the middle part of the heart, and the patient should keep his legs straight and relax his arms; and if he cannot do that, he should lie down, extend his legs, and ease his breath; and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	And if you wish, cauterize these wounds with a knife, if you are subtle and wise in the art, but be careful not to burn the whole heart, for you would cause severe damage to the entire body; and it should not reach boiling, as the hearts are very delicate there, and only the wise can see.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When there is an abscess in the liver, and you need to know if it is within the liver tissue or in the peritoneum: if it is within the tissue, the patient feels moderate pain; but if it is in the peritoneum, they feel severe pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And when this cure requires the patient to rest on their head, it is necessary that the patient be comfortable and at ease; then apply the signet over the joint where the abscess is, and afterwards warm the cautery which resembles a spear, from which comes this form:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And cauterize with the cautery until the veins are burned, and a pustule appears, as long as the infection is completely healed; after the cure, follow up according to the treatment of wounds, as long as it is healthy; and it is not advisable to use this cautery except by those who have studied for a long time in the art of medicine, and whose hands these illnesses have never corrupted.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Then it can be daringly operated on, but I still think it is better to leave it.
dou cautere de pleuresin	The cautery of tears" is not a standard medical term in medieval texts or any
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients said that one must perform a cautery on tears with the root of an aristologe (a type of plant), and in this manner: take a long root of aristologe, as large as you can find, dry it, and make it as long and as thick as your arm; moisten it in oil, hold it over the fire, and cauterize (apply the hot root) between the eyebrow and the eyelash, and small cauteries downwards in the part beneath the beard; also cauterize between the fifth rib and the sixth, slightly declining behind; and cauterize across the midline of the lower body, and another on top of the stomach, and between the shoulders, and along both sides of the lower ribs beyond the deflected point. Do not press your hand down, but hold it open as if smelling something.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And they say that no old man should use fire cautery like a razor, scorching it and placing it between the ribs, until it reaches that abscess; and suddenly there is great pain, as we have said of the abscess in the liver.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this case, there is fear or the sick die now, and a fistula forms that cannot be healed.
de la mice	of the mouse
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of the mouse according to the divisions of treatments mentioned, and it does not benefit, then they resort to three ways of cauterization that are good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.
