Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	After you have drawn out the two flames until the bones are pierced on the other side, then quickly remove the cautery, and thus you will have four. And if you see that the cauterization is complete at three nails, do not cauterize the entire cautery at three nails.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the cure when it has been putrefied for a long time, then this should be moved more than the other treatments mentioned before.
de ydropisie	Dyshydration" is the English translation for
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cauterization is not indicated for the dehydrated, except in the manner called "asclytes".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	If your treatment according to the methods we have mentioned in sections does not benefit the patient, then you should perform four cauterizations around the anus, one on the stomach, one on the liver, one on the heart, and two behind the back on the spine, and one in the groin; and these cauterizations should be close to the affected area.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After leaving the cautery open for a long time to allow pus to drain, and never allowing treatment of the patient after the cautery; then healing will hasten, and the two intentions (or sides) will be healed together with God's help.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The shape of the cautery for the stomach should be like the claw that we have shown above; and for the back, it should be olive-shaped, according to what is set forth above.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of stones
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the stones are swollen in a hydropsic patient and are filled with yellow urine, you should cauterize on the back of the foot between the little toe and the ring finger; and gently hold your hand with the cautery without turning it.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And don't enter too deeply, so as not to damage the citrus tree, and perform the cauterization according to this form:
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After that, make two cauterizations on each leg, at the tip of a sharp knife; and perform the cauterization longwise, one on the inside of the knee joint and the other outside, along the leg; and leave the cauterizations for a long time without dressing, so that the wound heals; then treat the other wounds as we have mentioned.
de la menoison	of the wound
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	When the pain in the stomach comes from cold and moisture, and the retentive and digestive virtues in the stomach and intestines are weakened, and cannot be cured by any remedies; then you see the patient suffering greatly, despite having a strong constitution, and you perform a severe cautery on the stomach as previously described in the cautery of the stomach, around the navel with thin cauteries, and two cauteries on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see an abundance of moisture and the patient is suffering, perform a cautery on the wrist, and cauterize each part, and several small cauteries on the stomach to alleviate the great pain, as the cure is beneficial when there is good assistance.
de la cure des emorroydes	Of the treatment of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When hemorrhoids are of long standing and consist of corrupt, cold, moist humors, they are treated as we have said in the divisions, but they do not benefit from cautery: make three incisions along the spine of the back, starting from below the muscles and moving upwards in a triangular pattern, and one incision at the anus; if you think that the stomach is cold, the meat is not cooked, and there is bloating on the face, then apply a hot cautery to the stomach as mentioned above, and another to the liver, and yet another to the heart, using a cautery hammer; leave the cautery open for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After treatment, reset the shoulder as long as it is healthy.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshiness called "thelul
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you deal with the fleshiness (thelul), if the cautery appears too sharp, then set it on fire over the entire affected flesh; leave it in that state until the heat has reached the vein, thereby alleviating the pain. Repeat this once or twice, and if there is much flesh, cauterize each part as we have said; then apply beneficial remedies as long as they remain healthy; and if you cauterize with a large cautery on a hard surface, it will be more helpful.
de plaie mal curee	From the badly treated wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure cutting or opening, as we shall relate in its place, such a disease arises that it can only be healed by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When no vein is fistulous, but it becomes inflamed and discharges putrefaction and corrupt moisture, you must try all possible subtle treatments, and be sure to know the entire extent of its power.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	After heating the cautery that seems sharpest, insert it into the fistula according to the amount of the attempt's penetration, and repeat the cautery until the corrupt and putrid flesh is burned once, or twice, or three times, depending on the amount required; be careful not to burn the sensitive nerves and large veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	He should pierce the fistula into the bladder and intestine, taking care of these passages, and do not make a fire where it is meaty, and think that it is not poisonous; afterwards cure the passage as long as it remains healthy, and if the passages are closed, know that the passage is completely sound; and if the materials are not removed, know that the passage is too narrow, and the bone is corrupted at its base; and thus, as we will say of this in its place.
de la maladie des reins	Regarding the disease of the kidneys.
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When the pain of kidney stones and heavy urination comes and does not allow a woman to urinate, then it is necessary that you perform cautery on the kidneys from both sides with the cautery knife that we have mentioned above; and if we cauterize them in the middle, there will be three cauteries in a row, and this will bring greater relief.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak from pressure and moisture, causing the patient to retain urine, then perform a cauterization on the upper part of the bladder where the urinary opening begins, with the fingers, both right and left, making each cauterization as long as a thumb; also perform a cauterization at the back, if necessary; and make the cauterizations in the shape as described above.
de la marris	of the stomach
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the wound is cold and moist, and does not allow any healing, and the flowers of the wound are corrupted and their healing is delayed, then one must make three cauterizations around the wound, as we have said in the cauterization of the bladder, and two cauterizations on the back; and these cauterizations should be made with a clamp, as we have said.
de la hainche	de la hainche" translates directly to "of the spine
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When viscous moisture descends to the spinal column and for this reason it cannot move from its place, and the symptoms are that the leg appears shorter than the other when measured together; and there is found a weak back department, it is necessary that you cauterize the patient above the spine in a circular cauterization, marking in front of the spinal column around the area as it turns, so that the spinal column is within the circle; and the cauterization should be like that which was done on the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this cautery is not present for you, do three cauterizations of the olive oil, and let these cauterizations be as perfect as all the others; and heal it as soon as it is cured.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain in the back
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes from the back, and it is due to cold and moisture, and the patient is cured as we have said in the previous section, but the cure is ineffective, and the illness is long-standing, then you should purge the patient of heavy humors, such as bad pills or other similar good pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	Afterward, he performs cautery; and the method of cautery is according to two manners: that is to say, with burning medicines, and fire cautery.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Fire cautery is performed in many ways, of which one is: you cauterize along the ribcage, making three triangular cauterizations according to this form, ensuring good depth and width, with each cauterization spaced approximately two fingers apart, and they are olive-shaped. Never perform cautery directly in the middle of the chest, for there should be three according to this form.
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see, cauterize with the hot iron the circle that we have spoken of in the dislocation of the spine; but do it in such a way that the circle encloses the entire spine, and all the edges of the heart are burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is the method used in sciatica when the pain is confined to the spine and does not reach the thigh or leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if the pain reaches the thigh and leg, make two cauterizations at the place where the patient feels the pain, and one on the top of the ankle; the cauterization should be cut with a knife, and burn the thick parts of the heart; and if the patient feels that the pain spreads to either foot or near it, cauterize there three times or four in the spot where he feels the pain, which is called the "point.
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if the pain is so intense in the knee and extends to the thigh, make a cut with a sharp or circular instrument, and be very careful in all your cauterizations that you do not leave them too long, lest you burn the nerves and large arteries, and cause the patient more harm and contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen many who have cauterized the ankle of the foot, leaving it until the leg was completely swollen, and the foot as well, pierced and corrupted throughout the foot.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After an abdominal treatment, he died.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pain is in two parts together, apply cautery to one and the other according to this manner.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And the wise ones say about the cautery of the joint, which is the way, take a piece of iron, as thick as a new dime, or slightly thinner, and make it twisted and turned in such a way that there is a distance between one twist and the next, approximately the size of a thumb; and the twists should be on both sides, and they should look similar, and use a well-made iron, and this is its form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And heat it until it is completely red and oozes pus, then place it on the affected joint of the patient, and turn to the healthy side; apply cautery once again, and leave it for three days; then make a poultice with butter, and keep the wound open for a long time; after the dressing cure, as long as it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we should use this cautery little because of the pain it causes, and we should see few who use it; yet these are good cauteries, which the patient can endure, and where they are most needed.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The hot medical cauteries are made by using an instrument to cut a slit along the edge of a plate, which is either of iron or steel, attached to a long handle. It should be about as thick as a finger, open at both ends, and joined together in this manner.
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	After that, place the hot plate of the cautery on the patient's healthy side, and quickly place your hand over the plate; then pour between the two circles of the hot awl, which is heated over the fire for a little while, and leave it for an hour, allowing the patient to feel the heat and burn.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it has a true burning sensation just like fire; and when the burns have passed, lift your hand with the instrument and raise the affected area gently, leaving it for three days, applying butter until the blackening from the burn disappears; and let it be in this state for three more days after the treatment of the wounds, as long as it is healed.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And if the pain extends to the thigh or leg, use the instrument with gentle pressure according to what you did for the hand, increasing it gently; and this is the method of hot awl, which I have written about in the treatise on rectifying medicines.

ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	Where it has a small opening for the tip of a knife to enter; then place this pot into another well-sealed pot and add alkali and lime, stirring gently until there is a thick paste on top, leaving it so until the liquid in the sealed pot drains away. Then take all that liquid and pour it over the lime and alkali as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And thus it becomes very beneficial and is used in many medical works and cautery for other limbs, as it acts like fire, and with other medicines such as fennel, aniseed, and lime with soap, all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galen tells us of a treatment by which an honourable man was cured of the pain in his back and sciatic nerve, and the swelling, and says that no other cure was done, and he was healed completely once this treatment was performed, and he bathed as he teaches below.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And he says to do this in such a way that you press the fresh and dry niter (sodium nitrite) into a fine powder with some fat, and apply it to the back and thigh and leg where the pain is, and wrap it; and leave it for three hours or according to the amount of pain the patient no longer feels the burning.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then make him enter a bath until his body is slightly warmed, and make the water enter his eyes, and it will remove all the pain and heal him.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use such medical cautery unless after the evacuation of the body.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with goat's hair, it provides great relief; and the cautery should be done in this manner.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take lint and grease it with old oil, and apply to the fossa between the big toe and the other called the 'fossa'.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	After taking a piece of dry goat horn, heat it in the fire until it becomes charcoal, and place it on the cloth, leaving it until it stains; repeat this process, and do not stop doing so as long as you think it is necessary for the pain to cease; and this method of cauterization is called "goat horn cautery.
de la dolor dou dos	of the painful back.
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain arises in the back, whether from sudden impact or excessive blood let, or due to the presence of cold, expanded-seeming matter, none of these signs warrant cauterization, except for the one stemming from the infusion of cold material.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary after the patient is voided of foul pills or other similar things, that one makes incisions on their back, where the pain persists, in three lines marked with a cross, and on each line make V cauteries or more according to the virtue and quantity that the patient can endure; and the cauteries should be made according to the cautery called 'point'; and if you see fit, make III cauteries or IV at the middle cautery following this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This illness often strikes small children, and the signs of its onset are that they have a tight throat when they swallow, and pain; and you will find in the lower back a severe pain that radiates to the other joints.

Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	So the cauterization should mark every part of the wound equally.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see, cauterize around the wound with fire, marking two or three lines, and let the points be close to each other.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After the cure, hold the limb as healthy as possible according to what we have said, and be sure not to apply cauterization to any numb areas that are affected by nerve damage.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When the pain of joints is due to moisture that has spread to each member deeply, and when the pain comes suddenly, they call it "podagra" properly, and when it is from a cold cause and cures with no medicine, then it is cured by cautery in this manner: make a number of cauterizations around the joint of the foot, and let the cauterization be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if it is necessary to prick on the face of the foot, make a cauterization at each 'point'.
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come up to the knees and other joints, it happens often that he gets cauterized on each knee with three cauterizations or four of each part, using olive oil; and if you need more, do so, but don't hold your hand too tightly until the expected heart's heat is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend to the knee and back, administer the cauterization that we have mentioned in its chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, make two incisions around the fingers; and if there is no pain in the thumb, make incisions on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come up to the wrists or shoulders, cauterize each part, and do good governance for the patient and apply medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you govern it well and purge the flux, it will be healed by God's help.
de la routure dou syfac	Of the dislocation from joy (or satisfaction)
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When dislocation occurs in the shoulder and the bones descend into the armpit, it is new, and you should know that when you attempt to cure it, nothing must disturb that day; he should consume things that leave the stomach empty so that the bowels can descend from his belly. Then place him on his back between your hands, command him to keep his breath until the bones are healed, and rearrange them at your leisure, fixing the dislocation on the bone of the wrist, and make a sign on each side like half of a circle above the body; then heat the fire with this shape:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	as long as it is white and it sheds scales.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then realign the bones to their proper place; and have the attendants hold his hand so he does not return to the previous position; and stretch the patient's legs, placing pillows under them, and apply pressure with your hands; then take the cautery tool in your entire hand, holding it straight, and apply it until you reach the bone, and if you do not touch the bone on the first attempt, repeat this process several times until you do; be careful that the joint does not pop when performing the cauterization; do not burn him; and ensure that the patient does not die or suffer any other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that if you do not go close to the bone with the cautery, your work is worthless.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is necessary that the cauterization of children be subtle according to their size, and of adults also large according to their size; after three days, treat the wound with butter until the scald is healed; afterwards, cure other injuries until they are clean, and lay the patient on his back for forty days until the wound is well sealed; and it is necessary that his movements be limited for a long time, so that the boil does not appear when he goes to his room.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after forty days, when he wishes to rise, apply a well-made bandage and leave it for another forty days; and have good rest, working little and guarding against too much drinking and eating, and excessive laughter; and by following this instruction, he will be completely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And now I will describe the treatment for cutting in his chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the stomach
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures occur in other stomachs and are recognized, and you see that they no longer grow, hold the cautery near the wound according to its size, burning it a third of the way through; after treatment according to what we have said; and no one among the ancients has said that it should be cauterized with a three-angled cautery in this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first mark the place of the fracture with a sign of a cross and make a line along its length above the break, and another one extending from it, and hold your hand over the entire cautery area.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the initial treatments are lighter and more gentle.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in any limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain arises in any limb, whether from strain or injury, and this pain persists for a long time, and medicinal treatments are ineffective, then it is necessary to cauterize the affected area using a cautery instrument known as "a point," and the cauterization should be done according to the length of the limb, its smallness or largeness, and its strength or weakness, and the position of the twists and the intensity of the pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If the patient is healthy after the first cauterization, that's good; if not, start again with a new cauterization on another part of the body, as it often happens that the part closest to where the treatment was performed needs another one, so you should perform cauterizations until the patient is healthy.
de meselerie	It appears that your request is incomplete or missing context. 
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	These issues are never helped by cauterization, especially the illness that arises from the putrefaction of fluids and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	Do not burn the sight, be wary if the disease is in its beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, do not let it remain or linger, and doubt not that the corruption may spread throughout the patient; then make cautery on the head: first on the new growth, and the other towards the forehead at the end of the hair; and on both horns, and behind on the crown; leaving your hand such that the cauterization reaches the bone, and until the skin breaks out so that the vapors from the thick humors can escape; and cauterize the mouse according to what is appropriate.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules; et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	And if the malady is spread everywhere, and it appears manifestly, then you must cauterize these parts of the body with the cauteries we have mentioned on the head, and cauterize first near the navel, and second on the spine down the collarbone, and six times on the spine down the back, and one time on the hip joint and another on the side of the pelvis; and also on the elbows and on the tender parts of the toes, and each joint of the hands and feet, and in the pits of the hands; and be careful not to burn the nerves that are on the last toe joints, and never cauterize on the bone of the wrist, or on the bone of the stomach, or on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that the more you perform cauterization, the greater the aid it provides and the better the outcome; and know that the patient feels no pain from cauterization as a healthy person would, because the body is already corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cauterization be great and small according to the members and joints, as you will find in the manner of the irons.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After treatment, apply a poultice of meal with honey and other remedies until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When swelling appears in any member and is cured by medicines, oils, and bandages, but it is not completely healed, then make cautery on the member according to its size and the severity of the condition; and the cautery should go slightly into the hope of the heart; then treat with poultices until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And never should cautery be performed on the hand, foot, or back, at the end of a nerve that affects the member, and thus if the swelling is removed; nevertheless, no one should attempt this unless they are knowledgeable about the members and the passages of the moving nerves in the body.
de albaras	Of albars (or 'albaras' in Old
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is ignited, and the medical art has no effect, then cauterize with a hot iron, according to the extent of the wound, until the white (scab) is removed, and it changes color; then apply a cure of flour, beans, lentils, with rose oil, plantain leaves, collicon juice, and alder bark, each in a separate part; mix them together, wrap them in a cloth, and keep them on the wound until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment of a cancer by cautery.
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When cancer appears in its early stages and you wish to arrest it, cauterize it with a cautery that seems circular, encompassing the entire area around the cancer.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	Yet wise men say that one should also cauterize in the middle of the cancer; nevertheless, this does not seem good to me, as I fear it may become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have never seen it work successfully; and a more right thing is that it be cauterized around, with a cautery called 'circular', as we have said regarding many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	from the flesh that cannot die
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When anyone has a disease called "adubelati," and they do not want to die, either because of the excess it causes or due to the great age of the ill person and their weakness (that is, too much), and they have little blood, or because of time; and you see them hastening to die: then cauterize around with many small cauterizations by pricking; after which leave them alone.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For she will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it pierced throughout with cautery, make the cautery so hot that...
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	Place your hand in the middle of the disease called 'adubelati' as long as the cautery has pierced the heart, and make the cautery such that the patient feels no pain, in a way that the course of the decay is halted.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the treatment, until it is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	Heal the fire with iron.
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another kind of disease is called "corrodens", which is nothing other than a rotting of the member, as it attacks the members just as fire does dry wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in a member that can be treated with fire cautery, then heat the cautery clamps both very small and large, according to what is suitable for the member or the disease; after cauterizing from all sides until you have reached all the corruption, and leave nothing of it, so that everything that is corrupted is removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	Then leave it for three days, and apply oil to the cauterized member, rubbing it until all the burns from the fire are removed, and all the corruption is gone.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the treatment of wounds that cause pain.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if after three days there is no healthy growth, it is good; and if not, repeat the cautery on the limb that has remained stuck in a corrupt state.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this method is sometimes effectively cured with a strong medicine instead of fire cautery; however, fire cautery is of greater help, and I have already described the use of a strong medicine in the previous section: take as much as you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	From the particles which come as pieces.
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Many times it happens that a particle, due to some defect, is born with a disease called "close" according to our understanding, and it is a great fault that hurts the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cautery for this disease is according to two manners.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	That is to say, the fire cautery, and the hot water cautery.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	For the fire cautery, take a heated knife also as if it were a feather of a fowl, and make it from good iron to the extent that it can pierce the nail from all sides, and have thin margins; then place it hot on the nail, and turn your hand completely around the nail until it reaches the bottom of the nail; leave it thus for three days until it begins to produce pus; then make a poultice of bitter alder leaves ground with silk, and leave the poultice on all night, and the nail will break off and be uprooted from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then clean the wound with hot water until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they are moved by heat, the body's strength is often broken, and this happens many times in the hand and foot, then it is necessary to apply a hot water cautery; and it is done thus: take a rod of iron or steel, or a file, and place the nail and the rust on it, that is, verrucas; and put the rod around it so that it covers everything, then add a little hot water, and hold your hand firm, and press your hand while turning it so that the edge of the rod reaches the base of the nail, and can find the hot water path all the way to the base; and allow the patient to bear the bite of the hot water for an hour; then leave it as it is, and it will come out from its roots completely.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	First, do one after another, until you release all those who are in the body, then treat the wounds that cause pain.
li cure dou trembler	It cures the fear of shaking.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee; et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When anyone shivers from cold or quartan fever or any other ailment, it is necessary to perform four cauterizations or five on the spine of the back, one cauterization between each spine; and one cauterization on the fish, and one on the stomach with an olive cautery; if this stops the trembling and hastens the healing from the cold illness.
des pustules puans	from pus-filled pustules
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Never is it apparent through external defects or pus-filled pustules that come from deeply corrupted, putrid matter.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	it is necessary to act at first when they appear that one makes cautery on each head of the pustule: a subtle cautery with birch bark, from which the point is taken to the fire, or with long root of aristologue, or with lenticular cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And never should one cauterize at the beginning when they appear, according to this manner, and they cannot grow worse forward, but are broken off the excesses from which they come, and are healed; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	as the artery is cut off
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many serious consequences arise from the blood of an artery that is cut at a wound, or during the incisions into an abscess, or when cauterizing a member, and similar things; it is a very painful thing to endure.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	Nevertheless, if it happens to anyone, apply your index finger quickly over the vein wound, and pull very strongly until the blood stops completely; then take several small and large olive oil cauterization tools, as hot as possible, and place them on the wound. Then, according to the size of the wound, pick up a lot or a little salt, and with your finger hold the artery in place where it is cut, and place the cautery over that vein, holding it until the blood stops.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if a sudden sneeze occurs while you are raising your arm above the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, quickly take another from the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And continue to apply them one after the other until the wound is healed; and be careful not to burn the nerve, and let no further harm come to the patient; and know that when the blood flow from the artery cuts off, it cannot be well healed, especially if the artery is large, unless by one of the four methods we have mentioned: either by cautery, or extraction when it has not been treated, or tightly wrapping with strong thread, or applying medicines that have the power to stop the bleeding; and bind it and hold it firmly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever eases the pain by tightly binding the patient with cloths or placing hot objects on him, or other similar things, does not benefit but rather makes it worse.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to someone who does not have any suitable medicine, he should put his two fingers on the wound of the vein as we have said, and press firmly until the pain subsides from the wound and the vein; and do not move it, but apply cold water often as it becomes very cold until the blood is frozen and thick and numb; and prepare remedies in advance for what he needs cautery and medicine.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	We begin the second book of surgical treatments.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter about every illness in which it is necessary to use fire cautery or burning medicine, along with the applications and causes and instruments and shapes of cauterization; I placed that chapter on the most important parts up to this point, and now I will proceed to this chapter by the same path so that you may find it more easily than if you were to search for it elsewhere.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so, before I begin, it is necessary for you to know that this chapter involves more risk and danger than the first one on cauterization; therefore, greater care is required.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you not to undertake foolishness.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	Because many ways of people come for treatment.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	if they come from such who were so afflicted with their illness that they died shortly due to the severity of what they found in their illness and the magnitude of their suffering; and of these one should be afraid.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And there are those who give you their attention and say: "Wait, I am blinded"; and the disease is terrible.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	You should not give your consent to those who come to you with such methods, but place greater emphasis on your honor than on their self-interest, and act prudently, not foolishly, regarding what you are certain of, and what you can safely acquire; use prophecy and guidance in treating your patients, so that health may be restored; this will help you gain a good reputation, glory, and lasting fame.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear child, our lords grant you good understanding and integrity, and if you seek the holy inspiration from his hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	I have ordered this chapter for you, in devising by chapters, according to what is before or the chapter of cautery that I have devised from the head down to the feet, so that you may find more easily what you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	chief filled with water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	You know that this disease comes very often in children at birth, and when the child's head is too tightly stretched, no one knows the reason why it happens.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease except in children, and to all those that I have seen, death hastens; and for this reason, I think it is better to leave the work in parts for treatment.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw children whose joints were filled with water, and the head swelled each day so that it could not be supported; and the moisture was so great that it became a wound, gathered beneath the bone on the inside, between the heart and the bone; and the work is such that the moisture is between the heart and the bone, and the abscess is small, so you make a wide cut through the head; and it should be as long as necessary for the moisture to flow out; and see here the form of the spatum (instrument):
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is deeper, and the abscess larger, then make two cuts in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is under the bone, and you see the openings of each side of the head widely gaping, and there is a sharp, strong discharge when you press it with your hand inside, and it does not return, then you must make three cuts in the head according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, remove all the moisture deeply.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After loosening the cracks in bandages and powders, and applying wine and oil, leave it thus for up to five days; then remove it, and treat the wound with bandages and compresses, and continue to stretch the limb equally, and give the patient dry meat from a bag of moisture until the member is comfortable and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another method of incision is that you observe or measure the size of the abscess and the alignment of the water; for it never appears in front, nor behind, nor on the right, nor on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Measure then the abscess and the fullness of the water, and cut according to your ability; and beware not to block the artery; and quickly let out the blood, so that the patient does not die from slow bleeding and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	Of the flame cautery, 
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When a person has a disease called "cataract" either in one eye or both, and the disease is old, and medicinal treatment does not help, then the final remedy is cautery to close the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Therefore, when you see the patient turn their head back, rub the affected area with a rough cloth until the arteries open, then gently pull the skin away from the patient's body, checking where the vein is located, and ensuring the lines of the tendons are behind the ears and properly exposed. Then mark the lines of the tendons, and cauterize both using a sharp instrument, going deep into the flesh, making sure to do this across a wide area on top of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you see, turn the spatula under the artery and cut through the cloth above, cutting as well as it needs to go through.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, it bleeds continuously from above.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open by touching, it is necessary that you measure the quantity of space of three fingers, then tie it with a thread and make it go up to the bone; and what amount of blood should be put inside is six parts, or perhaps a little more or less, according to what the patient can withstand and the flow of the artery. Then examine the wound: if it remains on the bone without pus, cut and tie the wound and apply treatment until it heals.
de emigrainne	from migraine headache
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When an old migraine comes with catarrh, due to moisture in the eyes and sockets, and ancient exhaustion and similar conditions, and all medical treatments do not help, then we must drain the arteries of the eyes and apply heat, as we have described.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of extracting them is that the patient pulls out the hairs from their temples, and locates the artery which opens in the temple, as it opens well with its beating, and is very deep that no one who is not expert can reach it; and if it is reached, then the patient gently extracts a small piece of cloth, then rubs the area with a coarse cloth, and applies hot water until the artery appears clearly; then take the spatula with this shape:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	then scrape the skin gently until you reach the artery, then hold it with pincers and separate the threads that bind each part; if the artery is thin, turn it at the tip of the hook, then cut off that piece according to the quantity of two joints.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not cut, it will not heal completely without pain at all.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw out the blood from the veins of six, until three; and if the artery is large, it is necessary to tie it with two pieces of strong silk thread so that pus does not come before the wound heals, and no complications arise; then cut off the excess between the two threads at that very moment, and if you see fit, cauterize the wound with a cutting instrument until the joints are cut; this is the moving part, if the patient has no fever and is of hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For cautery is aid to finish moisture: therefore it is of greater aid against moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Where it is necessary for the extraction of arteries, one should fill the space with thick cotton and place several well-made bandages; and when they are removed, take care to apply dry medicines that create heat, and bandages, as long as the wound is clean; and if the artery bleeds heavily while you work, hasten to stop it with cautery, or use vitriol and press with your hand so that the wound is cleansed; and if you do not have this at hand, place snow on the wound until the bleeding stops, and then apply cold water as needed, and pull as is appropriate; and what is more mobile and lighter in the extraction of the artery is to cauterize the vein with this cautery cutting from both sides, but the cuts should be well spaced to retain heat for a longer time.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instruments are too tight, they hold less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus; et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it must have between the two blades a considerable space, and then, when you have sealed the two eyes, place the hot iron until it reaches the bone, and open the vein in two places; and they should be spaced apart between the two joints, because this cautery is not properly joined everywhere; and this is the form of the cauterization:
des larmes	tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears from the eyes descend into the veins that are on top of the head, and no medicine helps, you see the face of the patient contort, feeling as if from a chill, and the skin becomes cold and moist so that the hairs of the eyelids fall out, and the eyelids become scorched by the heat of the tears, then this cure is necessary.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they called it the "old cure," and for the patient with this condition, you should pluck the hairs from the forehead, then make three incisions on the forehead evenly according to its length; one incision is as if it goes all the way down to the nose, and the others are two on each side of the forehead below the eyelids, taking care not to cut into the arteries that are on either side of the eyelids. And keep your hand away from the continuation of the jawbones, making each wound about three times across. And have a piece of sponge and cloth to wipe off the blood, then use the sharp spatula part as shown:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the incision that is made on the temple down to the second incision; and scrape all the heart that lies between the two openings to all the satisfaction that is above the bone, then make another from the middle incision down to the other second, and then extract this spatule.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	if you insert the instrument called "cultelei" into the first opening, and it is very sharp on one side and soft on the other, this is its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	and place the sharp side towards the opposite direction of the heart, and the soft side towards the bone, and insert it until it reaches the middle opening.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the veins that descend from the neck to the last, until the incision reaches the heart; then make another cut in the middle, reaching to the other side. Then extract the blood evenly and press the wound to remove it; place a piece of dry cotton in each cut and cover them with moist cloth soaked in wine, oil, and ash, and ensure that no abscesses form.
