On the third day, loosen the bandage and administer a strong infusion of water, then apply basilicon ointment with rose oil, and other remedies to cure wounds, until he is healed.
dou reume des eulz	when the veins return to their original state.
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	If any catarrh comes that is accustomed to affecting the eyes, and you see them red and small, weakening sight, and burning papers; and hair falls out, and it feels as if there is a sharp pain in the head, and the patient sneezes, then know from these symptoms that this matter and catarrh do not come from only one cause, but rather from many veins, and the cure for it lies in addressing those.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And instruct the patient to press their forehead, then make a deep cut between the eyes, and another one wide enough to insert a finger.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	Starting from the cut on the left temple to the right temple, make an incision reaching the bone; move your hand away from the nerve of the temples that moves with blinking; when the bone is exposed, wipe all blood with a sponge, and then separate the two edges of the cut and place old cotton on it; then cover it with moistened linen cloths; afterward, wrap damp cloth soaked in wine and oil over it, and keep it from becoming infected. When the bone is healed, it is important to rub the bone gently until new tissue begins to form, then apply drying substances that prevent infection.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take two parts of wheatflower and three parts of chalk, mix them into a plaster; and apply it to these wounds to draw out evil by all means.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	ear infection
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Anything that causes an ear infection is one of the four things: grains, animals, mineral stones, or similar objects; seeds like beans, peas, or other such things; or anything flowing and moist like water and mud.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When anything that is not shaped to fit the ear, like a stone or other object, enters the ear and does not grow in the ear, it should be exposed to the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see a stone, and it exudes any drop of violet oil or oil of myrrh, then it is ready for extraction; and it causes clearing of the nostrils, and stops up the nostrils when sneezing occurs, and places pieces of cloth or wool inside the ear, and pulls the ear towards the top.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Many times this treatment causes fever; and if it does not cause fever, then it is ready for extraction with delicate pincers, the shape of which is as follows:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it jumps out with the pincers, that is good; if not, it is ready for extraction with a very fine, small hook; and if it still does not jump out, make a chain of iron and press the top of the chain or any hole in the ear firmly, and fill it with some wax so that the air cannot enter with the chain; then treat it carefully, because many times this causes fever as we have said; and if it doesn't work in this way, take a lot of care in doing it, and use a pointed instrument if necessary, and put some cotton inside; then press the clot on the stone or any object, and extract it.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if she does not depart from all the things that we have said, hurry to split the ear in such a way that the abscess hardens and the spasm subsides; and the manner of the incision is as follows: first make the patient with the cephalics healthy, extract the blood according to its strength, then place the patient between your hands and return the ear to its original position, making a small incision at the base of the ear where the fat or tissue is attached; let the incision be like a crescent moon until you reach the stone, then remove it according to your ability, and suck it into your mouth; and the cure as long as it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if there are grains present and they swell, then perform extraction; but if it cannot be extracted, then apply a delicate spatula according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and so forget the incision of that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not attempt this if you think the grain is moist from earwax, having made many attempts; then extract it with subtle pincers and suction, as we have said, so that the extraction is gentle.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the case that a chunk is extracted from the ear, it is advisable for the patient to use frequent sneezing and fill the ear with fine cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And lay bandages on that same ear, whether the chunk is inside or out.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If she jumps for this reason, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If the bone does not come out, take many thin pieces according to the length of your thumb and lightly heat them over fire; then insert the patient into an opening or perforation in their ear, and try from another side, and strike with another piece on the piece inside the ear; continue this process of piece upon piece until the blood has completely drained out, and thus it will come out entirely; and if you see fit, take a thin wire, insert one end into the ear, and heat the other gently over fire until the thinner wire is burnt; then make additional incisions with other wires until the blood drains completely, as we have said before.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	During the extraction of an animal, if it is small-sized, like a bug or something similar, treat it as we have said in the previous section; but if it is large, one must use pincers for its removal; and this is the easiest thing to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	When dealing with worms that have infested the ears, if you treat it as we have said in the previous section and the treatment of distillations, but the cure is ineffective, you should examine the ear under sunlight. If there are no visible worms, use fine pincers to remove them; if they still cannot be seen, take a stick and carefully extract them using the shape where they are located.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it should be narrow from below and wide from above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And then apply the most subtle suction in the ear according to the amount of suffering of the patient, drawing out all the air from the eardrum; do this often until all the pain disappears.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not come out, obstruct the eardrum with cotton as I have mentioned before; and if they do not protrude as we said, administer distillations that the ancients have tried in treating worms, and you will find them detailed in the section on distillations; and distil your oils and medicines into the ear using all these instruments, forming them as you see fit.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And take a fine blade of silver or steel, sharp at the small openings, and over them for distillation; and to press within the distillation with a well-made brass instrument, and if you see fit, take a razor and wrap it tightly around the tip with cotton; then pour your oil or juice, and whatever you wish from your medicines into the jar, and let the jar be in the ear; then insert the razor entirely into the cotton and press your finger firmly until the oil is distilled or slightly heated from the ear; and let the patient smell it, and make sure the distillation is not too cold, for the medicine would not be as good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	ear candling
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born with any perforation in their ears; and the same thing happens to adults due to a blow or an arrow entering the ear, and this obstruction never fully closes in the ear unless one can see it; and sometimes the perforation becomes closed, but not completely.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	When the obstruction fully closes, if one cannot see it, it is a matter of poor healing in various ways, and in this case, you should place the patient's ear towards the sun; and look inside. If you see the inflation clearly, you will see that this is due to the swelling and shape of its contents.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And make cuts and incisions all around, front and back, so that the ear is not damaged; if the pain is from a wound or a bone in the ear, hold it with fine pincers and gently pull until the whole bone is extracted.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	If the incision is deep in the ear, take a fine and sharp razor, heat it slightly over the fire, and then apply it to the wound in the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the incision causing great pain in the ear, make a slight perforation, and be careful not to damage the nerves of the ear; then insert into the ear a plug according to the width of the opening, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Keep the bandage on as long as the wound is fresh, or take a cloth and moisten it in rosewater, and sprinkle vitriol powder on it; and if you notice the ear is swollen, it is necessary to remove the bandage and replace it with another moistened cloth in cerate made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is gone; then treat it as long as it is clean.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if the onset of swelling occurs, immerse a sponge and wrap it in cold water, and place it on the ear, and use other treatments to remove the swelling caused by distillations.
de la char des papieres	Of the work of papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	Always know that when papers come in moist and dry, it is necessary to extend them with tongs and pincers, taking care to cut off a piece of spatula from their roots; then place the crushed glass over them.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if, after peeling, the cautery is performed with a delicate lenticular cautery, and the cauterizer after the incision moves; and often they repair themselves, since nothing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized with fire, those roots are burned and do not grow back.
de la gresle	from the frost
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times come to paper certain things that seem greasy in their form and hardness, and for this reason this disease is called "grandine," which is a gathering of great moisture on top and bottom of the paper; the work is as follows: take care if the grandine becomes silent from one side or the other, and it is a light thing to know; then make them wide, scrape gently from each part, and take hold with pincers, and cut.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot cover it without piercing the paper slightly, it does not harm the patient; and if the split is great, if the gathering has a stitch, treat it as long as it remains healthy; and if it is small, do not make much effort, because the stitches will soon return and cause trouble.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the pain is descending inside the ear towards the upper part, turn the paper and the pain will grasp it with a squeeze, and the head and neck press from both sides; but if the paper is moved by incision, it causes no harm; and when the pain is cut away, wash it with salt water and heal the place that caused it until the patient is cured.
de la graisse des eulz	from the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Xerophthalmia is a fat that is embedded in the layers of paper-like skin over the eyes, and it occurs more often in children than in adults, causing great pain to their eyes. It leads to cataracts forming in the morning, preventing them from bearing the light of the sun because tears flow constantly. Due to this, they keep their eyes closed at night and sleep on them, and the skin beneath their eyebrows becomes moist from the tears, appearing swollen and covered with a film of fat that opens up in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the joint with your fingers and feel the pain between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the method of performing this procedure is that the patient places his head in a healthy position, then takes a linen cloth and prepares a tent-like structure according to the amount of blood from each part, placing it on top; and presses with his fingers on both sides so that the blood collects within the circular area, making a groove with a sharp spatula, no wider than the wound made in a vein, and makes the skin completely smooth; and in various ways, more blood may come out from the groove, forming like a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Take therefore a whole piece of cloth between your fingers over the wound, and turn your hand to the right and left until it is spread; and be careful not to press into the fissure, do not go all the way to the oil, or you will tear it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the fissure does not open at first, slightly widen it until it opens; then extract as we have said, and apply moist cloth in hot water, and place on the wound, and twist gently.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And for such men who grind and put on anything to corrupt the moisture that is lingering.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it as long as it is healthy.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it turns to a hot abscess, treat the wound with soothing remedies as long as it is healthy.
des poilz des papieres	hairs of paper
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs grow abnormally on paper (or perhaps the skin), they become irritated, causing as much harm as those that are by nature, and lead to conditions like tears in the paper (or skin) and molting, and white spots; this is due to the destruction of the hair follicles. The cure is through four methods: cauterization with fire, ague medicine according to the chapter on cautery, or by incision and stitching, or using bands, as I will explain.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You should place the sick person's head in your healthy hand, then turn the paper from oil on your left hand; if it turns, that is good; if not, push an needle through all the threads above; and take care to cut the hairs at the edge of the paper or where they grow out, cutting them all along the entire paper, and turn it against the razor. Then make a cut in the paper, beneath the adjusted hairs, from the large tear to the small one; then extract the thread, and place beneath the paper a small piece of cotton and cloth, and sign on the paper a figure of a cross, as if from a sprig of myrtle, and nevertheless, it is important that the figure be according to the quantity you lift with the paper, which is measured in all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if you take a sharp knife and cut a great quantity of paper according to how soft it is; then make a small slit along all two lines that you have marked, and begin with a large tear from the corner to the edge, making one cut in each of the two angles, then remove the flesh entirely; join the two edges with a single stitch using fine wool thread, and dry the blood, wiping away any surplus thread on both sides with anything sticky. If this is not done, leave the stitches and thread for three or four days, then treat the wound without stitching using drying and constricting substances, because the paper revives when the wound heals and the stitching holds it together, but the stitch moves (as the ancients say), which causes pain; and if in another way: you mark the paper with a shape similar to the seal of myrrh, as we have described, at three points according to the form shown here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut off what overcomes the small forces equally according to the shape that is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you cannot hold the pincers, and the matter is not equal, take a needle with thread, and tie it around the edge; then take another thread beneath the large wound, and the third thread beneath the small one, and bind them equally between your fingers; then gently lower your hand equally, and remove all the skin you have marked, as we have said; then sew together the two edges of the wound with stitches, and treat it until it is healed; and if an abscess forms at your incision, soothe it with soot or similar soothing remedies; and sometimes the paper-like skin becomes detached. It is necessary to use what we have said about the incision; but stitching in both directions is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment for the cramp (or spasm) is as follows: and it is that you turn the paper and make it inside according to what I have said, then make two strips of it by art, also thin and long like the paper and wide enough with a spatula; hold both parts where you hold the limbs; then assemble them gently on top of the paper from the oil, pull the two strips from the formed parts; leave it like this for several days, and the muscle that is restrained will die, shrivel, and waste away until it disappears.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is delayed and the muscles have strength, then treat it while they are healthy; and when the wound is healed, and if lifting the paper does not cause any hair to grow back, then make the strips according to this figure and this amount of length and width.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work involves inserting a fine needle and threading it with soft, thin silk thread; then gathering the fragments together and tying them gently, making the length of the threads one palm's length. Next, arrange another thin silk thread swiftly and tie the ends loosely. Place the patient's head in your hand, and let the operation be revealed as it is a delicate one. Because the needle should pierce the skin just below the root of the hair, adjusting it to the natural skin, until you pull the thread from above the hair. Then extract the hair all the way up to the surface of the paper with the silk thread, and if there are one or two or three or more hairs, insert your hand until the hairs are completely detached from the paper along with the natural skin.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the hair does not come out with the pull, you will pull the hunt out by the root along the entire thread that you have ordered, until the hunt is completely pulled out from the opening and you see it through the eye of the needle; then you will pull the hunt and the thread, and close the eye and leave it for one or two days, until the hair grows back in its place and the scar heals. And if the hairs are small, accompany them with a long hair from a natural horse, and raise them along with the one you leave, until they become elongated and then remove them.
de la porriture de l’oil	regarding the impurities of the oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this illness called "aleacrati" or putrefaction comes upon the body, it can be in two ways: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it occurs suddenly from wounds, or cutting, or cautery, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the manner of performing this operation is that you open the wound, separate the edges, and place linen strips inside, binding them until the wound is healed; and it does not suit that you use in the treatment of it things that dry and restrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the illness returns worse than before; but it does involve softening things, such as fenugreek; and rosewater of water or linseed cooked, and oil of garlic melted in either eye, and wraps around a bandage, and treats it thusly.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the true value of your cure lies in being careful that it does not adhere to the shape it once was; and this work that we have mentioned is not only a remedy for this illness, but prevents it from returning to its previous form.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the matter that comes to the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This illness, which is dislocation, is truly called "axacrati," it is both natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from wounds, incisions, cauterization, and similar things; and the outcome of this chapter is such that if you prick a needle into it, the thread doubles up, and you insert it into the flesh, piercing from the left eyelid to the right, so that the thread passes through both sides of the eye socket; then the socket becomes closed over the entire needle, and the cover is wide at the spatula.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the paper returns according to what is necessary, that is good; but if not, take a razor and insert it into the fissure, turn the paper, and make two cuts on either side inside the paper; and let the edges of these two cuts form two angles of the incision you have made, so that when they are brought together, the shape resembles a letter with no "griesche" (a medieval writing error); then remove the paper, according to how much its edges are aligned, from the side facing the flesh, and adjust the two irregular parts, stitching them with a thread of wool; finally, apply the treatments we have mentioned regarding mollifying medications and bandages until it is healed.

And if the illness arises from cutting or stitching or cauterization, then you should make an even cut beneath the skin and between the hair follicles, following what has been said above; then separate the two halves of a single cloth, as I have mentioned; and one must perform the work according to the nature of the illness, for it varies greatly in form, and skilled physicians devise various means to restore its natural shape; and the patients themselves, according to what they need for treatment and instruments, in different dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	The phrase "dou soudement de la papiere" does not have a clear or direct

de l’ungle de l’oil	from the nail of the finger
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	You know that the nail has two manners: it is nervous and resembles a hard, smooth stone, and another which is not nervous but resembles white, frozen moisture, that when you touch it with iron and care for it as if with pincers, no one can; and both resemble beginning towards the great toe, and grow little by little until they cover the entire sight, all the light, and the movement of the finger.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	The method of incision is as follows: the patient places his head in a healthy position, then opens the fingers; holds a piece of paper in their hand, then curls the nail like a small pincers and extends it upwards; takes an needle, threads it with a horsehair, or a goat hair, or cowhair, and ties a strong thread to it; doubles the tip of the needle slightly and pierces it through the nail, all the way to the thread, and binds the nail with the thread, extending it upwards; then shaves off all the hair around the nail base, close to the cuticle, using a very fine spatula, and leaves the natural skin or cuticle intact so that by the incision, no tears come to the habitually moistened skin; and never extends the nail beyond the joint only, and with thread as we have said; then it is shaved off, leaving all the soft tissue around it, which is the shape:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And ensure that the scalpel does not touch and tear the flesh, and that the cut is not pierced; then, after making the incision, drop a little bit of crushed silk into the oil, and make a collar of litargyre (a type of metal), and leave it until the next day; then treat it as it should be until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	If the nail is not nerve-related and you cannot insert the needle, or the nails do not enter, this condition often requires treatment with medications; as I have mentioned in the previous section, if you see it covered with oil on the patient's skin, take a light scalpel according to this form.
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee. Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez. And if the appearance of the flesh causes harm in the eye through great damage, suspending it at the corner and cutting off a part but not all, so that tears do not come; then a red liquid distills into the eye which is made from lithargyrum.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that is born on the iris

des voines des eulz	veins of the eyes

de la fistule de l’oil	From the fistula of the oil
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers. de l’issue de l’oil	from the opening of the vein

When the veins are completely open and do not cause disturbance to the nipple or any reduction in strength, it is necessary that you keep the patient; then apply a poultice of mullein, aloe, frankincense, and sarcocolla, and then squeeze out the oil, and apply the poultice on bandages and cloth; and the manner of the cloth should be to fasten enough soft cloths in threes upon each other, and then place one over another according to the need of the vein; then squeeze it from above with a firm bandage, and repeat the application of the poultices for sucking without causing injury; then remove the poultices and leave the oil squeezed for a day and night, and if it becomes softer, it is good; if not, continue the poultice, cloth, bandage, and sucking until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	the sudden rupture of a veil
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee. de la bowe de l’oil	from the bow of the oil (or, possibly, "from the source/origin of the oil
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease called "alcunnati" is not merely from the bow gathered in the oil, resembling severe descending, but it is not severe; and the manner of the appearance of the work is such that you make the patient sit on a seat equipped and straight, then take the head between your hands from two sides, and move it until you see the bow come above your limbs; then insert it firmly, and let the light neither descend nor disappear, and have the patients look at things as they usually do; if it does not subside, know that it is severe, and if the bow's descent is not equipped as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. des aigues de l’oil	des aiges de l'oil" translates to "from the waters of oil

You should place the patient's hands in yours, one crossed over the other, away from direct sunlight, and bind them tightly with healthy oil; then take the instrument called "almagda" in your right hand if the patient's thumbs are on the left, or your left hand if their thumbs are on the right; then insert the tip of the instrument under the skin along the thickest part of the olive branch towards the inner corner of the eye, and twist the instrument called "almagda" firmly, and move your hand until it pierces through the skin in the corner of the eye, and feel that the almagda reaches the empty space; and you should measure the length of the almagda to be equal to the exact measurement of the space from the plum to the end of the darkness; this is the olive's crown. se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If he feels the pain descending now, if he sees the patient before him and the instrument in his hand.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting for a little while, then feel the pain returning along the second path, apply force with the instrument, and if it is deeply embedded and does not rise up, gently extract it by turning your hand back and forth; then immerse again in warm water for some time.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then apply hot oil or any other moist oil (rosin and wax in abundance), and wrap it with clean oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those of our time, place a warm compress with plenty of heat.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the plug cannot enter the oil due to its hardness, as there are some people with too hard of joints, it is necessary that you press the instrument called "alberit," from which this shape is:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	Then pierce only the conjunctive tissue gently, and do not go too deep, but make the opening subtle, then insert the plug as we have said; and at the completion of the work, prepare the patient for sleep with a comfortable position, on his back in a dark place, and restrict all movements, applying light foods, and do not let him move his head to the right or left, and tie him according to his condition for three days. Then release him in the same dark room, test his vision, and make him see nothing, and then apply the bandage again for seven days; and it is not appropriate that you perform this at the time of treatment or after incision now, but rather ease him, because sharp pain rises suddenly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	If an abscess forms, you should open it on the seventh day and apply the remedies that soothe the abscess; when it is soothed, release the pus and place a cloth over its face to cover for some time, and then return it to that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	Then leave the house little by little and let it heal in stages; and know that no disciples should interfere with this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us from Iran who told us that in their peaceful land, they make an extract from a certain plant that sucks out water, but I never saw anyone doing this in our land, nor do I read about it in the books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the appearances of the forms of almand, for he who does not know them will see them, and they should be pure gold.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the tip of this same instrument be very fine, and the rear part at a 90-degree angle.
de la char sor le neis	of the wound on the neck
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	No wounds should ever be allowed to heal in an awkward position, which can result in them resembling snakes due to the pressure; and if there are any such wounds with beautiful flecked or smooth healing, they will turn into bones of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In this case where the pain is chronic and not acute, you should place the patient between your hands facing the sun; open their nostrils, pour the medicine into those which are blocked, and treat them forcefully; then hold what you can sustain with a delicate, thin instrument from one side, as long as you know that part is completely healed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains anything that cannot be covered, open it with all the delicate, light instruments until nothing is left; and without delay, perform the operation as necessary; and for abscesses of a malign nature, hurry and cauterize until the pain is completely alleviated and all parts are healed, then apply heat or cold (or wine).
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If he opens his mouth and moisture comes out to the tongue, knowing it is healthy; and if moisture does not come out as it should, knowing there is something stuck in the bone above, preventing the instruments from cutting, then you must push a thick flax thread inside his teeth with your hands, leaving some space between each tooth, and place the patient's foot in a warm position, squeezing it gently until the moisture comes out through the teeth into the mouth; and children often do this at school, and it is a light task for whoever wants to do it. Then hold the jaw coming through the mouth with one hand, and the other jaw coming through the nose with the other hand, following each other as we who are in thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do as much as you know to clean the corrupted wound, then treat the child, wipe away the blood, and apply Egyptian ointment, and put it back on the wound as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointments have corroded all that is left of the corruption; then place a bandage on the wound for no more than a day, while it heals, and if there is a need for dry medicines, use them; this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, with which one distills oils and medicines into the wound.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be of silver or gold, resembling an open lamp, like a pipe, and direct it thus; if you see, make a closed pipe, and let the tools be full to purge the head; and have many at hand for the head to hold when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	Of the pain near the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times, near the nose, there appears a disease called "telul", which swells and grows very large, making it a sight to behold; therefore, it is necessary that you remove it at the beginning, and clean out the bone entirely, then apply heat or the burning medicine; and if you delay removing it until it becomes large, be careful not to touch it with iron, for it is an abscessed joint, and when you remove it, great harm can come to the patient. If the abscess is soft, without much redness or poor sensation, then remove it carefully, but if it is firm, red, and painful, do not attempt to remove it, as it may cause further damage. The patient should be drained of pus and the joint treated with drying and restraining methods.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	as long as the nails are cut and smoothed
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	You know that when the continuation of a cartilage structure is damaged, it benefits no one.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is therefore necessary to do the following when this occurs to no one, if you consider that the wound is fresh and filled with blood; then adjust the two lips with a single stitch, and treat it until it is healed; and if the lips are already separated on both sides, it is necessary to scrape all parts of their core while they are healing, then bring the two lips together with a single stitch, tighten them, and apply dragon's blood powder, and burnt incense; and place over the powders a piece of strong or other adhesive plaster, and leave it until it sticks by itself, then treat with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of sewing is such that you join the fabric together: either with needles, as we have said in sewing the belly; or with thread, as I have made known to you.
des apostemes des levres	abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	At home, there are often hard abscesses in the lips, resembling small grains, both smaller and larger; then you must turn the lips and cut each one open, taking them as pincers and scraping each part; then use a hot compress after the vitriol incision, until the wound is stained; then apply cold from an ice pack, and cure the wound with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	from the disease of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often, a disease of the gums, which the ancients called "albulus," occurs; it is necessary that you hold it with pincers and cut off the root, allowing the bowel or abscess to drain; then apply powdered vitriol or other drying and constricting powders; and if the gum returns after the incision, this happens again and again, sometimes even after cauterization; if it does not return after cauterization, these are the shapes of the instruments used for cutting.
des sordens	from the obstructions
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	No teeth are ever aligned at the top of the jaw, inside the mouth between the gums, which are ugly and rough; and no tooth is black and yellow and decayed until corruption reaches the gums, and they stink. It is necessary that you make the patient hold still between your hands, and his teeth should be in your lap, and clean out the teeth or gums that are visible, as long as nothing remains; and so do with black, green, jaundice, and other types until they are clean. If what is at the root of the problem is removed in the first attempt, it's good; if not, repeat the process on the second and third day, until everything is clean. Be aware that teeth require various instruments to clean them, according to what the work shows, because the tools used to remove teeth have different shapes than those used between teeth. These shapes and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	You should take care when treating a toothache that you do not delay drawing it out as much as possible, for no one should ever make an excuse for not doing so, as it is a very precious substance.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then, when the patient is constrained from drawing out the tooth, it is important that you are certain about the tooth's position.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the patient pleads for relief, thinking that the tooth is infected, and has it drawn out; but this does not relieve the pain until the infection is extracted, as we have learned with these patients; and when you are certain about the painful tooth, you should scrape around the tooth with a sharp spatula to protect the gums from all sides; then use pliers to move it gradually in small increments, ensuring they are well-positioned, and then firmly hold them; place the patient's chin between your knees, holding the tooth firmly so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth correctly without breaking it, and if it does not come out, take none of these instruments and push it gently from each side, and move it as you have done before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is broken and missing, it is necessary to fill the empty space with cloth, either in the socket or the gap; and if you tighten it gently with pliers, so that it does not break upon extraction; and it is very important to work skillfully around the gums to remove the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be very careful not to break it, and if a part breaks off, return the fragment to the patient, who will experience greater pain due to the evil of the root than at first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And be wary that you do not act as do the ignorant healers, who in their haste and boldness break the bones at every turn, and do not take heed of what we have said; but they bring on great illness through their chatter, or because of the bones they break, as we often see; and when the bone is dislocated, wash it with wine or oil and silk; and the bleeding that ensues, which often happens, apply vitriol poultice; and if this does not help, then cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments, with which to mute the bone first, should be long and thick-handled, not bending when you pull out the tooth; and these are their shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should be strong members so that they do not bend when pulled, and well-made of iron, and toothed for proper movement.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains stuck when pulled, it is necessary to place a moist cotton ball or butter on it for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the eyes are moistened, then apply the pliers known as "algefri", which make the teeth look like they are being cared for; and they should be made inside just like a file and this is their shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to emerge from these claws, then it is necessary that you uncover the flesh all around the root, and place the instrument called "alethal" (i.e., a plier), which has this form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And if it is very hard and does not break, and the root jumps out, that is good. If not, use all the instruments, whose forms are as follows:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one uses this instrument with two edges, its form is:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments that are used in the reasoning of teeth, and this instrument that resembles large pliers, whose shape is as follows:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	This instrument should be sturdy so it does not break, and be aware that many instruments for teeth exist; and also other instruments, which are not mentioned. The most skilled surgeons invent their own tools, according to the specific work and illness at hand, as there are many diverse diseases for which no instrument was created in the past. If one breaks or becomes useless due to a fracture or another issue, and he needs an instrument suitable for the task I have described, then he should use gestures to convey the shape:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And they should be large and well-holding to hold the bone, that it does not escape, but can hold and remove; and then return the limb to suitable medicines for this, and if there is decay in the bone, small or great, use all these instruments.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to the natural shape of the body, and its form is ugly, especially in young women, it is necessary that you know if the tooth has grown after the original one and is not in its proper place, and cannot be filed or smoothed. Then extract it. And if it grows alongside the other tooth, take this instrument whose shape resembles a small beak, and made of sharp steel.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And take a small and sharp knife in both hands each day for the pain of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it is apparent that it can be filed, file it from one side as its shape allows.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	It is also done like the filing of metal for making needles; file the tooth little by little with your hands every day gently, until it stops moving; then, in the end, with no rasp, the tooth is too sharp and it cuts the tongue, so you must file its roughness until it becomes even, so as not to cut or damage the tongue.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth hurts
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the tooth aches, whether from impact or pulling, and the patient cannot bite down without pain, he should be treated with constricting medications, but this is ineffective. If it needs to be restrained, use a gold thread, for silver wire turns green and decays, but gold never changes; and ensure the thread is neither too thin nor too thick, according to the space between the teeth. If you need to align the teeth, take the thread and tie a double knot between the two healthy teeth, then place the gum tissue between the loose teeth, as many as there are, until you reach the healthy tooth on the other side; then repeat the covering and gently but firmly pull until it does not move anymore; and ensure your plier is at the root of the aching tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then cut the bones with a pair of pliers, assemble them, and reconnect them between the healthy tooth, and place it so that the tongue does not bleed; and then leave it as tight as it can be until it heals, and if it loosens, the thread will unravel, so tighten it again from another thread; it should last for all its time, and this is the shape of the teeth and the arrangement of the two healthy molars, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth is extracted and replaced in its place, fresh one by one, as we have said; it should be done only by someone wise and patient, and never should the shape of a healthy bone tooth be made, and it is placed where the deficiency is, and tightened as we have said, and lasts for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	from cutting the tongue's ligament
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	No matter what, this is the ligament that comes from beneath the tongue, either by nature or accident; for instance, when a deep wound occurs; and the work involves opening the mouth of the patient with care, placing their head in your hand, and gently loosening the tongue; then cut the nervous ligament widely, as much as possible, so that the tongue is dislocated from its position, and if there is any hardness or resistance, and it's a sudden wound, use a hook and cut widely through that ligament; be careful not to cut too deep, for the artery located below; and once you've done this, lift the tongue using rosewater or oil, or cold water, then place a thin linen under the tongue; repeat this process each night until the patient's teeth no longer cling together.
