Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if the blood flow increases due to an injury, apply a poultice of vitriol to it; and if the pain decreases, cauterize it with a slow-burning cautery, which is good for this; then apply other remedies until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you see it is red, black, or hard, so the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is a chancre; and if it becomes pale, and there is moisture, drain it with an onion, and cut it with a fine spatula on both sides; and if the pain decreases in your work, apply a poultice of vitriol until it is stained, then return to your work until everything is treated; then lift the limb from rest and stretch it, and apply other remedies until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	From the abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	No matter how often holes appear in the throat that are called "godath," and they are properly known as the two amandres, when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, be careful: these are difficult to diagnose with a small or pale color, so do not touch them with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if they are red and the root is thick, do not touch them with iron, also to prevent the spread of pus; but leave it until it dies, and then you will remove it, or it would break on its own; and if they are of a white color again, and the root is thin, have an instrument ready to cover it, but first make sure that the abscess is cool and calm.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then make the patient sit in front of the sun, and keep his feet in a healthy position, open the mouth, and press the tongue down with the instrument between his hands, pressing it firmly against the entire tool, and use silver or fine gold, just like a knife.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	You should not press the tongue against all of this instrument, and if you see the abscess, take the needle and thread it into the wound, pulling it out from above as much as possible; do not touch any part of the threads with your hands, then cut them with the instrument, forming a shape that looks like a hook; nevertheless, the head is bent, one side higher than the other, very sharp, and made of iron or steel.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument at hand, if it is like pincers, then this is its form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	It should be carved on one side and smooth on the other. Once you have extracted one of the mandibles, extract the other in the same manner, and after the incision, rinse the wound with hot and cold water, and if blood flows, rinse it with water containing extracts from pomegranate peels or myrrh, or similar substances, until the blood is cleansed; then treat it while it is still fresh, and be aware that no other abscesses will form in the throat besides these two mandibles, so extract them just as you would the two mandibles.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was located inside her throat, namely a small abscess; and she had her throat tightly closed so that the woman could not breathe through the blocked passageway, and could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she remained thus for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so swollen that it had forced two ribs through the two openings in the throat.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I then quickly inserted a needle into one of the openings, and drew it out through another, and squeezed a large portion of pus; then I repeated this on the other side, opening the throat and pressing the tongue; after inserting the needle into these abscesses, and draining some of the pus, only a little blood came out; so the passageway in the throat was opened for her to drink water and wine, and I continued to cut away at the abscess for a long time. The abscess returned again, and filled the space that I had emptied, becoming very large. Then I cauterized it inside the throat, after which it did not grow back; and from these efforts, I left only God as her healer.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the retina detaches from the eye, and it is inflated and distant, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is thin and round, it is called "retina".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help, and you see that the inflammation around the wound has subsided, and it is gentle, then you must press it; and that which is round and not distant; and it is bloody or of a dark color, then you should avoid incising it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger for the ill patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see this, according to the manner I have said, you should make the patient lie facing the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument of which we spoke above; then insert the pin in the wound, and pull it out, and cut it with one of the two instruments I mentioned for the incision of the two mandibles.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And you should not remove more than the excess beyond the natural limit; for if you do, it causes great pain to speech and movement, and after the incision, use what we mentioned for the incision of the two mandibles, and treat it until it is healthy.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient feels great pain, it is necessary that you use a tool for cauterizing the sensitive part.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the method of cauterization is very sharp.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the patient should place his head on a healthy surface, and then press the tongue against the instrument we mentioned in this chapter of cauterization, using it with sharp, but not excessive heat. The application is done according to this instrument's form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let the physician hold a brush, as if it were a spoon, and place the instrument with all the medicine on the eye; have the patient lie on their side so that the saliva and mucus from their mouth absorb the medicine, preventing it from going down to the throat and causing discomfort. Then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it onto the eye for half an hour until you see it calm and the pain from the medicine is eased. And if you notice, take cotton and wrap it around a tool, moisten the cotton with the medicine, and pass the instrument through the cotton into the socket, pressing it against the eye until the cotton sticks to the eye; do this several times until the cauterization is complete, then let it dry, and after three or four days, or five, if you need to repeat the cauterization, repeat it, wiping the medicine around the eye with cotton dipped in cold water, making gargles until the patient is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This treatment is safer than cautery, especially for incision; if it is performed with fumigation in this manner, take calament and hyssop and oregano and rue and chamomile and similar herbs, and combine them all or any of them in a pot, and place it there, and boil it; and make sure the pot is well sealed with strong clay, and have a cheveit (a type of instrument) placed over it in this manner.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	It should be of silver or gold, and one of the joints should be pressed into the mouth of the patient until the vapor rises to the eye through the nose, until the eye becomes numb; then it often returns, as long as the eye dries out, and be careful not to do this at the beginning of the hot abscess, as many things can happen; and do not perform this action except during the decline of the hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not available, take a cane and put inside the patient's mouth a piece of cold iron, so that it does not burn too hot; for the piece of iron does not allow the steam to weigh down the mouth, and it is a good remedy altogether safe.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Often a sore throat is caused by bone or a spine from a fish, or some other thing. Therefore, you must treat what you can see, and press the tongue against the sun with all your instruments until you see the object; and if it does not open and remains in the throat, you should make the patient vomit so that the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps this will dislodge the object through vomiting. Sometimes patients swallow a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a lettuce root, or a dry cracker, and then you should tie a thread to the sponge and pass it through; and when it reaches the throat, it will become stuck, and then you can pull it out forcefully. If it does not come out as we have said, take an instrument made of salt according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be curved at the tip so that it can enter the throat more easily, and hold the head raised high; and beware not to touch the epiglottis, lest all of it come out, nor push the bone inside; and you must move the patient to insert the instrument, because it needs to be moved where the object is stuck; if it goes down, pull it out gently throughout the entire instrument until it comes out.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Never is the throat treated with medicine, as I said in the previous division, except with medicinal remedies; and if that does not help, then look at the throat of the patient in sunlight, and press the tongue with the instrument I told you about.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the vein, take it with all its small hooks, or subtle pincers that are suited to it.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if the vein is not suitable, take a sharp knife and insert it into the throat of the patient, then press or lift the knife repeatedly on the vein until hot. Do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient becomes dehydrated every day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	then take a full glass of cold water, open the mouth, and pour it in until they swallow it, moving the hand often; and as soon as the vein senses the water, it closes.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not fall as we have said, and the patient inhales the foul smell from the smoke of the eye's treatment instrument, do this many times, for it will eventually fall without resistance.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	The method of fumigation is as follows: you need a pot with hot coals in it, and place a perforated cover over the pot with the treatment instrument inside; then pour your fumigation mixture, and have the patient put the tip of the cane in their mouth, seal their mouth, so that the smoke does not escape, but stays until it takes effect. The smoke will now begin to work, and if it does not fall, repeat the fumigation many times. Have the patient endure thirst, eat salty and bitter things, and do not drink water; then it will be necessary for him to cough up the phlegm through this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument with which one treats the wound, if it is possible to see, resembles curved pliers designed to enter the throat; and it looks like a hawk's beak, and has the roughness of stone, so that whatever it grasps, it cannot let go; and here you can see the shape.
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many appearances of abscesses are, according to what memory brings to mind in this book, and they vary in terms of perforation and incision; and there are two ways, one being in the same appearance, and from those that retain moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second method is for the joints where they are within the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscess of the head is different from that of the base, and the abscess of the muscular limb is different from that which comes to joints, and each has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if, for abscesses, one must not pierce the bowel until it is completely healed; and if for others it is necessary to pierce them when they are hardened, but they do not die according to their healing, like abscesses that are in the joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when an abscess comes from damaged joints, and it is left until it becomes gangrenous around, then the ligaments and nerves of the joint may be corrupted, which causes contraction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	If the abscess is in the main member and you delay piercing it until it becomes gangrenous, it will harm the principal member; if it is at the root, pierce it only when it is rotten; otherwise, do not pierce a healthy abscess, for fear that it spreads inside and becomes a fistula, and cannot heal completely.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you should know the time of perforation of the abscess which is killed according to completion, and this is when the pain is soothed, and the fever departs, and the pain and redness lessen, and the swelling in the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and you should make the perforation depend on the abscess' location, and where it opens; and the perforation should be long in the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints and tendons and arteries, and everywhere equally, without any swelling.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these cases, according to that limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in a fatty part of the body, it is good to leave the incision open until it is completely healed through digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you perforate it too soon, the body retains the blood from it, and it is filled with much filth; and by chance, the lips harden and you deepen the wound within.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if an abscess is pierced at any place according to the thickness of the body, as needed by the limb.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And you should treat small abscesses with small incisions; for large abscesses, with large incisions and many cuts according to the size of the abscess; and if such abscesses need to be drained, and covered; when they have become as big as a cloth and are swollen, then one should do it like they do with boils: and if they are split into three angles, or if they are treated similarly to the fuelle of myrtle, like abscesses from attackers; and if such require a round cut, other cuts, and similar treatments.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	For those who have no head, like a superficial sore abscess, you should pierce it thoroughly; and when the abscess is large and has gathered great pus, and you pierce it, do not drain all the pus at once, but some of it; then bandage the abscess until the next day, and then take nothing from it again; repeat this process many times, gradually, until all the pus has drained; especially if the patient is of weak constitution, or a pregnant woman, or small children, or old, frail people.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For sometimes the patient experiences a sudden tremor due to the discharge from the bowels, which may cause the ill person's death, and you must not be alarmed.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have felt your abscess, if the wound is clean, and the abscess in the wound is small, then apply a bandage of linen or cotton; but if it is a large abscess with many openings, then put on each one a bandage so that they touch each other. And if you find in the abscess a piece of hard skin, and you have cleaned it around, then fill it with old cotton or shavings of dry flax without moisture, and bind it for three days; then remove it and treat the wound with care until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bloodletting occurs during your work, then administer cold water and ice, and moisten the compresses, and repeatedly apply them to the affected joint.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If bloodletting persists, apply countermeasures and treatment, and use the powders I mentioned in this book; if it is winter, and the joints or abscesses are very sensitive, then you should place wet compresses of wine and hot oil on them; and if they are in a state of inflammation, and the joint is fleshy, then put moistened compresses of water and cold oil, or wine and fresh oil, until the third day, as we have said; then drain the abscess and clean it and treat it as appropriate, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And it is necessary to know universally in the treatment of abscesses: for I have already told you how to proceed with the treatment of abscesses, and here is this chapter.
des soros	from the birds
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Or, there are small abscesses that come from the head, and they often resemble threads, just like the vesicles of a chicken, and they have many similar appearances.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	Some are thick and such that they contain moisture, just like veins; and if there are such that are hard and resistant to cutting, then there is no doubt that the arteries do not act contrarily.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work on the body is such that you should try all instruments called "entromissory", from which the form below comes, something it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	Because if it contains moisture, they make a hole from above down long.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is evacuated, it doesn't leave any skin, allowing the moistened skin to return; then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment if available; if not, use water and string, and apply it to the wound, leaving it until the next day; this will correct what has lingered from the night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then begin the treatment again, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you know for certain that it does not remain at night; then dress the wound with suitable medicine until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	If the abscess persists and is large, follow this procedure: drain it from all sides, remove the flesh, and apply all your care to draw out the pus from the wound where it lies; if the artery resists, do as I have told you.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	Similarly, treat the abscess if it is deep, cutting and dressing it as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And cut the abscess and the moist tissue first, if it is lighter, because they contain little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if there is no moisture in any of these abscesses or sores, and among these hard abscesses that I found on the head of an old woman, they were as hard as stones, sharp, and white, and could not be crushed; and if anyone had tried to cut them, it would have caused just as much harm as a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming on the head, these that appear at the top of children's heads and at the roots of ears, keep the opening closed as much as possible to let the pus drain; and treat them as appropriate.
des scrophules	Of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times this abscess appears in the neck, and dislocates the bones, and infests them with anger, and never comes elsewhere in the body, and it is painful, and entwined with one another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly within its rib cage, just as the nodule and abscess of the head, as we have said; and there are many manifestations of these scrofulas.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and some of them are malicious and do not want to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In that one where you see a good disposition for touch, and it resembles the color of healthy flesh, and is motionless from every side, not even constricted at the collarbone or artery or passageway, and is not excessively deep; then you must cut it open from above, and scrape each part, and the two lips of the heart in its place, if needed, as we have said in the chapters on the head; and gradually, little by little, be careful not to cut the nerve or vein, and do not use excessive force or cutting, so that the hand does not slip, and do not look too far ahead, lest you cut something you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery and it does not allow you to work, apply vitriol or any powder that stops blood flow, and close the wound; leave it until the inflammation subsides, and the wound softens, and then begin to heal.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the wound is stained with blood, it returns to your work until you complete it; then pay attention to your clear sign if there are no small pustules, if you clean and dress them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein in the root of the abscess, it is not advisable to clean that abscess at its root, but rather tie it with a double strong thread and leave it hanging without harm; then apply the wound with old cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment and treat it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you clean the entire abscess, it is necessary that you bring together the two lips of the wound and sew them now, so that there is no delay due to the size of the abscess.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	If you need to understand how to address the root of it, and pull it out with force, then cut it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrofulas that retain superfluity, pierce them where they appear to be closing; and the piercing is done as mentioned above, then apply these treatments with ointment and similar things, so that it does not corrupt what remains from the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, continue the healing treatment with care until it is healed.
de squinance	squinance (n.) - squint or cross-
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	They old ones spoke and talked about the anatomy of the throat; but I have never seen anyone in our land who has done it, and these are their written words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those with a squint, it is important that the fold in the throat, called the "epiglottis," be left alone; and one should not intervene by this means, because all the veins and the source of pain are in those who have an abscess in the mouth, or in the throat, or in the tonsils.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the throat, it is important to cover the epiglottis to prevent the damage that comes from constriction.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	When we want to cut the epiglottis, it is necessary to make it in three circles or four small cuts across, between the two circles, or according to the size of the cut, without touching the cartilage; and these cuts are very suitable for cutting through the epiglottis so that there is no charring, and the knife blade remains long.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	If the masters are fearful, it is necessary that they stretch the throat skin to the entire ring, then cut through the heart while it reaches the trachea; and avoid blood vessels if you see any, and then remove the charred material as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the tracheal flow that jumps out from the broken place, and due to the loss of voice; and leave the wound open a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed and there is doubt about strangulation, gather the two edges of the wound together where the cartilage is, and cut it all through until it heals; then administer medications that promote healing as long as it remains healthy.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albuscasim (a type of herbal medicine) should not be used until the throat is completely blocked, and the patient is judged to be near death, as it lacks effectiveness.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then they should operate on the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe, and they breathe through the wound, thus preventing death; and for this reason, the ancients ordered the wound to remain open as long as the malice of the illness persists, and it passes in three or four days. Then they commanded that the wound be sewn up and treated, as long as healing continued; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a dame took a knife, and stabbed it into her throat, and cut part of the tongue from her mouth; and I was called to heal her, and found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that had issued from it, and realized that it had no strength or control, leading only to the throat, and the vein emerged through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hastened, and sewed the wound, and healed it until it was clean; and it took the dame no further harm than that she lost her voice, and later returned to her normal state; for this reason, I say that with the incision of the epiglottis, there is no cause for fear.
de la grosse gorge	from the great throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	Cysts of the throat are called "throat hernias," and they are large abscesses with a color similar to a arrow, and they often affect women; there are two types: natural and accidental, where the former has no apparent cause.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental type is also of two kinds, one resembling fat, and the other resembling an abscess arising from an artery; it causes fear, and one should not attempt to perform any surgery unless the case is minor, test and examine all access points: if you find it similar to ordinary flesh, and cannot be moved in any way, as one would with a nose, and remove it entirely if possible, and secure it well, treating it accordingly until it heals perfectly.
des nous	From us.
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	There are many ways of which I will speak, showing their similarities; and now it is necessary that I explain the whole difference between us and them.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that issues are hot and feverish as long as the ebullition has not passed, and when putrefaction is complete, then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With the new, there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains satisfaction, which is its own sac, according to the condition of the body, and begins like a grain, becoming large; and they are similar in two ways, either fat or moist, and have much color as I said in division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	You should, when you approach the treatment of pain, test and inquire about all the instruments called "entromissory" first, according to their form as they appear in this chapter or subsequent ones.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	The method of inquiring about abscesses is to press more or less moistly on the abscess, and move your fingers in and out, as long as you know that the instrument has reached the core, then extract it according to the size of the abscess; be careful not to tear.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If moisture runs from the abscess, what color it is, do as I said for other abscesses; and if after extracting the entromissory instrument no moisture comes out, know that it is full of pus, so cut it in a cross shape and use it as tweezers to gently remove the crust on each side, taking care not to damage the healthy tissue underneath; and if you cannot extract it without damaging it, then remove it piece by piece so nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if it does not heal, the pain returns again and again; and if it heals a little bit but without any great distress, it employs the wound with certain corrosive powders or hot water, constricts the wound, applies soothing things to the abscess, and treats it with other remedies until it is healed; and when the wound is very large, it costs the two lips of the wound, and treats it from the source.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the pain persists or other symptoms occur with any haste, use the vitriole (a caustic substance) ground into a powder, and leave it for two or three days until the wound becomes infected and the blood flow subsides; then return to covering what has been affected by the new.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	See here the shapes of the instruments introduced, and they are of three types: large, medium, and small; and there are three quarters called 'albaret', and one called 'breb', and they are also like needles used to cut sorceries, made of gold, silver, or iron, and move best those that are yellow, and are more tested for enclosing fistular corbel-gaps; and these too are of three types: large, medium, and small, according to the amount of the gap's width.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The shapes of the hooks are very similar, as you can see: large, medium, and small; and there are hooks with two curves in three ways; and there are hooks with three curves, also in three ways; and some have two curves, and some only one curve, in three ways as well; all these types are necessary for their use.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The head of these tools is sharp, and there are some that do not cut through completely from one side, which strips the skin, preventing access to the vein or nerve; and these insertions are responded in several ways, so that the patient does not lose blood at the opening of abscesses; and they are three types: large, small, and medium, as you can see; and they should only be used on fleshy parts like legs, arms, mammary glands, wounds, and similar places; and never make another small instrument resembling the cuts of a fist, according to this form, to stop the flow of blood.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it should never be placed in places that are healthy and without injury to veins and arteries, according to this great form.
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Never inflame the breasts of any man when they begin to be corrupt, as long as they appear like women's breasts; they remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wishes to cure them must do so according to this form described in this line b until g.
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scrape off the fat and apply medicinal herbs to the wound with burning charcoal, then gather together the two lips of the wound with stitches, and heal it as long as it remains healthy; and if the breast inclines downwards and becomes soft due to its size, just like women, making two incisions on top of each other in the shape of slits, so that one holds the other at the end of each, ensuring the larger incision contains the smaller according to this form described in this line b until g. Then scrape off the leather between the two lips, remove the fat, and apply what we have mentioned about stitches and powders, as well as anything necessary for the healing, while it remains healthy. If it is not healed, or the incision has not fully healed because the patient does not want to rest, or due to the flow of blood, then you should fill the wound with moist cotton in a corrosive dressing; leave it until it removes the remaining fat and flesh, then heal it as long as it remains healthy.
des apostemes des asselles	from the abscesses of armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	Abscesses that come from beneath the armpits are hard scrofulous nodules or ones that contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those that contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from line .b. to line .g.
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus in the abscess is drained, apply a cloth to the wound for the next day, then remove all the cotton and continue with appropriate treatment until it heals.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess resembles scrofula, then treat it as we have said regarding the incisions made in scrofula, and if the wound opens, apply the cautery as we have mentioned before.
de la routure de l’artere	from the rupture of an artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When an artery ruptures and the flesh above it swells, many abscesses form, and the same happens in the veins, which become inflated and infected; and if you recognize this to be due to an artery rupture, the abscesses are long and deep; and when you feel them at your extremities, they feel strained; and in the case of a vein, they appear red and inflamed; and it is foolish to treat this abscess, especially when it has separated from the flesh and is infected with angles (possibly meaning gangrene) and other maladies, and it becomes very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary to observe the care of fire, and he who is at the head should also be cautious, and for him who has an arterial pulse, make a cut above the skin along; then open the arteries on both sides, until they are exposed; then insert a needle from below and pierce it through to the other side, and tighten the artery with a double thread in two places, as I have taught you in the extraction of two arteries in the temples; then mark the place between the two threads with an instrument, until there is no more discharge; then apply the treatment that has been described, while the wound is fresh; then cure it with suitable dressing, as long as it is clean; and if the abscess is through a vein cut, it is necessary to hold in your hand what remains of the abscess from the entire skin, then insert the needle below the place you are holding, and pierce it, and make a double thread, so that you draw it from the other side; then tie the abscess as I have told you, or the thread to one of the two parts in two places; and if you doubt that the threads do not come out, insert another needle through all the abscess below the first cut, and tighten the threads in four places; then cut off the excess, then cut off the superfluity around the wound, and leave what is attached; then place a moist cloth of wine and oil on it, and apply treatments and dressings until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	from the abscess of nails
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Similarly to abscesses in arteries and veins, nail abscesses occur when they are injured or due to excessive work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this occurs more often in joints and digits where there are many articulations, which is the source of these abscesses, and its appearance resembles the color of human flesh, and it takes various forms with great pain; and when they form, the patient feels a sharp pain, and it is not completely healed throughout the body, but only towards the heart; and it moves well in all directions, neither advancing nor retreating, neither downwards nor upwards, and the one in the joints should not be covered with iron; perhaps it would cause contraction; and that which is at the head or forehead causes the skin to puss.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, and it can be grasped with tweezers, dig it out at its base; and if it's large, suspend it on a hook, scrape off the skin, then cut out the flesh and sew up the wound, until it heals.
des grosses boces pendans	The phrase "des grosses boces pendans" translates roughly to "pendent
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	It occurs in bellies alone, and nowhere else, and is called 'fungus' due to its appearance, it has subtle roots, and large drops; and there are both small and very large ones. I have seen people with two or more such growths in their bellies, which were more like fungi than anything else, and there was no discernible difference, they were white, had thin roots, and were constantly moist.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I gathered them and found in one eighteen ounces weighing, and in the other six ounces, and the work of incising is such that you look at the patient's moisture, and the color of the artery is white and moist and of subtle root; if it grasps with a wide spatula, then have fire cautery in your presence.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For cutting often brings too much bleeding, and if it does not stop for you, then hurry to cauterize; and if you see the patient afraid and anxious about the incision from fire, take a well-made thread, and bind the artery as we have said, and leave it for a day; then restrain it, and do not cease to tighten the thread until it cuts through the artery, without any effort; and if the roots are thick, be more careful in cutting, especially for the abdomen, but you can still cut half of it, then cauterize so that it does not bleed again; then dress the wound, and be sure not to cut the thin part that is red, poor in sense, and white with milk.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an abscess enhanced, and I will come to the treatment of the ulcer right after.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the wound is closed for a time.
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the wound is due to cauterization from a wound or incision on the soft tissue, and it's located on the stomach or in none of the bowels, as can occur with other ruptures, or from bloodletting or artery cutting according to what lies ahead, or from flatulence; and if it's through an opening in the soft tissue and evacuation of the bowel, then the abscess has a color similar to that of the body, and is a slight thing without pain, and opens up through various issues.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to an intestinal issue, then it is more varied, and when pressed by its own force, it repairs itself and then returns, and sometimes it tightens at the entrance to the bath or through hard work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light issue and opens easily when pressed in the hand, without constraint; and if it is due to blood, it appears through these signs: large and hard abscesses, and it is fixed according to its quantity; and if it is due to windiness, it feels soft to the touch, and the work involves observing whether it appears due to blood from an artery, a vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If it is necessary, let the healing continue.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For in the case of abscesses, as I told you in the chapter about them, whether due to an artery or a vein, there is often doubt and fear.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if it appears to be due to the intestine or bowels, it is necessary that you instruct the patient to retain their faeces, and lie completely straight, then make an incision around the entire opening of the bowel; then have them lie on one side, and carefully remove a portion of the abscess above all the sharp edges; then bind it firmly with a strong thread or sturdy silk thread, making sure the intestines are undisturbed. Then open the portion of the abscess that is extended over the binding, and insert your finger to explore the intestine; if you find it caught in the binding, free it and return the intestine to its proper place outside the abdomen. And if you discover a bowel obstruction, use the pincers at the oncine to remove excess material; and if the artery or vein opposes this process, gently manoeuvre around them, then return to your task, taking two needles, and insert them in the manner that we have described, making an incision in the same place as before. Then pull out the abscess in three parts over the needles, and if you can see it, remove the needles, leaving the wound to heal on its own, and allow the dead flesh to fall away naturally. Once the abscess has healed sufficiently, continue with the cure as appropriate, and finish the treatment of the abscess as we have said; then extract any blood or moisture that you find, treat the wound as necessary, and bind the wound.
dou chancre	A cancerous wound
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have discussed in the previous section the symptoms of cancer, and how it should be treated with medicines, and how to avoid iron therapy; we say that cancer spreads throughout the body, and requires great caution in its treatment, and they [the ancients] state that when a tumor is located where it can be removed, such as those found on mammary glands, or the leg, or similar places, it must all be cut out as soon as possible; however, for large and old tumors, one should not even approach them, because I have never been able to heal any, nor has anyone else before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And for the work, when a tumor is located where it can be removed, as we have said, you should never purge the patient of black blood; then make them healthier if there is visible repletion, and cut out the ill limb in a good place to perform the operation; then drain all the pus or cancer, and shave it from all sides, leaving nothing; let the blood flow out completely, and check the wound with your hand or any object, and if there is any sign of infection from the incision of an artery or vein, cauterize it until the bleeding stops; then use another cure as long as it heals.
de ydropisie	Of hydropsis 
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have already discussed the symptoms of hydrops and how the collection of fluid is formed, as well as the signs of each condition and the remedies that are effective through medicine or iron. In these two cases, only treatment with medicine should be employed; one must not use iron on these two conditions: namely, tympanitis and yposarca, for they are deadly. Therefore, when treating this hydrops condition, which is called "eclites" due to medicine, and the cure does not benefit the patient, consider if the patient is weak or has another illness besides hydrops, such as intestinal distress or similar conditions. In such cases, do not use iron, for there is doubt; but if you observe the patient has strong vitality and suffers only from hydrops without any other illness, and he is neither too young nor too old, then proceed thus: place the patient gently on your hands and have the minister press the abdomen while driving the fluid to the lowest part of the pisu (a medical term for a specific body region). Then take the sharp-pointed spatula according to this form.
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And make incisions from the second part.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	Cut with a sharp point, but do not insert it so deeply that it reaches the intestine when pushed in, and do not let it pierce; then observe if there is any inflammation towards the intestines. If necessary, make an incision through three joints starting from the base of the thumb, and if the hydropic is due to liver disease, make your cut on the left side of the joint; and if it's due to mucus, on the right side. Avoid placing the patient face-down over the incision so that excess fluid does not flow into the weak part. Then cut through all the skin with a tool, and the muscle, and gently press your hand against the entire space between the skin and the fascia as if scraping it with the thickness of a nail or more; then pierce the fascia until the fluid flows out clearly, which is the sign of water, then remove the tool and shape it like this:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it resembles a thin silver chain, and is made of fine gold or silver, and has one small opening on each side; on one side there are three openings, and on the other two, and one on the other; and the part that holds it is cut as if it were a feather, and this is the shape of the incision where the scribes cut the feathers.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.
