At the top of it, there is a hole, so that when the instrument comes into contact with water, it sinks immediately onto the instrument; then empty half or a third of it, for if you empty more than is necessary at this moment, by chance the patient may die due to the resolution of his spirit from the weapon, or he might lose his palm, or approach death; but empty according to the amount of its virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the patient signify, and his pulse. Then take the instrument and hold back the water, and it is held back now by the core that stops the hole which I mentioned, that you pierce in this way; then continue with the instrument on the other side, if you see the patient suffering from it, and draw out a small amount of water; do this every day, and be careful not to let any more water out until only a little remains.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt about the patient, and leave him with much water, whether through a wound cure or hot sand, and by sweating or a bath and in the sun, and become discolored; then treat with drying medicines as long as he is healed, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the removal of the water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	from the obstruction of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	No child is born without an opening in the penis, or the opening is very small, or it is not in its proper place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary at once that he does not pierce all the very fine spatium according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	then open the very subtle gap of the bladder, and hold it closed and keep it thus for three or four days, and when he wants to urinate, remove the closure, let him urinate, and then put it back; and sometimes it is not necessary at all, because the force of the urine will not allow the closure to remain.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	If the gap is small, it is a sign of a weak bladder closure, as we have said, and it will widen.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have a complete opening in their joint are afflicted, for no one is born with a dislocation at the top of the limb, which is why they cannot urinate until they raise their limb; and they cannot engender because the matter cannot reach up to the marrow, and this is a grave illness.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the method of the operation is that the patient lies on their back, then the top of the limb and its socket are opened to the size of a feather, so that the dislocation can be corrected as it should; and beware of the discharge of blood which often comes out, and if it happens, stop it with what stops the bleeding, and treat the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	from the pustules of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Often, this inflammation occurs in the penis, and it appears as a ugly mass; and there are both malignant and non-malignant cases; so you must prick them with a subtle needle, cut them, and clean them thoroughly, then apply moist cotton in an Egyptian ointment, and continue the healing process with a diaphonic treatment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the inflammation is malignant, with a putrid black color and stench, then you must apply cauterization.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have achieved it, and if the blister is in a som (a term for a type of skin growth or sore) that is raised and has a part within the skin and a part outside, then it is necessary to remove the blister inside first; and when it is sealed, then treat the outer part.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For if you treat it together, unless the base of the blister is thoroughly secured, it will turn black and corrupt the skin and wound; then it is necessary to remove all that is black and corrupted, then apply a plaster made of honey and flour from crushed pomegranate skins and eggs, and continue treating it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if a blood clotting occurs, then apply the lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cautery is carried out according to the following procedures: that is to say, in case of blood clotting and corruption; if the tip of the member is corrupted and retracted, it is necessary to insert or guide a cane into the urethra and allow the patient to urinate; when the hair at the top of the penis is dry and has become infected for those who have not been circumcised, or there is a wound or abscess, it is then necessary to peel it with a sharp instrument until the ligaments are loosened and the discharge from the member is freed from all sides; if this task is complex, it is advisable to peel it with a spatum along the tip of the penis and the scrotum; then carefully separate them and place a fine, moist linen cloth dipped in cold water over the affected area so that it does not dry out.
de la circoncision	Of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not a dislocation of the continuation like other wounds; however, when we perform this work on our own will, and especially on children, it is necessary that we make the best and most gentle operation for healing.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of circumcision for their children, because they do not practice it in their laws, and we have only what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have observed most of the masters and elders who perform circumcision near the anus, with force, and at all costs; it would seem better to leave it, because there are two openings, and perhaps one is closed while the other remains open.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or she returns to the wound, and the pain is doubled, and the tip of the member is not assured during cleansing; and in the cleansing of the nail, by chance the iron escapes, and it corrupts the work, and often they heal in such a way that no cleansing is needed, which I wish.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the cleansing that is done with force on all the ligaments of thread, I have found the goodness of experiment, for the forces cut precisely as well from above as from below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Because when you press your hand, if the cut is even in both places, then tighten the thread well around the leather; and make sure the manner of the first operation so that the child, if it listens, believes that you are not doing anything but tightening the thread around the stick as gently as possible, and then let it dangle in all ways that you can; then stretch it straight between your hands, and place the forces between your hands or under your feet so that the baby does not see them, nor any of the tools; then close your hand on the stick and blow in its heart, and pull it up until the part of the stick is entirely removed; then clean it well from the dirt that is gathered on it, and tie it with a double thread, then connect it to another ligament; and hold it by the second ligature at the pouche and the index finger, and cut between the two ligaments, then lift the heart gently from above without haste, and pull the chief of the stick; then let the blood flow little by little, for that is the cure; and apply powder on top and on top of the powder, a mixture of a half-cooked egg white temper with rose water, preserved with good rosemary oil and fresh herbs, and leave it until the next day, and continue to treat it as long as it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of purification is as follows: both shoulders should be shaved and cut, and the hair on them should also be long and equally distributed.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error in purification occurs when the veins are not cut correctly; then you should extend your finger to make an incision, so that the vein forms an abscess; and do it equally, and if you cannot hold it with your finger, use pincers, and then cut.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if it persists for three days, and the skin under the arrow is swollen, leave it until the abscess has healed, gently peeling off the wound; cut it as best you can, and be careful to avoid the shaft of the arrow, which will not harm it in any way.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Treat therefore the place of a sudden wound from gunpowder, which we have spoken of in dealing with gunpowder, and if one uses too much heart, it will go up, then it will cause no harm; treat it, therefore, as we have said, while it is sound.
dou retenement de l’urine	retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is caused by an obstruction such as a stone, or frozen blood, or bowels, or a newborn, or similar conditions, as we have discussed in the previous section. If the urine cannot be released and you see that the retention is due to a stone in the bladder or at the neck of the bladder, then the patient should be bent over on his knees; pressure should be applied to his back, and his belly should be extended from above the back. The patient must be restrained as much as possible. This will force the neck of the bladder to express the stone above, allowing the urine to flow freely. If, however, this does not work and the patient experiences severe pain, it is necessary to administer extraction to all instruments called 'syringes', which have the following structure: these are made of fine, lightweight silver, similar to a bird's feather. The length of the syringe should be about one palm and a half, and it must be slender at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the method for urination is as follows: take a double thread and tie one end of it to the top of a wool or cotton ball, then insert the thread into the syringe; cut off the excess wool and insert it up to the top of the syringe, then grease the syringe with oil or butter and egg yolk, and place the patient on a couch. Lift the bladder and fill the urethra with moist oil and olive oil and tepid water; then gently insert the syringe into the urethra until it reaches its base, then double the urethra over itself towards the tip; next, insert the syringe before the bladder, and let the patient feel the urine flowing to the empty cavity, but do not do this unless the flow is directed correctly because if you force it, the thread may break. Then cut the thread from the wool ball one by one, and the urine will follow the thread; pull it out firmly, and drain the urine; repeat the process with the syringe until the bladder is empty, and comfort the patient.
des maladies de la vessie	From the diseases of the bladder.
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When burns or blood comes to the bladder, due to its putrefaction, you should draw off waters and medicines using the instrument called "clepsydre", and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and if it has three openings: two on one side and one on the other, as you see; the hollow part where the medicine should flow is shaped so that it absorbs well the moisture without addition, if one can draw out the moisture and squeeze as needed. And when you pour your medicines into the bladder, place the head of the container in the moisture and draw out gently what remains; you will draw out the moisture from the container and then press firmly on the container; the moisture enters the container and goes directly to the bladder, so that the patient feels it; this is the form of a delicate enema with which one enemas the bladder: thus:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is of silver or gold, and the joint is higher; then open the chest from the side where the ribs split; take a sheep's bladder and fill it with the moisture you intend to use for enema; tie it between the two breasts with a good double thread, and heat that moisture over fire. Then insert the nozzle of the enema bag into the rectum, and squeeze your hand onto the bladder until all the moisture has reached the bladder; and if you do not have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, make a circle of it, and pierce it around evenly. Then thread a strong string through those holes, gather the circle as one would a dal, and place inside some oil, moisture, and water, and tie it with the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, pressing your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already discussed the methods of dealing with stones and their extraction, along with the use of medicines; I have explained the distinction between stones that are rain-related and all other types, and I have indicated which kinds require surgical intervention, be it in the bladder or the testicles; I will now clearly and concisely tell you about these.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is embedded in the bladder occurs more frequently in children, and this is a sign that there is an acute leakage from the bladder, resembling water because of its subtlety; it opens the way for the patient's pain, greatly affects their testicles, and often becomes chronic; indeed, these leakages damage the foundations. The cure for children who have stones is light until they reach four years old, but it is much more difficult in older individuals, those between youth and old age; the treatment for those with large stones is less complex than for those with small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, it is necessary first to purify the patient with a cleanse, in order to draw out all impurities from the bowels.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it never fails to seek out the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet, and lift them up and move them to the sides, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and never moves up again; then place him between your hands with his legs extended downwards, in a position where the bladder is tilted downwards; then fasten him down and touch the stone inside. If you feel the stone in the space, then hurry now to cut into the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not come out at the touch, wet your index finger with oil from your left hand, and if the patient is sick, or your right middle finger with oil, and if the patient is young and fully grown; then press it back into its socket, and hold the stone, and when you feel it on your right side, near the bladder's neck; then press upon it with your right finger, and push it out through the opening where you see the cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the attendant to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to stretch his right hand upward and extend his left hand downward, removing the skin covering the bladders at the point where the incision is made; then use the knife to cut out the stone, shaping it as follows:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And they make an incision between the scrotum and the fundament, not in the middle but on the side of the left thigh; and it should be straight on the stone, and both sides should meet at the fundament, and the cut should be wide enough to avoid difficulty, and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, not too large; so that the pressure from the side which is at the fundament causes it to come out easily; and know that there are stones with angles and edges: these are difficult to pass; and if they are under the skin, resembling a glans or testicle, and round, their exit is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	If there are angles and edges, make the cut larger; and if it does not come out, you should use tweezers that are also like a file at the tip, to extract the stone so that it does not escape; or you can insert a thin, curved instrument at the top; and if you cannot extract it in this way, you can enlarge the opening slightly, and if it is decorticated, extract it with vitriol; and if there are more than one stones, first extract the largest one at the neck of the bladder, then cut from above, then pull it out forcefully, and afterwards the smaller ones, if there are more.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, as it should be cared for, it makes a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things can happen to the patient: either he dies, or his urine flows again through the opening where the bones cannot unite; but nevertheless, strive diligently to extract it, either with pliers or by cleaning out the debris, bit by bit, while you treat the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and bind it tightly, and place over it a moist cloth soaked in oil and wine, or oil and rosewater and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess; then bandage the patient on his chest, and do not loosen the bandage for three days.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you dislocate it, if there is a great rise of oil and water in the joint, then apply healing ointment and basil ointment until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if abscesses and corrosions occur in the wound, and congelements of blood in the bladder, and it retains urine, which is known to happen without warning: then press your finger into the wound and extract the blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder and cause decay; then cleanse the wound with water and heat and cold, and aid it in every way you know, until it heals; and remember, when you treat it, that you bind both thighs of the patient and apply medicines to the joint.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is caught in the urethra, and stuck in place, and urine cannot pass; then through this treatment that I say, you should cut it many times, it is excusable to perform surgery for this cure.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have tested it thusly.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take the iron at the forefront according to this form, and insert it into three pieces of wood.
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a thread and tie it around the urethra beyond the stone, so that it cannot go back into the bladder; then gently push the iron into the urethra until it reaches the stone; and pull the iron back to your hand in the urethra little by little, as you are able to pierce the stone from another side; soon urine will come out, then press your hand on what is remaining of the stone inside the urethra.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is broken and jumps with urine, and rubs the patient; and if you cannot do this for any reason, then take a thread under and above the stone, then make the stick sharp on the stone between the two threads, then pull it out forcefully, loosen the string, and clean the frozen blood in the wound; and treat it as long as it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of the women's stone" 
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	When a stone is trapped in a woman's body, the cure is difficult, and it is hindered by three things: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; the second is that it is hard to find a woman with good knowledge who understands how to remove it, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third way is that perhaps one cannot find a woman with good knowledge in this art; and the fourth way is that if the stone in the woman's body is larger and more difficult to remove, then it must be cut deeper, and much fear exists. If such necessity arises, it is advisable to seek a knowledgeable midwife, or at least someone who understands the subtleties of the female body, and command her to do what you instruct regarding the removal of the stone; and pay close attention if the woman is a virgin. Then she must push her left hand down on the swollen bladder, and grasp the stone. If she finds it, she should pull it out from under her fingernail and recommend that the patient press their index finger into the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, she must move it gradually from the entrance of the bladder down to the thigh, until it reaches the root of the thigh; then cut into the stone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the hard part, where it is moved, and feel the stone in that area; and do not move her leg either above or below the stone, or make a small incision first. Then turn the rake towards the thigh, if she feels the stone deeply in the wound as long as the stone can come out, and know that there are many kinds of stones: namely, small and large and rough and smooth, long and round, and those with edges.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if you know these similarities to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the blood does not stop flowing, apply vitriole powder and hold it for an hour until the bleeding stops; then return to your task, as long as the stone is hard, and have tools that I told you for extracting stones from men, so that you may be helped in your work; and if the blood still does not stop flowing, and it's from an artery that has been cut, apply powder to the place and press with rags and bandages, and do not repeat this, and leave the stone and do not extract it, unless the patient dies; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat from the blood has subsided and the limb is relaxed, return to your task, as long as the stone is hard.
de hernie carnouse	from herniated cartilage
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Rice water is nothing other than a mixture of moisture or white sputum, which is separated from the heart of things, containing the egg white, and is called 'sputum', never properly part of the egg white, if one believes it to be another thing; and this is the membrane surrounding the egg white between the white sputum that we have mentioned, and it has no pore.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this rice water is due to weakness that affects the testicles, and this matter is expanded.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And never does it come from percussion on the joints, and this moisture takes many forms: it can be yellowish, or without redness, or black, or watery white, and so on; and these are the signs to recognize this gathering, for if it is white as we have said, the abscesses are bright, very long in shape like an egg, and do not open the joints, because they are filled with moisture.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the flesh itself, the abscesses are bright with a part of the egg, and because of this, one thinks it is another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the joints and the white, one feels it well; then, when you want to know the color of the moisture, try to feel all over the affected area, as its shape is as described above.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes after, judge of what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we treat it with iron, it is necessary that the patient be healed according to their ability and the fullness of their body; then place them on their back, on something slightly elevated, and cover them with many sheets; then have them sit on their left side, and command the assistant to sit on their right, and extend the staff to one of the two ribs near the heart of the chest; then take the scalpel, and cut the skin of the chest from above the long bone down to the elbow, and make the incision completely straight by cutting through the skin of the chest until it is as white as possible, and carefully remove the flesh according to the patient's strength; then make a large opening in the flesh with water, and extract all the water, and then place your bandages, and close the opening; do not touch the heart of the ribs, but only cut through the flesh; cut it carefully, otherwise the water will return; and if the wound is successfully closed, then put them back in their original position when you have completed the work with the scalpel. Then sew together the two leaves of the chest at a seam, and treat it like other wounds until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the heart corrupted by another illness, it is necessary that you hold the vessels that are suspended, in doubt of the flow of blood; then cut off the clot from all the suspension, and extract the heart, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the wound is assembled in two parts, together, knowing that these are two branches; then cut off the other part as you did with the first, equally, wipe the blood, and place in the wound a clean cloth moistened in rose oil; and apply another clean cloth moistened in wine and oil, and place over the two cuts, and cover with doubled cloth, and tie it to all the ligatures according to this form.
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two strips, and use woolen cloth according to this form, and join them together with stitching at the thigh's gullet, and one of these pins into the base up to the back, and the other on the hand's joint; and the third over both angles, and gather all the tightness in the loop of the breeches. And never use this cautery with a metal knife, but you should pin one delicate cauterizer, cutting through the skin, and make it hot as we have said, so that the white satisfying substance that contains water is revealed; take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that satisfying substance at once, and scrape it with this delicate hot cauterizer.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And the poultice in all ways that you can, as long as it is completely dry; and be careful that the fire does not touch the wound; and know that this work is safer; and move gently to avoid blood loss, and take care with the cuts of surgery; and if anything goes against you, whether it's an abscess or a discharge of blood or any other thing, cure what goes against you, according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	If the patient is afraid and does not want to undergo this operation because of its horror, then apply perforation, as I have told you, and make sure that when you are completely certain, through the signs we have mentioned, that the pain is due to moisture, place the patient in a raised position. Then incise the abscess from below, deep into the whole spatule (area), and make the opening long along the body; let all the pus flow out. Then apply cotton and bind it, allowing the remaining pus to drain, then treat the wound until it is clean. If the white cloth does not allow the pus to drain from the wound's opening, you should insert a quill or the instrument used to draw off water from hydropsic patients, in the form mentioned above; open the wound wider and know that the pus will flow again, and gather after six months or so, and when it gathers as before, then the patient's condition will improve.
de l’aposteme des coions	from the abscess of the hair follicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Knowing that in this section there are many bad arrangements, which is why I think it is better to leave it; and I will tell you about the work and similarities of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say therefore that many abscesses come where the hair follicles are; and most often they occur in the skin; and this is due to many cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	This is due to excessive acidity and ague that spread to the hair follicles, or from percussion; and the color of the abscess matches that of the skin; it does not cause pain, and is a serious abscess; and sometimes there are many painful, dark-colored, and pus-filled abscesses, or of bright red color, and they never come from new arteries or the swelling of veins.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is due to an artery, if it is blocked by the hot inflammation of an abscess when you press on it with your fingers; and you must not touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	What is made from vein inflammation is blocked by its disposition to the pressing of fingers, and it can be cut well on this model and on other parts; and it releases the heart of the blood, then warmth comes above, and the pain subsides quickly, and delivers the suspension of all parts of the blood.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the inflammation is already hard with these cuts, then you must drain the blood and cut it; and if it is hot to the touch, or inside the vessels, you must free all that tension, and cut it properly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the base of the hair is at the rear, it is necessary that you cut it entirely off, and extract the root, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is completed, apply a moist woolen compress with rose oil and wine to the wound, then use other remedies until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the hairs
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess surrounded by a wrapping similar to a boil, with the hairs being soft and immobile, causing the patient great pain; and its cure for this illness is very precious, as well as frightening, just like the one mentioned above, and nevertheless, we will tell you about its work, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	You should place the patient in a comfortable position, then tie down the affected limb with a suspension bandage at your discretion, to all vessels near the point of interest, and stretch them taut; then use a scalpel with a broad, sharp edge to cut through the vessels, while they are exposed, and scrape from each side, as we have said for extracting arteries in temples; then insert a needle where there is a double thread, and secure it to the first joint where the vein entered, and then to the other end; then cut them evenly straight according to the length of the body, and remove corrupt moisture; then treat the wound as others, so that no vessel leaks and affects one of the joints; for by this, there will be no harm, and all vessels will have visibility, so it is necessary to tie down the joints to all vessels; so the vein does not lose its nourishment due to vessel incision, and dries up and cannot aid itself.
de la routure dou syfac	from the rupture of the sinew
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The consequences of this rupture are as follows: if it occurs from the section (amputation) or through extension in the abdominal region, near the angles, then the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the openings; and this rupture is either from the sinew (tendon) or from the extension, and these two conditions have various causes: percussion, a jump, straining, lifting a heavy weight, and similar things; and the signs when it is due to the tendon's rupture are that it happens little by little over a long period and does not come suddenly; and the abscess remains equally sized towards its entirety because the rupture (tendon) pushes the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is a successful section, that it brings sudden pain at the beginning, and various abscesses appear beneath the skin close to the bone, due to the release of intestine and flesh from the syphil's fire.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And never drain the abscess with the intestine, but hold it in place, causing great pain to the patient, especially when pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these poor treatments with iron, for that reason one must be wary.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the method for this chapter is that you command the patient to move the intestine back into its place inside the wound if it can be done; then carefully hold it in your hand and ease the pressure; next stretch out the heart on top, and shave all the flesh down to the bone. Then insert your thumb index between the muscle and the white flesh that lies beneath the outer skin of the testicle, and between the second flesh, and remove what is behind the testicle, and between the second flesh; then move your right hand inside the heart of the muscles, and position the white flesh on top with your left hand, easing the testicle towards the tailbone. Order the assistant to stretch out the testicle upwards, and free what is attached at the rear end of the ligament; be careful if there is no sign of intestine or firm white flesh, and if you find anything, insert it into the abdomen beneath the skin. Take a needle with a thick thread made from four threads, and sew it through the posterior part of the white flesh after the skin of the testicle; then cut off the appearance of the threads, as much as there are four; then arrange them one on top of another in the shape of a cross, and tie the white flesh that we mentioned is beneath the skin with a strong thread from both sides. Envelop the threads around the muscles, and make them secure so that no vessels can enter inside, preventing an abscess. Put the first ligament as long as two fingers, then after these two ligaments leave the white flesh beneath the heart of the muscles as one finger length; then cut off the remaining part of the white flesh below the skin, just like we mentioned before; then apply moist wool to the wounds and dress them, and use the thread that we spoke of.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And never should the white flesh be cauterized as we have said, after the incision, out of fear of bloodletting.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this happens often, and leaves the wound open until it heals itself; if it takes time to close, then apply hot water, as we have said, until it heals; then treat the wound with other remedies, until it is completely healed.
de hernie carnouse	of a hernia (fleshy protrusion)
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this case, never have I seen anyone who dared treat it with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients say that it is made like a branch which holds together the bone, in such a way as you tie the vessels, after cutting them slightly below the joint; then cut through it, and treat the abscess of him who opens, until the vessels stop bleeding; and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	No rupture should occur from the wound, as we have said, and open the vessels; nor should any internal organs protrude, and if they do, it is a sign of danger, and it should be attended to every hour; nevertheless, if it persists in this condition, one should suspect either an abscess or gangrene, until the intestines protrude; and this occurs due to the extension of gangrene into the vessels, as we have said, for it extends, then softens and swells the vessel, and opens; and its cure is by cautery, as we have previously mentioned; and it should never be cured in any other way. The patient should lie on his back with his head between your hands, then cut the vessel affected by the gangrene from below, according to the amount of three fingers; remove the gangrenous tissue beneath the skin with a knife, take the edge of the knife, and place it over the visible vessels of the gangrene, press firmly into the abdomen, then cut both visible vessels of the gangrene on top of the knife edge, and stitch them closed; do not cover or extend the wound or do anything else differently, as I have instructed regarding the cure for intestinal rupture. Then treat it with a wound dressing.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you treat the wounds, if they are unclean and the injury is healed, as long as it is healthy.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The treatment is difficult, and it has no appearance in the fracture, but the cauterization moves in this place, and it is closer to healing.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the thick skin of the limbs
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the limbs is softened in no man, because the muscles inside are relaxed, and it is easy to see. When one wishes to treat it, one makes the patient lie on his back and cuts off the soft skin on the natural skin; then brings together the two edges with a stitch or three firmly, and removes any excess soft skin with cuts between the stitches, and treats it like other wounds as long as it is healed, and pulls out the thread.
dou chastrement	Dou chastrement (Double cautery)
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	You know that castration is condemned in our law, and for that reason I would not like to speak of it in this book; but there are two ways it can be necessary: one is to answer questions about it accurately and to provide the cure; and the other is because we often need castration of certain animals to help us, such as a goat, sheep, cat, or other animals.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that castration is performed in two ways: either by attraction or by incision.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the method where we perform castration by attraction, we should keep the animal in hot water until the scrotum is softened and relaxed; then, with your hand, press on it until it is healed and you no longer feel it.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	From the castration of size: It is necessary that you fasten the animal, and press the skin of the testicles with your left hand, then tie the suspension, and cut each one individually to the point where they are well scalped; and leave no trace of pain or the subtle pain that lies on the veins; and this method of castration is different from that which is done by attraction, because at attraction, by chance, something of the testicles may remain, leading the animal to desire lust; then treat the wound until it is clean.
des hermofrodites	hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	An hermaphrodite is according to two manners in men: one such that between the two testicles appears also like the figure of a woman's nature, or it has hair, and never cuts itself short in court when urinating.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And another method is for women, where it grows on the palm like a stick and has two joints.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment for men and women is that you remove all the tight clothing, and treat them like other wounds; in the second case, for those whose urine flows through the skin of their penis, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	of the goiter
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Goiter is a tight growth on the natural part, as it is too ugly to see; and no woman can remove it completely like a hand, and this is its treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	You should retain the excess of the tendon in your hand or fingers, and cut it lightly; do not cut too deeply, lest bleeding occur, which can be counteracted with another cure until it is healed; and for a condition that arises at the opening of the mare's mouth, and its use, and perhaps jumps out, and resembles a cow, and for this reason the ancients called it "cow disease.
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	It is necessary that you cut it, as we have said about the tendon, and treat it until it is healed.
de erratique	erratic
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Erroneous is the judgment when one does not fully understand the nature of women, or if the wound is small; it is either by nature from birth, or an accident due to illness that comes upon them; or it is caused by improper posture, or some subtle or specific affliction, and is done completely during pregnancy, or on the side, or underneath, or in any way; and it requires knowledge of conception, childbirth, and perhaps even the flowers to be born; and this knowledge is obtained through observation of dance.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the symptoms are soon apparent, whether they are due to your own fault or through chance.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is a subtle affliction and the symptoms are soon apparent, act quickly: place your two index fingers together, and have the woman lie on her back with her legs spread; then form both legs into fists until the subtle affliction disappears and the symptoms vanish; then take wool, moisten it in oil, and apply it to the affected area, placing the woman face up each day so she cannot tighten or move.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if it is hard and sticky, you must then use a scalpel similar to a mistletoe leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the swelling is from cold, suspend it at the joint and use a scalpel; have medicines that stop blood flow, such as witch hazel, dragon's blood, incense, in abundance; then apply a wide bandage so that the wound cannot close, and thus, after a while, apply a dry linen compress; and continue other treatments until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when gangrene occurs from cold, you must cover it according to this manner; if it is not abscessed.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an abscess that has enlarged in the wound, one must not attempt to treat it with fire.
des emorroides	hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are open veins that, without proper treatment, can become chronic. In the previous section, we discussed the similarities and signs of good and bad hemorrhoids, and now I will describe those that receive treatment.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and their complications, when they are completely in the anus and not felt, can only be properly treated with fire.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the mouth of the mare, one can feel, are those that one can cure.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is therefore necessary that you place the woman in a cold house, then stretch her legs with tongs and cut the flesh at its roots, then sprinkle medicine to stop the blood, such as wormwood and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then bind her feet to the wall for an hour, then immerse her in cold water. And this process of bleeding will take place, if she leaves it in a decoction of sumac and bark from pomegranates and gall nuts and similar things, and then take flour from barley, mix it with honey and ash, and make an ointment to apply to her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it becomes dry, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If it is not, then make cups and apply them to the back without hurting the breasts; then take linen, moisten it with juice of plantain or elderberry wine, and place them on the joint.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess has rested, continue to treat the wound with care until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red and resembles a rough head, so it should be treated as I have said before; then heal it until it is whole.
des apostemes de la marris	from the abscess of the breast
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many types of abscesses occur in the breast, such as chancres, old abscesses, herpes, and fistulas, hemorrhoids, hot abscesses, and many other diseases already mentioned in the previous division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is therefore necessary that I discuss here the hot abscess that occurs in the breast, which is not a solid abscess but one that bleeds; and if you want to know the work of fire, consider whether the abscesses are red at their onset, filled with heat and fever, and turn red if you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Then do not hasten to pierce, but make the patient suffer until the pain is soothed; then place the afflicted person in a reclining position, and give them two small pillows on which to rest, and align their feet towards the parts that are weak in the leg; and spread his hips wide, and put his arms below his knees, and bind them tightly with a good bandage. Then open the patient's anus from the right side, and insert the instrument used to open the mouth of the wound, from which this form arises. And it is necessary that when you insert this instrument, that you first stick the point in so as to know the depth of the wound, so that what enters from the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and does not hurt the patient; and if the instrument is too large, then cover the depths of the wound with cloth, so that the instrument does not cause pain. And place the cone of the instrument on top, and color the instrument.
