Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess opens and they make an incision with their hands gently, if it is necessary to cover the wound, let them use a spatula; and when the bowel is empty, you should put moist cloth soaked in rose oil or dry green oil into the wound, right up to the edge of the wound, and put another cloth soaked in clear water outside the wound over the wound and on the thigh, and let this stay there until the healing process comes after two days of treatment, as long as it is healed; and never lift the bandage or the wound with a enema of water and honey, then with cooked water or lily roots and aristologe long soaked; then return to treatment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is healed in the thigh, it is necessary to be careful not to use heat, but treat it as we have said in the previous section.
de l’enfantement	from childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	Skillful midwifery begins with knowing the signs of natural childbirth, and these signs are when you see a woman straining downward and exhaling strongly: then the child should be born immediately. At this point, understand that these children are born according to nature's figure, coming out head first, and seconding with the mother; and when you observe these signs, it is necessary to gently press on her belly so that the child comes quickly. For when it descends onto her pelvis, it seconding with her, and the womb expels its excesses through good purification; and this is what happens naturally, whereas anything otherwise does not come about naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it never comes upon its feet, but strikes the body here and there, or the hands, or upon the belly, or sometimes turns about by chance onto its neck, and assumes other evil forms; so it is necessary for the doctor to be wise and cunning in these matters, and to ward off error and disappointment, and I will show you all the forms how he should help.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the fever comes upon the head through natural causes, and the woman gives birth with great difficulty, and her strength is weak, then she should lie on a saddle, or the women should hold her; and prepare the remedy from oil or fenugreek, cooked as described below:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and cut the second one, and dig into their fingernails as deep as the moisture that is inside; and press the woman's belly until the child descends, and if it does not descend, it is necessary to cleanse the woman with fenugreek mucilage mixed with sesame oil; then make her sneeze and blow her nose from a cold condition, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: now the child will come out.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	If both hands come out, it is necessary to gently reset them little by little; and if they still cannot enter, place the woman on a chair and raise her feet upward; then remove the chair from the ground and have the woman lie down, so she does not try to stand up; and if her hands still cannot reach, cut through the forehand that is previously mentioned, extract the child, and reset them equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	From the exit of the child on his feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes on his feet, he should be pushed upward, and then little by little, until they are even; then press on the feet and extend them little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	He should jump up to his toes if commanded to press, and it will make him sneeze from the condition; if he jumps far, God wills it.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not happen as we have said, little by little, until it is according to the natural form.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it becomes slightly easier.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not work as we have said, take a small amount of musk, oil of roses, and gum resin, and grind them all in a mortar; apply this mixture to the female organ both inside and outside, then let it sit in warm water until below the ribs; when it is moistened, make a collar of myrrh and place it below, leaving it for an hour. Then place her on a seat, have her sneeze, press her mouth and nose slightly, and gently massage her belly, as the child is now ready to be born.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	from the emergence of the child on his knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this position, he should move his hands little by little; then he should rest on his collarbone, and let his feet hang down, and lie on his side; and gradually he moves his hands little by little, takes hold of his hands on his stomach, removes the cushions from below, until he is fully turned upside down; and if the child does not turn, take his feet and form them, then raise his stomach upwards, and press your hands; and gently rock the child; and instruct the woman to press herself as the child turns.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	From the birth of the child who comes with a strong hand during
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	I know how to bring the hand back: if it cannot be brought back, then have the woman rise and walk; if she cannot walk, lay her on her side with her legs raised, and administer the musk as I have mentioned; and if she does not give birth, have her sit on a chair, and study ways to bring the hand back, and deliver the child according to its natural position, and have her sneeze, and command her to push as the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	from the birth of the child onto its mother's chest, with its hands spread and its face turned towards its mother's back.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	I want the patient to hold his hand, then turn it slightly and gently; and when it is even, he should apply a light, muscly, oily compress, as we have said, then instruct him to move it slightly; and once you have done that, place it on a warm seat, and command him to press; and make him sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in the same way for all the rest
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it acts in this way for all the rest, if the seconding (presumably a medical tool or technique) is applied to your finger, as long as the moisture is drained; and if it gets stuck on its face and neck, cut it from the edge so that it is not retained, and the embryo dies; then bring the child inside, while you have placed it as it should be, and command the woman to press herself at times; then slightly release (the pressure or tool).
de l’issue des gemelz	from the issue of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	You know that twins are born many times, and never three or four at once; and this is not a strange thing, and it often happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Twins are a strange thing, and do not live long, they have no name; I know that they are multiplied, and their deaths are caused by the joy that divides them, which is connected to the mother's womb; and they never emerge as naturally as one would expect, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they are severely stuck, as the cure is as we have said, and the pain is sharp, then do it quickly and lightly; and act thus as it should be done for their safety.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	They should never be formed in the womb I, II, III, IV, V, VI, VII, or more up to XV, and are entirely shaped like an infant according to the measurement of its wise glory, and it is necessary that the skilled midwife knows all this, for by chance similar things may happen; so do as it requires.
de l’enfant mort	Of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you cure the woman who has suffered a stillbirth or abdominal pain, as I mentioned in the previous division, and there is no discharge, and you are forced to intervene manually; it is necessary that you know if the woman's health is good and free from any complications or fear of death. It is important that the woman be placed on her back, with her feet inclined downward and her legs raised. The practitioner should use both hands, applying two parts of the following: moistened eye drops mixed with althae and fenugreek powder and linseed oil, then anoint the perineum with these oils and eye drops; gently massage it, then apply light pressure to the areas where the ligaments are suitable for descent, taking care that the child does not fall on its head. Insert the ligament in her own natural positions - at the base of her tongue, her colum, mouth, palate, under the beard, or near the symphysis pubis - and if the descent is successful, hold it there with your fingers or a forceps, applying moderate pressure; it is better to insert the ligament with the right hand while holding the speculum with the left. The shape of the ligament is as follows:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then find another joint, where you need to insert it, so that the extraction is even; and then hold it equally by moving from one side to the other, to make it mobile, and be sure the joints are cut so as to hold them in place, just like this form.
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	If a part remains stuck, and none of the oils on his fingers help to loosen it, squeeze it into that part, and pull the other part; and if nothing comes out, put this joint higher up the limb, and do what you can until it completely comes out.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes forward over the other, and it cannot be brought back due to tightness, you should wrap it up with a cloth until it is completely loose; then cut at the joint of the palm or at the wrist, and do the same for the other hand, holding both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the child's head is large and stuck in the birth canal, and has a sharp point, it is necessary to insert the spiny spatula between your fingers, press on the head, and extract the water; or you can use the instrument called "almidach," with which the form is made along with the tools of this chapter that follow; and thus do the same for a child with a large natural head; then, pull out the bones with tweezers, and if the head comes out with force, it may be broken; as long as the moisture in the worst part has left; and if it cannot come out, cut it off in pieces as you can; and if it is swollen in the belly or under the ribs, pierce it until the moisture runs.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the fever is on its feet, it has a light attraction, and the direction towards the mouth of the wound is gentle.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is twisted in the belly or thigh, you must stretch it out with a cloth wrapped around your hand; and make an incision on the belly or thigh until the moisture within is corrected; and if another member is broken and remains stuck, twist your hand towards the wound, and pull until it reaches the mouth of the wound; then use a saw or something similar to cut through, and pull it out. If the mouth of the wound becomes narrow due to hot abscess, it is not advisable to work on it, but rather to apply moist and greasy substances; and dress it with poultices, using soft water that soothes and moisturizes.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the dislocated joint is on his side, and you can put it back even, as we have said about a living child; and if it cannot be set right, then cut it off piece by piece, leaving nothing of the second joint.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, apply what we have said about abscesses that occur in the married state; and if bleeding occurs, it should be treated with strong restraints, and other remedies should be applied.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman whose belly had been cut open and an infant had been torn from it, then another was cut open on that same place, and the other injuries were healed.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, a small abscess appears on the cheek, it swells until it opens, and begins to cause great pain.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called upon to heal it, and I thought for a long time, but I could not close the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied strong herbs, and an bone came out, and after a few days, others followed.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was very amazed because this belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	If I thought it was a bone from a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I examined the wound and found a bone in my hand, as long as the woman was getting better; and after observing the woman for a long time, I noticed that she had a slight bowing of her limb; and I have never recorded this chapter to be anything other than because, when a master encounters something strange, he knows how to help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring the shoulder back to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	After this comes the form of pressure, with which one binds the books; and at its turn, to the two ends of the limbs.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Nevertheless, the horns should be more subtle in their tightening, and made of ebony or box; and the mouth opening should be broad enough for a fist to fit inside, with margins measuring one palm and a half long; and both sides of this same opening should have firm adjustments, each about half a palm long or slightly longer; and these adjustments are inserted into the mare's mouth to open it when turning the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, more subtle and lighter in appearance, should be made of ebony or boxwood, resembling pliers; it should have two adjustments at each end, approximately one palm long and two fingers wide; when opening the mare's mouth with all the instruments, make the woman lie down on her side, with her legs spread apart, then insert both adjustments into the mare's mouth and join them together, holding the instrument's head beneath her thighs; then open your hand over the entire instrument, as you would with pliers, according to how far you need to open the mare's mouth, until the strain makes it do what is required.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	The surgical instruments are all carefully arranged, and there are many of their kind; when the mirror has made them appear clear, then the work is done more quickly, and with greater skill for their abundance.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not disregard the instrument even if you have not prepared it, for the need is no excuse for negligence.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the secondine (a type of instrument or technique) is used during childbirth, it is necessary to instruct the patient to hold her breath and then exhale slowly while pressing her hands to her mouth and nose. If she follows these instructions, all will be well.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If it is not possible, take I a needle or a plug, and make I an opening in the cover, and insert herbs that can open the mouth of the wound, such as calament, rue, anis, chamomile, cassia, and centaur; all these herbs, or any of them, should be cooked or put in water over the fire; then place a cane or plug in the opening, and turn the other end into the mouth of the wound, holding it until the vapors enter the wound; then make the patient sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the treatment does not help, then do the following.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if after this treatment it persists and is not strong enough, tell the patient to moisten their left hand with oil of sesame or musk, then wrap it back in its natural position, and seek help from a second person; and as soon as they find it, press and stretch it little by little straightening, so that the dislocation does not slip during extraction; but he must gently move it to the right and left, and then treat it.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the opening of the dislocation is narrow, we have mentioned the cure of sneezing and herbal fumigation; and if it does not improve from all that we have said, be careful not to drain it; but he who is at the opening of the dislocation, should tie it to the woman's ankle, then give her a four-part treatment; she will release it and come out, but nevertheless, when she gets stuck, there will be a bad smell in the stomach and head, and the patient will be worse.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	If it is necessary, then suitable fumigations should be used: no one among the ancients has tried the fumigation of arugula and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument used to fumigate the woman for the retention of flowers and the placenta is this one:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is a glass instrument resembling a horn, and it has a narrow top naturally, and wide openings over the fire; and the fumigation should be on the coals, and the smoke until it is spent, and then repeat another.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who have not had their foundation pierced, but it is covered by a subtle mark: therefore, when circumcising, one should pierce this mark with a sharp instrument, without damaging it, and avoid touching it; then apply a moist cloth soaked in wine and oil, and continue the treatment until it heals.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not heal, insert a thin wire or pin, and leave it for several days, allowing the child to move freely; it should be removed when the wound has healed.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And never comes this sudden stop of a wound or abscess; it is necessary to cover this stop, if it is cured, as we have said about the pain of the bone.
de la fistule dou fondement	about the fistula from the depths of the foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistules that originate from below the foundation are more serious than those that come from above, or in the space between two parts, if there is a fistula or several; and when this nodation is old, it opens, and still emits white or subtle discharge, and never do these fistules heal; they are known by the fact that there is oozing or pus when the patient evacuates, and sometimes they jump around.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if the ulcers penetrate to the bladder, and to half of the penis; and they reach the joint of the thigh, and to the root of the knee.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus, you recognize the fistula that penetrates but does not heal: and it is good to insert your index finger into the anus and push a fine needle of iron or steel into the fistula when there is no curvature.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if it has curvature, if you insert a fine plunger or a horsehair, as long as you feel the attempt or the hair in your hand; and if you do not feel it, and it does not produce any expulsion of pus or wind, as we have said, know that it will not penetrate; be quick to cure it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula persists all the way to the bladder or to the urethra, if it leaks urine and cannot be sealed with medications.

If it is pierced all the way to the hip joint, then there is a chance of veins being affected close to the place; if there is no curvature or change in the pain around it, and it remains bent, neither medications nor any treatment helps; and for these persistent fistulas, there is no sure cure except through hard work and the vain efforts of those who meddle with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the case where it is neither persistent nor old, there is hope for healing with heat, as I have experienced, and the patient lies on their back in your hands; extend their legs up to their hips, and bring their hips towards their stomach; then wrap a tent of cloth or, if there is curvature, a soft material, as long as you know where the pain originates.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels pain in the foundation, it is necessary that you press your index finger into it, and then he feels that the pain is piercing; and if you uncover between your thumb and forefinger where the satisfaction or chill is felt, then know that it is persistent; unless worked upon, it cannot be healed.

Then apply moist compresses, until the wound is completely healed, then use treatment with ointment, making sure it is clean and sealing.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is in such a state, it is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant. Beware of those evil-looking materials that resemble a bird's feather, and do not linger on them.

des emorroydes	Of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are of two kinds: those that are inside the anus, resembling grains of resin, with small or large ones, and sometimes they are accompanied by blood, and extend from the anus down to the rectum; but those that protrude outside have little moisture, and sometimes a bit of cold or hot liquid, and have the appearance of the skin. The treatment for hemorrhoids inside the anus is to order the patient to lie on their side until the anus relaxes and the seeds fall out; if they are stuck, take them with tweezers or hold them with your finger nail, then cut them off at the root. If they cannot be held due to moisture, grasp them with a piece of cloth, cotton, or a strip of chamois, and remove them gently. Then cut them off and apply hot powdered medicines as instructed in the cautery chapter; or cauterize them as mentioned, and treat other conditions as long as there is no infection. If the anus cannot be relaxed, wash it with a strong enema to clean out what is inside so that it can be removed easily. The treatment is light if the patient's condition improves quickly after applying these remedies, and cutting off the hemorrhoids without using a knife.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary to administer the stitch in this manner: take a twisted thread, and wind it around an needle, then draw the thread from above and pierce the needle from the other side, and pass both ends of the thread through the needle, and if it is too thick, tighten the forming thread, then tie the thread, and remove the needle, and do thus with all others, leaving one for draining the excess blood; then place a moist cloth over the wound, or wax, and put it on the wound, and instruct the patient to rest; then leave it until they heal, and when they have fallen, apply treatments and other remedies until they are healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	The phrase "dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement" translates roughly to "the gently drying of the
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is drying of feces in the intestine, due to natural constraint, and when the illness is old and no medicine helps.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary that you scrape off the dry skin with a spatula or your fingernail, which does not allow it to moisten; then treat it as soon as possible, and if it cannot be moistened, repeat the scraping stronger than before until it becomes moist and slightly cut; then treat it as long as it heals.
dou fremit	Douloureux" is the Old French
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Mice are small, hairy creatures that burrow into the body and grow rapidly; and they never harm it by their touch, but cause a sensation as if dead from trembling, spreading throughout the whole body, especially in the hands.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a cane from a goose feather or a strong falcon's feather, and place this cane on the trembling until the purplish circles cover the whole trembling; then turn your hand over the entire cane until you cover all around the trembling, and set it straight, and remove the trembling from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you find yourself in need of a cane made from either bronze or iron, make it according to this form, and be sure that it is both strong and flexible.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Do not touch, for fear of hurting, and do not press. If you see, cauterize the tremor as it is described in this chapter of cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of a douche (or enema)
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	One should never use a enema with silver or lead, or melted gold or iron wire; and one should never use these small and large instruments, according to those to whom they are prescribed.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those are the ones that are prescribed for the treatment of children and those who are weak and suffering, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	He must prepare a small and wide bladder if it is too narrow above; he will bind the abdomen according to this manner:

And let the medicine be neither too hot nor too cold, and apply a warm compress with oil or egg white or something similar, then gently squeeze it out; then the attendant should hold the patient's legs against the wall, and allow the medicine to flow out as much as possible; and if he sleeps through the night, it is even better.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you use the enema for an illness due to intestinal stagnation, and the medicine flows out quickly, repeat it as long as there is no further need.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoid is at the anus or abscess, it should also be enema as delicate as for a child; and this is the shape of the delicate enema compress on which the skin is drawn tight.
des plaies	from wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already spoken of the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you about the treatments for hands and medicine, according to their completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are, and according to the place where the wounds are made, and from what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are through the striking of stone, and the cutting with a sword or knife, or with a spear or staff or arrow, or similar things; or they are made according to the places on the body, such as a wound that opens on the collarbone, or on the head, or on the side, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the cure for each wound, and begin with simple head wounds, because the remembrance will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound appears on the head, and the bone is not broken, be careful if it's caused by a stone or similar objects, for the skin is still torn and the wound is deep, and you slightly doubt an abscess: do it soon to heal the most from the headache, especially if there is little blood loss from the wound, and treat the affected part accordingly; and remove the patient's excess wine and heavy meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not want to heal, then reduce his meat intake and do not drink wine or eat char; and apply a poultice of rose oil only or aromatic wine to the wound, especially if an abscess forms as it comes; in its early stages, keep it clean without letting air, powder, enter until it is healed. If there are burns, apply any suitable remedies while it remains healthy.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is great, like the size of a sword or similar, and the lips cannot be brought together by pressure, then they are sewed together, as I will say about wounds in the belly, from the stitches.

If the wound is open and deep, reaching the bone, and it bleeds profusely, then stop the bleeding with a bandage; treat the wound with medicine, and replace the skin with hard wood in place of leather, and instruct the patient to eat hearty meats, such as testicles, cooked wheat, as well as poultry and similar foods.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	If you find putrefaction in a wound that does not reach the bone, and it bleeds profusely and emits a bad odor, then stop the bleeding and treat it; but if there is an artery in the wound, or a vein without a cut, and medicines cannot stop it, then cauterize it, and if this does not help, tie it off with a thread.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, the cure is light: it is that you apply this powder that will soothe the fire so that it heals.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the method for the powder is this: take one part incense, two parts dragon's blood, and three parts of the living charcoal, mix it finely, apply it to the wound, and tighten it until it spreads well and joins together with all its moisture; then bind it tightly and leave it untouched if it does not swell, because the medicine is not removed as long as it remains healthy.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never should charcoal be used alone, unless one has incense or dragon's blood, but the fire should have healed the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the fire has moved the wound, especially if there is no powder applied; but put on some prepared ointments, or a paste of barley flour made with water and honey, until it is soft; then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if a bone fracture occurs with the wound and it is small, extract it with delicate pincers; and I will tell you below about the fractures of the skull.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the collar (or neck).
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound occurs on the neck and it is simple, then there is no distinction between it and any other wound in the head, but if the wound is deep in the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is an artery, then there is no other remedy but to let it heal, and do not put anything constricting, as that would harm the artery and cause it to retract; and do not apply any hot things to the wound, because the substance of the artery is cold, and its continuation is connected with the brain, which is the highest member. But use medicine accordingly, such as washing with lukewarm water mixed with rose oil, and clean bandages also in lukewarm water, and other remedies from mineral sources in this manner, and moist compresses.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is great, cutting it open and binding it with bandages, then treat it until it heals.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and severe, filled with pus and bowing, then pierce them lower or cut them open; and if the artery is severed, and bleeding occurs, then ignore it and use cauterization; and if there is a sharp pain in the throat or heart, and the passage of air is blocked, do not touch the throat but reset it according to its natural position; then tighten it gently and leave it for no more than a day, applying treatments without delay until it heals; and if the wound has pressed into the bone, dig out any pieces of bone you can reach, leaving those you cannot until the wound festered and becomes disfigured; and for fresh wounds, apply the powder I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones or a fistula in the wound, treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	wound from a spear or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from a spear or knife, and deep, then consider the signs of its severity as the patient alone can show: then know that the wound is mortal; but if it is not too deep, and still has all its blood, do not apply powder in the first hour, nor bind it tightly so as to prevent further bleeding that might return to the body and cause the patient harm; instead, apply an attractive dressing and change it twice a day. And if you have no dressing, put old cotton in the wound to suck out the moisture, and keep the patient sleeping on the wound for three or four days, or more; if there is no spasm, nor any shaking or extreme pain, know that the patient is recovering. When you see these good signs, then know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Cure the wounds with various remedies and others, as long as they are healthy; and if they cannot heal, know that there is a fistula; then treat them as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	If the wound is from a sword or knife cut, and it is shallow or deep in the front, back, or side, treat it accordingly; if large, sew it up; and if small, use powder, and if it has penetrated into the bone and broken off pieces, clean the wound thoroughly if the pieces are devious; if they are not devious, let the wound heal, and gently extract foreign bodies; for other wounds in other limbs, judge them as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	disruption of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The disruption of the belly is great and medium and small; from a large wound there flows no time the intestine or the nerve of the intestines, which causes the entry of evil; and stitching is more difficult, and never worth less the small wound than the large one, because one must handle the intestines more carefully, if not from above and below; for the intestines soon swell, causing pain, if they are pressed again, and therefore the smaller wound is more mobile, because one moves the intestine to its proper place in contrast to others. And know that the rupture of the belly occurs according to four manners: The common stitches have their place in the stitching of the belly, and the stitching of other wounds on the body and other specific stitches are common to other wounds; nevertheless, they are more suitable for the stitching of the belly, and I will explain each one.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small and nothing of the intestine is damaged, and it is a difficult thing to reset, then this is one of two ways: either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen due to the injury.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in this way: moisten a sponge or a thin cloth with hot water alone, or cook water with squinant (a type of herb), and cypress, and spices, and raise the intestine until the swelling is removed; and never use wine as a constricting agent, and let it cool down slowly.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, if the intestine is filled with water or blood and the veins are closed, because by this means the entry becomes lighter for a little while; and if it cannot enter, make a slight cut in the wound with the instrument used to treat hemorrhoids; and the first cure is to move that which is blocking, that we should not cut without great need; and this is the instrument to split: cut inside the lump and push outward, observe the shape.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound has enlarged and the intestine protrudes, return it to its natural position in its proper place, if you have the ability, because this is preferable.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large, and it's in the lower part of the belly, then you should make the patient lie on their back, and raise their legs higher than their head; and if it's in the lower part of the abdomen, place the head and breasts higher than the lower parts, and pay attention so that the affected area is higher than the other; thus it is necessary to apply what I say for both large and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, prepare a moistened medicated oil and apply it to the entire wound with your fingers, then close the lips; this is the common method of stitching. Insert one or more needles according to the width of the wound, leaving two spaces at the head of the wound, and thread a strong, fine needle; pierce both layers of skin with the two points of the scalpel, assembling the two points of the scalpels together in three places; then tie a double thread around the needle from both sides, closing the wound neatly, continuing to do so until all the wound is closed. The needles should be neither too fine nor too thick; the fine ones capture all the tissue, and the thick ones cannot enter the skin and flesh well. Therefore, they should be medium-sized. Do not push the needles too far from the surface of the skin and flesh, or else they will open up the wound before the stitching is complete. Then cut off the needle points so that they do not disturb the patient while sleeping, and place a tent or cloth at the ends of the stitches to hold them in place until the wound is healed. This type of stitching is more suitable for small wounds; for larger ones, you simply stitch with one or two needles, threading a strong, medium needle, assembling both layers of skin and scalpels together, leaving spaces about as wide as a thin finger between each stitch. This method cured a man who had been stabbed in the belly, where the wound was more than a palm-width long and extended several palms from the intestines; it was deep within the abdomen.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought back the intestine after it had been out for twenty-four hours, and the wound healed completely within fifteen days, and it was cured, and it became healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And they marveled that he did not die, and it was a miracle; I did not cure him with any treatment, as I was in a place where none were found, nor any medicine; every day for two weeks, I put clean cotton on the wound and washed it with honey and water until it healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you the two proper ways of stitching: take the needle and the thread from the outer part of the wound until it reaches the inner; when it has pierced through the center, do not move the chief [of the stitch] but continue stitching or withdrawing the needle as you have done initially, and repeat on the other side until the stitching is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second way of sewing, which Galenus calls the proper method, is like nothing else, which joins the two parts together naturally, and applies one end to the other with great care: pierce a needle or the sharp end close by, and make a single hole in the flesh; leave the two ends of the thread intact. Then turn the needle and pierce it from the opposite side towards these ends inside; then pierce each one from the opposite side towards the others inside, through the other threads on either side; and this is the most moving way of sewing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen calls this method, and no one testifies to it: one must sew the belly with two needles, each with a thread; you should poke one needle from one side and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew intestines; and know that when the rupture is within the belly, the stitching is more difficult than for other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgment of the wound is like the judgment of other wounds: and it is that when you open a fresh wound and drain all its blood, if the arrow has moved, then you should stop the bleeding and apply a poultice with charred herbs, and if the arrow has moved further, then apply any available treatment as long as the wound remains open; then bind it tightly, and seal it with wax and mirra; then treat the wound like other wounds until it is healed; and if you have no medicines, put old cotton and move it twice a day until it heals.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you need no other medicine in addition to these arrangements when the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound is affecting important members, it is necessary to moisten a light linen cloth with hot temperate oil or rose oil, and place it around the affected area, and under the armpits; and if it feels painful or pus-filled, which often happens, then give it enemas of black wine, especially if the pus reaches the intestines. Puncture it inside, and know that when it is the large intestines, it is easier to heal than the small ones.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The internal organ called "young" cannot heal when it is weary, and this is due to the condition of its vessels, and the subtlety of all the body, and the proximity of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	If the gum (or 'zirbe') jumps out of the wound, reset it as you would the intestine, while it is still fresh; and if it has become old and turned white or black, then hold the black part still, as there are vessels and arteries beneath; then cut away the tissue in between, and hang the two gums down from the edge of the wound until the extraction of the gum is complete, making sure the wound bends.
de la routure dou boueil	from the rupture of the bowels
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestines are ruptured and the wound is small, it cannot be restored in any man, as I have seen a nobleman with a lance through his stomach; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, it became gangrenous and fistulous, and there issued excretion and flatulence; I applied treatment according to my ability, and did not cease subtilizing until he was healed, and the wounds were sealed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him healed, I doubted that the patient would not have pain in his stomach; but he felt no pain, only improved conditions, and eating and drinking; and certain physicians said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be treated in this manner: take a large reed, then gather the edges of the wound together, and when the reed has opened the mouth, place it between the two edges, so that it draws them tightly together; then cut off the head of the reed, and let it remain in such a way that he cannot unfasten it, then put another reed in the same manner as before, until the wound is completely healed; and dress the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If the disease is severe in the intestine, and causes no harm to the patient, one can bind the intestine with a thin thread cut from the intestine of an animal, in this way: take the tip of this intestinal thread, which is well-stripped, and tie it to the tip of this thin linen thread twisted, then wind the thread onto the needle and sew up the intestine, and arrange it in the wound; this method of sewing has no equal except according to the path of faith and hope; and if the wound is deep and wide, especially when it affects one of the main intestines, no one will heal it with any subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	whether it is a fistula, wherever it may be.
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Every wound or abscess, when it opens, is generally called a "fistula," especially if it is covered with hair and deeply infected.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	A fistula is according to true nature, hard and white, without feeling pain, just like the feathers of a bird; it doesn't heal clearly, sometimes thin and other times thick; sometimes moist, and other times dry; and I have already spoken in the division of wounds that every wound that is not healthy, and there is no discharge, is only due to one of the nine causes: namely, the smallness of blood or pus; or because of its evil nature; or because there is hard matter inside, preventing it from healing; or because there is too much discharge; or the flesh is rotten, and the material is of poor quality; or the medicine is not good for treatment; or because corruption has the manner of a plague; or because the proprieties in the region delay digestion, and late health, and are naturally flatulent; or it involves veins or bones, and I have already explained all these causes, signs, and medical cures in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is necessary that I inform you about the treatment of a fistula which is performed by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	You know that fistulas can occur in all parts of the body; for there are fistules that affect large veins, arteries, nerves, or any part of the digestive tract, bladder, or any of the ribs, or the spine, or any joint in the hands or feet, and if they affect the primary member and its corresponding parts.
