Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all fistulas of this kind are difficult to heal and require hard work and knowledge; and if there is a fistula that does not come to the place I mentioned, but you have faith in its cure and understand it, take a needle or iron wire, and if the fistula is straight, insert it as desired; and if it is crooked, seek a delicate surgical probe to adjust it according to its curvature; for the fluid will flow around the bend. And if the fistula has an opening that cannot be properly probed by instruments, clean it with a syringe from one of the openings, as moisture passes from one opening to another and cleanses it; then do it carefully at your convenience, knowing if there is bone or nerve, and if it is completely cut off, and ask the patient about the pain he feels when you press your hand on it, and the place where he feels it; and when you know the exact location, and whether it is far from a joint, or a nerve, or an artery, or a vein, or any of the places I mentioned, then cut it as I told you, and remove all foreign matter and corrupt flesh inside; and then cure it until it is completely healed, and if the fistula is very deep and straight, cut it completely, as much as possible, then place moist, medicated bands around it, and insert bottles with medicine until the superfluous fluid at the bottom has been washed away; and then apply hot poultices of clean, healthy fat while it heals; and if it does not heal through these means, cauterize it as we said, and if the bone is corrupt from the fistula, cut it out.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein or nerve does not affect the principal limbs, as we have said, and if the bone is exposed with corruption and blackening, the king must treat it until all corruption is removed, then heal the injuries thoroughly while it is sound; but if it remains unsound and bends back as before, know that you are not yet free: expose it and keep it in that state until you have removed all corruption, then restore it to its place; and if thus healed, it will be well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If no, know that the corruption is too deep for you to treat it; if there is no other way but to let nature take its course; and if there is a small bone corrupted, and you can pull it with tweezers, extract it with an instrument suitable for this purpose, and if there are many bones, break them not, leave none intact; and if moisture opposes you, causing doubt or fear, cauterize and dry, and heal the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, apply something putrefying to the wound, and let it fester until the pus has formed around the bones; then they will be more easily removed. If it is a large bone, like that of the leg or thigh, scrape off the corruption as much as possible until all blackness is gone, then dress the wound; if there is a great deal of putrefaction extending almost to the bone, cover and protect it completely until the corruption is healed, and then treat it until it is healed. And I will tell you about a fistula that occurred in a man's leg, so that you may take an example from it and provide aid in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	He was a young man around thirty years old who had a pain in his leg due to something that arose inside his body, causing substances to flow towards the leg, and he had a large abscess that could not be opened; but because of their foolishness, they pricked the abscess so much that many matters corroded, turning into a fistula, and he suffered from many openings through which all bowels and moisture from the body leaked out. Many tried to cure him for two years, but found no wise man skilled in such arts until I was called upon, and I examined his leg and the medicines used to cure him, and what had corroded through the openings into the flesh; and the young man's skin turned red, and it took on a citrine color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I set up a tent in one of these gaps, and then I examined all the gaps, and I found that some came against each other from every part of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I quickly acted and pressed into one of the gaps until I discovered a part of the bone, which I found corrupted and pierced, and the corruption reached down to the bone itself; I knew what appeared to be the corrupted bone, and thought there was no other corruption except that which I had left; and I began to treat the wound with medicines for a long time, but it would not heal. Then I examined it again, and discovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continuing in the bone, so I treated it and then opened it up, and applied medicine; and it healed and became sound, and did not want to begin the operation again, except for the weakness of the patient who could not bear it, and for the fear of death that I had of him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For in the evacuation of blood, it often becomes completely clean, and a hard scar forms in its place on the bone, and it has a good disposition and causes no harm or pain to anything at all, neither going away nor coming back.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be treated in this manner: take a linen bandage, stretch it over the opening of the bone, and instruct someone to pull it upward; then tie another thicker linen bandage over the first one, and bind it to the flesh that is detached from the bone, pulling it downward so that you remove the corrupt flesh from beneath, and expose the flesh on the bone where you see or feel the corruption. Place ashes or a table under the bone to prevent further corruption; and it should be treated as much as possible, so as to see and feel the corruption, and be treated again afterward.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if a bone is corrupted and will not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part, then expose the whole thing; then apply hot coals from one side to the other of the corruption, and be sure to cauterize it over a long period, as we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, cut off the corrupted joint, and if it is in the continuation of two joints, there is no other way but to cut them both; and if the corruption is in the fingers of the hand or foot, this thing is very difficult, but you must inquire how the corruption opens, and cleanse it in every way that you can, as long as the vein or nerve does not oppose you; and know that there are many instruments for cutting and cauterizing these bones, according to the position of the bone, its appearance, thickness, size, and hardness, and therefore it is necessary to match each instrument to the work; and know that the operation will show you the instrument you need, according to the knowledge of this art and the testimony of the ways of the diseases; choose the instrument that is suitable.
dou feu	with fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The joint dislocates either internally or externally; and when you have treated the inflammation with remedies, and they do not help, it is necessary to cover that limb until the inflammation disappears, so that the patient escapes from death or harm, which is greater, due to the defect in the member; and the signs of this are that the limb becomes black, as if burned by fire, and then turns white, since the inflammation spreads from one part to all parts of the body; hurry to cover it, and if it is caused by the bite of some venomous beast, such as a scorpion or a snake or similar, treat the head of the affected joint immediately, and do not give it time to come to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes up to the hand, so that the bone is dislocated at the joint, then the corrosion does not reach the arm; and if it comes to the arm, then the bone is dislocated at the shoulder; and if it passes by the shoulder, death is certain, and there is no cure outside of the quantity of its virtue; and thus it acts wherever the corrosion appears: if it starts at a joint, the bone is dislocated after the other joints; and if it comes to the foot, it dislocates the whole foot; and if it rises in the leg, it dislocates at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy than to leave the patient to die; and the manner of applying either bandage or splint to the limb is that you bind it above and below, and extend one assistant with each ligament, and you separate the skin between the two ligaments with a broad spatula, until the bone is exposed, then apply the splint or bandage, and place a linen cloth on each side so that the bandage does not touch the healthy part, and cause further damage and abscess to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if the bleeding occurs when you open, cauterize the vein carefully or apply certain powders to restrict it; then return to your medicine until it is completed, bind the afflicted member with a suitable ligature, and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to a man in great pain: he had a blackness that looked like a burn from fire, and that ulceration came first on his right big toe, until it discolored the whole toe; and when the man saw the ulceration, he covered his foot, and it healed; but after a long time, the ulcer returned on his left hand, and he came to me, and I placed reflective things over the purification of the body after the corruption, and it could not cease. And he begged me to cut off his hand, but I had no hope of reflecting the material; and I also doubted that if I cut off his hand, he would not die, since the strength of the man was weak; and he became completely despairing, returned to his land, covered his hand, and it healed; and I have never heard of a worse consequence for doing otherwise, if one has need.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	No abscess appears in a fat flesh, and it stays for so long that it causes great swelling; then it bursts and perforates, and the bowels jump out, and remain visible, just like a vessel; and the skin covering it is as thin as delicate cloth, and does not cover the bone or nerve, and such a condition is called "sain," and not "fistule"; but if it extends so far that it reaches the bone completely, then it is called "fistule"; and the flesh, if you cut all around it, especially when it is thin like cloth, should be cauterized to prevent its putrefaction.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you believe that the skin has become hard and the corruption is not completely healed and the skin is dry and brittle, then treat it with a cleansing enema in this way: examine if the breast is swollen and if there is an unpleasant odor coming from it; then give an Egyptian medicine made thus: take ashes, oil, and litargy (alum), in equal parts, and place them in a vessel over fire until the medicine turns red and becomes as thick as honey. Then, according to your need, mix it with water and honey, and use it for the enema to clean the breast and close the fistula; leave the medicine on for two hours, then extract it while squeezing; do this many times until the breast is completely cleansed and the pus is drained. And if Egyptian medicine or ash water is not available, grind ashes from vine roots, pour water over them, let it settle, and strain; use this for the enema as you know that the breast is thoroughly cleaned. If the patient cannot tolerate either of these, then give him an enema with a mixture of water and honey or ground litargy; or use just honey or sweet wine to cleanse and wash; when you have done this and believe the breast is completely cleansed, give him a cleansing enema using what causes charring in the breast, and apply some diaphanous plaster made with rose oil and wine. Or you can use various medicines and ointments whose properties I explained earlier in the chapter on ointments. And if the fistula opening in the breast is very small and the catheter cannot enter, enlarge it slightly with a hot iron; then place a small amount of Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment inside until it is enlarged enough for the enema. If the wound is too wide, cutting it will leave only part of the catheter inside or outside, and if the fistula opening downwards has more tissue above than below.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	For when the bowel is in perfect condition, it does not allow itself to protrude; and if you cannot cover the opening of the anus as you see fit, arrange yourself so that the bowel descends to its lowest point, for when the bowel is perfect, it does not allow itself to protrude, and if you cannot cover the opening of the anus as you see fit, arrange yourself so that the bowel moves slightly downwards, and do not leave any part of the bowel protruding; and take consolidative medicines to apply over the wound, and place them on a linen drape that covers the entire wound; then press firmly around the opening in the anus, making it wider than before, for often, in order to press the bowel, they remove the covering, and you must know what comes from the bowel: whether it is venom or poison or enough or too little, or digested or undigested; and be careful if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or no, and when your medicine has taken effect and you see the nature that arises over the opening of the wound in the anus, then you know that healing is approaching, and then loosen it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you unbind the wound, change the other drape, and renew the treatment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast is bowing downward due to indigestion after many days, know that the breast will not open.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons manifest after a long time, do not despair of health, for health approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are people whose spirits are so tormented by their wounds that they do the opposite of what is beneficial; and if the breast bowing downward due to indigestion after many days does not open, know that it will remain closed; and if the breast refuses to open, it is distant, so apply moist medicines with a subtle substance and dry in virtue as a final remedy, for there is much vitriol present, which is the last medicine. Take the final remedy and make it with rose oil and mix it with old wine of equal substance; then conserve it and use it; and do the same with heated honey thickened with cooked grain flour or alyssum root, which is like flour made from grains and herbs; use simple or composite remedies: grind them and make powder, and add to the honey I mentioned, and use it; and if the cure is prolonged, and this cure does not help, then know that corruption has taken hold, and it exerts pressure on the bones, or hard members, or ligaments, as in the case of a fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	from the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Gangrene is an abscess that forms under a nail in the hand or foot, or occasionally in other areas; and when it becomes old and one does not take care of it, it can lead to gangrene in the toes, causing them to rot and fall off as far as the root of the nail, and possibly even the entire toe. It causes intense, foul-smelling pain, and the flesh around the toe becomes wide and discolored.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When treating it as we have described in the previous section, if the treatment is not effective, you must remove all debris stuck under the nail, and then cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cautery is very great aid if the bone is healthy, and the nail is sound; and if the nail catches fire in the flame, and begins to burn, and you need to point it with a tool, and pull it out upwards, and gently remove that charred part, and apply to it hot and corrosive medications to remove all of it; then treat the wound with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corruption is in the bone, cut it off and pull it out, for as much as the bone decays, it cannot heal; and if you see both corrupting, cut it as mentioned above, then treat it until it is healed; and if it is burnt and blistered, and causes great pain, you must first treat the wound; then cut the nail with a sharp spatumile diagonally from above, and be careful that the cut does not reach the flesh under the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if this happens, apply something soothing.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain from the deep wound causes him great suffering.
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	He who is born into the hands of no one, perhaps because he is very fleshy, and perhaps he has a bone there, and never an angle, and none are born in the socket of the joint, where birth is against all reason.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	He who is born in no place at all, does not move, and he who is born at the joint of a limb, may remain immobile; for the size of him who is fleshy is very light, in that same manner: remove him from his root with a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born at the root of the joint is difficult to cure: if you keep him covered.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For him who is born or has an injury elsewhere, it is necessary that you first cover the wound thoroughly to the bone, then dislocate the bone to a suitable position, and then cure it as long as it is healthy.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The dislocations that come at any joint come either from birth, or from a wound becoming stuck, or from a burn of fire, or from similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	If you need to tie this suture, so that it must be repaired according to their natural forms; then place between two moistened cloths or drapes in rose oil, so that they do not adhere; or place between two pieces of fine cloth, as long as the limbs are sewn together, as appropriate.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If dislocation occurs in any of its fingers with the palm, tie this suture as appropriate.
des vils	of evil
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	They have thick, enveloped veins, full of melancholy excess, which come to many parts of the body; and there is more in the legs of those who walk, work, and carry, than others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is necessary for you to administer purgative once, and then cleanse the basil (i.e., the bowels).
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The cure for iron (or possibly a specific condition) is according to two methods: one is with the use of cupping and drawing out the black blood; and the other method is that you open the vein and drain it entirely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The procedure (or surgery) is as follows: first, immediately apply hot water to the leg, making it as warm and comfortable as possible, until the thick blood becomes thin; then, lift the sick leg from above the ankle towards the hip; next, cut the vein in one place, or two, or three, with a broad knife, then drain and extract the black blood with your hand, from the upper part to the lower, until enough blood has been drawn, as much as the patient can endure; then bind it up, and instruct him to consume food that will turn his blood black; and repeat the evacuation and cleansing when the veins are full, causing harm to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Lift the affected leg and if there are many hairs, immerse it in water, and raise it with hot water until it turns red and swells; then warm the veins. If you do not have a bath, heat it over a fire, and then apply it to the long vein at the top of the knee or at the ankle joint; cut open the skin over the vein until it is exposed. Cut the skin around the vein from both sides, making it red and bleeding; like a white cord. Pull the leg away from the body until the skin lifts off the vein, then make a second cut at the first joint; pull and cut again from another angle as you did before; continue cutting and pulling in this way. Once all the muscle is severed, cut the vein; and if it cannot be pulled out, insert a needle through the entire length of the thread and pull it along with the thread, pushing from behind at the same time, and turning your hand back and forth until it comes out. Be careful not to cut, as this prevents pulling and can cause harm to the patient; once you have completely removed it, apply a moist woolen cloth dipped in wine and rose oil to the wound and dress it until healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if it (the dislocation) is tight and twisted and wrapped up together, and it is not at all straight, as we have said, then you must cut it crookedly but do not cover it; treat it as we have previously mentioned.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The way to cut the joint without damaging it is to make a cut that does not pierce the vein; it should be done with great care because if it were too thin, it would cut into the vein, but since it needs to be thick as we have said, this is its form:
de la voinne civile	of the vein's cavity
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is found in the legs, in warm parts where no herbs or trees grow, and on land where there is no moisture; and sometimes it appears elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens because of putrefaction that comes from under the skin, as it winds and turns inside the body.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein appear, it is that there is a very great swelling in the leg, then the color changes, and the vein begins to protrude strongly, as if from the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the vein opens, it is necessary to wrap around a piece of cloth from one and a half to two fingers thick, and leave it on the leg; and at every instance when there is no discharge, wrap around the cloth again, and do not cover it at its base, until it has completely drained; for if you cut it, it will return to the flesh, causing abscesses and putrefaction or other illnesses. For this reason, it should be treated little by little, up to the point where no part of it remains in the body; and it is often a vein that is about five or six fingers long when it is first opened, and when you cut it, it retracts one or two millimeters, and pierces through to the bottom, completely draining. And there should be nothing left inside, and remedies should be applied to the wound daily to prevent putrefaction until the cure is complete, as with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And in no case should this vein be cut again, especially when it opens at the ankle joint or at the foot, and there is much bleeding and from which it jumps; then treat it as we have said above.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	vers that are born between skin and flesh.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called "beef disease" in our land because it often affects cattle, and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh. It spreads throughout the body, moving up and down, and it feels very painful as it moves from one member to another until it breaks through the skin where it was, and then it goes away with great force; and it is caused by the putrefaction of certain humors, just like worms, snakes, or lice in the belly. One doubts its severity, for when it travels through the body and reaches the head, it can go to the eye, perhaps retreat, and destroy the eye. This happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it healing and drawing, it cannot be done further unless it is completely healed: therefore, it is necessary that you hold the limb above and below with a strong, tight ligature, then cut and draw it out forcibly, and if the vein bursts, apply fire cautery until it heals; and the greatest harm it does is when it lets blood, as we have said; and if you see it coming close to the oil, tighten the ligature on the brow, then cut and draw it out forcefully; and it is advisable for the patient to use purification of the body with solvents and medicines to drain evil humors, and to cleanse putrid meats.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	The pain that comes from flatulence.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This illness is called "weakness" in our land, and it brings pain to any limb, and then moves from one limb to another; and I have seen this as I told you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and I examined her arm, and saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and after that, I noticed a small worm-like thing rising on her shoulder, brighter than anything else, like living silver when it moves from one place to another; the pain left that area and moved to her shoulder, and then, shortly afterward, spread throughout her body, reaching the other arm; then she told me that she felt it moving around inside her body.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was very amazed at how she moved from one limb to another, for I had never seen this disease in such a way.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Nevertheless, I wanted everyone to understand that the pain should move from one place to another, but I had not seen this happen as much as with the woman; and I thought it was because she had dry skin and exposed veins, which is why such stiffness appeared; and I did not find the same reason for those who are sickly, and have moist skin and closed veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see this disease cured, and the patient feels this pain, if it opens up as we have said, press it gently from above and below, until this constrained stiffness in the limb leaves; and cauterize the limb; and if you do not have these things at hand, cure it with those that remove stiffness, such as foul pills, stonecrop pills, and others like them.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The arrows vary, according to their appearance and according to the parts of the body from which they originate.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	Their diversity lies in that there are those with large and small tips, some with barbs, others sealed; and those with two angles, or with tongues, or with pieces; and those that shoot into any member do so in different ways: either into a principal member, like the head, body, liver, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it comes out in any part of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you below, appears: it is necessary that you fight against the extraction of this arrow, because death comes later in various ways; and when this bad sign does not appear for you, and the arrow is not completely extracted, pull it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when the arrow comes out and pierces the bone, and if there is satisfaction above the brain, it is when scotoma, sudden darkness, and seeing halos around objects occur; and redness and inflammation of the tongue, spasms, and difficulty in understanding, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps the arrow comes out from the nose or ears; and sometimes it causes loss of speech and voice; and also pus-like discharge from the wound that looks like a worm, and there is also sudden, strong pain similar to that of a horse's kick; and if these signs appear to you, and you are in charge of the cure, then extract the arrow even if it is not embedded.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of an arrow when it breaks or pierces the body is that it is near the left breast, and feels as if it were embedded in something hard, not empty; and sometimes the arrow becomes silent like the pulse, and there is black blood, and coldness and cold sweat, and fainting: so know for certain that death is approaching.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow that never draws blood is that no foam comes from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient's face turns pale, and they breathe heavily and stop moving.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow breaks in the deepest part of the flesh, it is very painful, causing great pain and heavy breathing; and all the muscles of the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow pierces the stomach, perhaps something from the unwanted flesh jumps out.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow pierces the abdomen, and something jumps out through the intestines, there is no hope for healing or extraction of the arrow in this case.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow pierces the bladder, the urine jumps out and gushes out, and the patient feels intense pain; know that this wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, as they make and feel hot and cold and pain in the throat and shoulder and aid (joint) and sharp pain down the back and stiffness and the knees and legs, and the limb appears similarly, are safe according to various dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or an artery, and it is not venomous, as I shall tell you what happened to me, because you do such things.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	There once happened to me a case where an arrow struck the ear or the jaw: I tried to remove it by reaching around behind the ear fat, and it was completely healed without any injury.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And tried another time with an arrow that had struck in the fat beneath the paper of the skin, and the arrow was completely withdrawn, leaving only the point against the flesh, and it was a large arrow with a blue arc, without causing any pain; the wound healed, and no ill accidents came to pass.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And pull a sharp arrow from the throat of a Christian, which had Arab ears; I cut the barbs, and drew it out as gently as possible, and healed the Christian.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And I pulled an arrow from a man who had it in his belly, and thought he was dying; but after thirty days, he showed no change in condition; then I cut the arrow, cleaned it, and drew it out, without any bad outcome.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you wish to help a man whose arrow is stuck in his back, and the wound has become infected; and the arrow remains inside him, and he shows no change in his natural conditions, nor does he experience any discomfort in his natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And see another man to whom an arrow has struck his face, and the wound has healed; but he still endures great pain without suffering; and many others like him.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And I treated a prince, the king himself, who had an arrow in his neck that was slightly displaced to the right side; and the arrow was completely embedded, and I was called to treat it after three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very tight.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I applied it very gently, and he felt nothing; but he had a sharp sensation and pain beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow I applied a soothing poultice to the wound because the swelling did not subside; and I could see the arrowhead.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I left the poultice on for several days, and thus soothed the wound, and held the patient for a long time until he no longer felt the arrow inside his body; and he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied a corrosive medicine to the wound for several days until it healed and then probed it; I felt the tip of the arrow that was embedded in the flesh; then I adjusted the opening of the wound using that medicine until the tip of the arrow became visible; and it took over three months for the wound to heal. Then, I used pincers and moved them from one side to another, but I could not extract it; after which I continued to try subtle and clever methods until I found a way to use pincers shaped in a certain manner as described at the end of this chapter, while I pulled on the arrow and reopened the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And they consider that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored: so I restored it, and the wound healed, and the patient was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	I have also told you about the quality of extracting certain arrows, so that you focus on what I am saying rather than what is written in books, for they cannot contain everything; but wise masters compare well and consider both small and significant things, applying new techniques and new instruments to unfamiliar issues in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not come out of the members where they are embedded, but in two ways: either through the vein where they entered or from another place; and that which comes out from the side where it entered is an arrow that has penetrated into the flesh and cannot come out now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not now move, let it grow until the flesh around it decays and becomes light; and also if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, leave it for several days, and each day move it slightly; then it will move, or pierce through all the surrounding wood, until the space around the bone is widened, and then pull it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone at the top and goes down to one of the brain cavities, and none of the accidents I mentioned affect the patient: do not pull it out, but let it stay as long as it remains straight for several days, because if it goes all the way down, it will be fatal.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is embedded in the bone alone and does not come out satisfactorily, it leaves the patient without any further harm if the skill of pulling it out is used.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply embedded and cannot come out, then apply tar to it as I have told you; then treat the wound while it is healthy.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is lodged in the flesh deeply and cannot be seen, one should try with all their might; and if you feel it, use any suitable instrument; and if you cannot because of the tightness of the wound or the depth of the arrow, and there are no bones or nerves or veins, leave it until the wound becomes large; and pull the arrow if you can, and if it has roots by which it is attached, remove the charred part from both sides as much as possible, then break or bend the arrowheads until you can pull it out. Be careful not to break the arrow itself so that you do not make the wound worse.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, wait until the swelling around it subsides, then treat it, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	If the signs of blood poisoning concern you, follow what we have said about treatment in that chapter; and be careful with incising near nerves and veins, and use whatever means you can to extract the arrow safely, at once or later, firmly or gently; and place the patient according to the position it was in when the arrow entered, for this is the greatest aid, and if you cannot do so, put him in a position that the signs show.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	He knows the arrow that comes from another direction, where it opens something of his body, or the skin is inflamed in that place if one sees or feels it apparently: so cut there, as long as the pincers can grasp it, and then pull it out: if it comes out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	If it is stuck in the bone, turn your hand round, until it enters the bone, widening it, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot be pulled out, leave it for now, and then try to pull it out again until it comes out; and if the arrow is embedded in the bone, do not remove it, but apply pressure around it, so that when you do extract it, the point of the arrow enters the groove of the instrument, and then push it out, and if the arrow is removed from the bone, apply an instrument with a pointed end entering at the same time to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is embedded, it is necessary that you remove all the soil around where the venom is, if you can, and then treat the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow comes out in the side or abdomen or near the ribcage, and it is accessible, remove it; but be careful not to touch the vein or nerve, then extract it, and dress the wound as needed, and treat it until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The form of the pliers used to extract arrows resembles an eagle's beak, and here is its shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways of doing this: great, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The form that points downwards like a horse's tail is also similar to the feather of a bird, to push the tip of the arrow, as this is the shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The form of claws to push and grip is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the common veins of the body,
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are 31 veins from which one can draw blood, of which there are 16 main ones: two beats located behind the ears, called "herbech"; and the two arteries prominently visible in the temples; and the two veins in each arm, called "aspires"; the vein across the forehead; the vein at the crown of the head; the two glands located on the collarbone; and the two veins found above the lips, called "augeherich"; and the two veins beneath the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The common veins from which one draws blood are five in each arm: one is the cephalic vein, located on the left side and called by the common people "vein of the head"; and the middle one is called "fast" and is composed of the cephalic and basilic veins, and is called by the common people "vein of the body"; and the basilic is on the right side and is called by the common people "vein of the belly", located above the femur, and it is the one that appears clearly when opening the vein.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the cure is the vein that is between the little finger and the ring finger, and if it rains; and in the leg, there are three veins: one is below the knee on the left side, and the second is at the ankle on the right side; and the vein called 'nasse', which is at the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg, there are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The treatment of veins behind the ears aids in the cure of old catarrhs and migraines. The quality of the treatment consists of raising the patient's head and rubbing the affected area with a rough cloth; then, tighten the bandage around the neck to expose the two veins behind the ears, hanging down from the head. Hold them there and feel for the pulsing beneath your hand; then take the lancet and puncture the vein just below the bone, drawing blood upward along the vein. Lift your hand above the affected area and repeat the process until you have drawn enough blood; then bind and dress it, as described in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	He heals the two arteries that are in the temples, if they are old and thin and accustomed to weeping, and at the back of the eyes there are hot tears. The quality of the healer is as I say: he pulls the sick person's neck until the two vessels open wide; he feels the pulse below his right index, and then signs with a stick; then gently presses on the vein high up on his left side, withdraws the lance, opens the vein high up, and stops the bleeding, as you did for the other veins. He lets the blood out according to need, then loosens the patient, and places his right hand on the artery for an hour, then wraps it with cotton; he forms a bandage and leaves it until it heals; we have spoken much of their healing and extraction, at the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The health of the vein in the forehead is as valuable as the health of the brain as much as old facial diseases, and to migraine and redness; its quality is such that the patient pulls his head by twisting, until the vein appears. Then take the instrument called "drier", whose form is as follows:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the tip on the vein, and hold it with your hand or something else, and let the blood flow out according to the amount you see; then release the patient's head, and tie the vein as long as it remains healthy without cutting a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Nevertheless, the flames should not be too intense; and if the wound is diagonal, since the bone is close, it may break the flame when it is thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The wound of the two veins located in the armpits is helped by itself, and at the edge, and at the red swelling, and at the pain in the eye, and for facial diseases; and the quality of its wound is such that the patient tenses his collar without twisting any ligament, as before. Then the healing, and indeed the wound, is slightly curved, a little long with the flame, and somewhat wide, because there is no choice.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are subtle, they may break; then draw out the blood carefully, as much as needed, and then bind it with cotton, and tie it tightly.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The venise of the nose is very valuable for a cold, sudden sickness, and facial ailments such as migraines and redness that come to the face, especially when it is old. The quality of the venise is such that the patient tightens his jaw, then pulls his nose to your left hand, and takes the subtle flame, long, and inserts it between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well enough, and the blood will begin to flow now; do not dig too deep, and let the blood flow as needed, then bind it for a night, for it is quickly restored; and this is the form of the flame.
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.
