The holy oil of the two glands is helpful for narrowing the eye, and for the beginning of inflammation, and for many ailments, and for impetigo, and for corrosion, and for herpes, and for boils; and its quality is such that it draws out the pus from both inside and outside, as we have said; and let the master be over the head of the patient with the illness, and let the patient sit on a seat, then clean the vein with long and wide strokes, then treat with warm blood, as much as is needed; then repeat on the other vein, then loosen the bandage, and tighten the veins slightly so that the patient does not choke; and leave it until morning, so that the wound may heal.
de la sainie des leivres	from the health of the veins
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The health of the veins in the lips helps to maintain moisture in the mouth, and it aids in healing gum disease, splits in the lips, and pain and swelling around them.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of the veins is such that you make the patient sit before you, hold their chin as I said; then turn the lip and look at the veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, and you recognize them by their black color and the small black veins around them: so cut both, and if you do not know them or are in doubt, cut the thicker one from each side, and also do the same with the two veins above and below, because it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	from the purity of the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The purity of the veins that are detached from the tongue is most beneficial after cleansing the head, and it helps with throat constriction, eye diseases, and mouth ailments; and the quality of purifying is such that the patient should hold their tongue between their hands in front of the sun, gently loosening it, and examine each side for a black vein: then cleanse both, but do not over-press, for they are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the neck, which are commonly cleansed, are done in two ways: either with a sharp flame heated to a moderate temperature, or with a delicate olive-shaped instrument called an "anesil"; and they are wide and narrow according to the width and constriction of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the flame burns brightly if it is very renowned, and it is wide as you can see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it requires skill to open veins that are smooth and contain thick blood and pus; and this is the shape of the olive-colored flame.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more delicately pointed, and is used to heal the delicate veins where there is subtle, citrus-colored blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The health (sainie) of the basilic vein, which is one of these veins, is very helpful for illnesses that affect the throat, and the collarbone, and the chest, and the belly; and it is important for the healer to heal gently and wash away the artery below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if it cuts the artery, and blood flow stops, as I have said, it must be stopped; and the fire should not be painful, but cutting like a blade.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the vein does not open clearly, it is necessary that you extract it and choose another one; either you want to apply pressure or clean the vein in the arm, it opens clearly; and cut it with a blade, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you come to know the vein, it is necessary that you extract the arm and touch the vein until you feel the pulse; then mark the spot with a sign, and bind the arm, and cut the vein with a blade; and be careful not to harm the artery when you see it swell, for that is the artery: avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see a discharge coming out at the top as urine from a child, and the skin is red and thin, know that it is without an artery: so hurry, and put your finger over it for a long time, then remove your finger when the bleeding has stopped, which often happens; let the arm be still, and leave it like that, and do not move the patient; be afraid, and do not move until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the skin is not stained and it bleeds, and no medicine is at hand, if you can open the artery, for the source of the retreat, and stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	Take a piece of fig bark, cut it, and take one half and wrap it tightly to the other side; if it stays in place without falling, that is good. If not, treat it as we have said, with powders that stop blood flow; the stopping will not cause further harm due to the small size of the wound and the strength of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	If the vein is infected from the top or bottom, it is necessary to drain blood from it, for it is composed of basilic and cephalic veins as we have said; the healer should press on the nerve below, and if he cannot find it exactly, he should find the nerve and open it; it will swell and cause pain, and healing may be affected, and in some cases, it does not heal at all; this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in any other person due to its subtlety, then you must cure it with an instrument; take care not to injure the nerve.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if the vein is between the two bones, make it open long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The treatment for the head wound is as follows: it draws blood from the head, and aids in the healing; and it is beneficial to apply olive oil or myrrh flame, as this is the safest of all veins, as it does not affect any nerve or artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Nevertheless, it is advisable to seek the most gentle method, and do not be concerned if it hurts the first time, just try again; and sometimes the veins swell up in some people when they are punctured for the first time, but this should not cause concern.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the health lies according to your own thinking.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about health is that health is maintained solely for the purpose of preserving health and preventing future illnesses; and healing should take place in one of the three veins, namely, the cephalic, femoral, or basilic vein; and one should heal during the beginning of prayers at dawn, and in autumn and winter after meals, when the signs of saturation appear; and one should heal on the first day or third day, after two to three hours.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The healing that is administered for illnesses has no fixed time, but rather as needed during the day or night, whenever it is necessary; and one should not heal children until they are twelve to fourteen years old, nor women who have recently given birth until after seven months.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	One should not treat the old who have passed sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when anyone wishes to be cured, in any way whatsoever, it is necessary for him to empty the bowels with a light enema, if he has retained much feces, so that the veins do not draw from the intestines too many harmful residues to the principal members; nor should one cure someone who is excessively salt with meat or wet, as long as they have such conditions; and be careful to cure after colic, vomiting, abdominal distension, frequent sexual intercourse, hard work, overstudy, and fasting; then subtilize the humors carefully, if they are thick, through diet, drinks, and medications, if you have access to them; then enter the bath, if nothing prevents it, to purify the blood, and cure the vein from the third day onwards, as we have said; and be careful that day to avoid work, exertion, lust, and similar things; and be peaceful and joyful, and make yourself healthier than those whom you are curing, and rub the affected area with your hands twice or three times, then gently press the swollen vein from above, for when it is too tight or stiff, it cannot be corrected otherwise; and then rub the area with oil, and place your left-hand index finger under the vein, a little below where you wish to cure it, so that the vein does not rupture while applying treatment.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that flow as if tied with cords in the body, and if they are of a kind that are troubled by impurities, when one applies fire, it draws away from the flame, and cannot open the vein, thus becoming one of them; and if he opens the vein, the wound is too tight, so it is necessary for the healer to be aware of these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens the first time, it is good; but if not, it begins again from the previous place or with greater difficulty, as the limbs are not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the limb is swollen and the patient is afraid, let it be for one or two days without binding it; perhaps abscesses will form later. Do not enter a bath, but continue the treatment as it pleases you; if the opening is small, carefully perforate it subtly, and doubt not that it may release as much blood as you see, precisely in that same wound, for fear of swelling; and work a little more gently so that the limb does not swell. This often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the vein swollen, do not recommence the treatment, and apply a little oil to it, for it lightens the body of blood, and the oil moves in this vein the substance that causes the swelling; and thus administer the oil in each wound that you treat veins, to stop the flow of blood; and the same is done with lint and bandages when applied to the vein; if it is very swollen, the oil softens and spreads it.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if a large abscess occurs, which happens frequently, especially when the vein is only slightly open, act quickly and apply a moist sponge with hot water and hemp for an hour; and you should do this after the blood flow from the vein has stopped, and if it remains in place after several days without turning black or green, it does not cause harm; and if you notice, apply any aloe or myrrh prepared in calament juice, or similar substances.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often there appears an abscess and swelling in the holy basil; then place your hand upon it, and if you feel the joint soft under the pressure of your hand, that is when the appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	So be careful not to apply anything we have mentioned, for it might cut off the flow from the artery; but make a dry plaster to harden the joint, then use another remedy until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each case of pain according to the quantity of its strength and the color of the pain.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the wound is still infected, let it continue to heal until the redness disappears; and if you see it swelling, leave it alone until it becomes less pronounced; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for the strong and robust person, who needs to extract blood, to make a wider wound, with broader incisions; and for the weak one, do the opposite, making smaller and more frequent wounds, and take care to heal them diagonally rather than deeply, and this method of healing saves from infection and nerve damage, and is better than long and wide wounds.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And to him whose body goes to the bathroom, it is necessary to give a mild pain in the juice of pomegranates; if he is overheated, he should drink warm blood three or four times, and if he has a cold complexion, he should take before going to the bathroom, a moist pain in syrup made from musk, or aromatic honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and dates, and a well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints in the bathroom after the release of much blood, it is necessary that he breathes a soup of coal and a subtle fragrant syrup, and uses other things that we have mentioned in the section or chapter on syncope for the evacuation of veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to extend his arm and heal it later, if it is weakened by much blood loss, he should treat it little by little, according to the quantity of its ongoing power.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wishes to extend his arm after the first dressing and has a strong cramp, he should heal it seven hours after the first dressing, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wants to heal from another place should be healed on the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is much blood within the body, which has been heated, and causes fever; so it needs to be drawn out in large quantities, and the wound widened until it feels better; then, after fulfilling all the conditions of health, place your hand on his pulse when he is recovering, lest death come instead of recovery, and this happens often when healing is neglected; and it is not right when you release the arm and cause blood to flow again, and close the wound, while it is still healing, for that would be harmful; but leave it until it feels better a second time; or if there is a sharp pain at the point of the flame, until the frost within the vein disappears, apply a little silk soaked in water, and press gently.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, let it be and do not squeeze it until the abscess is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it becomes necessary to treat the blood from an abscess a second time, if the wound is in the same place or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is cleaned in place of the vein in the head because it is composed differently.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the method of cleansing is that the patient should hold their hand in hot water until the veins are red; then tie it slightly so that the vein appears well, and now cleanse through it, not too wide or too long; and make the incision large enough to allow for drainage, without allowing any pus to escape, then return the hand to hot water and let the blood flow until you have enough. And if this is done, do not stop the hand from being in hot water, because more heat is applied than necessary; and cleansing of this vein is safer than any other, as it contains neither arteries nor nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The salve for the salvation of the hand's health on the right side is good for all diseases of the flesh: stretch the hand and immerse it in hot water until the vein is swollen if you see it; then cross the limb, embrace it from every side, so that nothing disturbs it; do not cut too deeply, because the nerve is entirely devoid of its covering, and then return the hand to hot water, for if the skin becomes frozen in the wound, it will not be able to heal.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as best you can, apply oil and silk to the vein to bind it tightly, and do this for every person.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The healthy person holds the mouse with their left hand to treat the pain in their right side; they do the same as I have told you for the left side.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The wise woman treats all diseases that affect the body, such as diseases of the womb, retention of flowers (perhaps referring to menstrual issues), diseases of the kidneys, and old ailments of the feet and legs, and similar illnesses.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of her medicine is such that the patient drinks warm water and rubs the vein until it heals, binding it over the joint of the foot; and if the vein is at the ankle, it goes up from there with much pain. Thus, depending on whether the swelling is greater or more severe in the leg or at the ankle, that is where treatment should focus.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you treat it on the foot, be careful not to touch the bones inside, and clean it thoroughly just as if you were bandaging; and apply the flames gently.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	If the pain does not subside, immerse the foot in water and let the vein drain completely.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the dressing is applied for the first time, repeat it a second time slightly above, as the bones are salty; do not doubt the nerves, as we have said, and do the same thing with the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The vein's lion is at the knee joint, and its inflammation causes pain in the back, when it is due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of its inflammation is such that the patient feels pain in the bath, and three turns are required to remove it from the knee, for otherwise the vein does not open; and if it opens, then all the ways you can think of, and by passing through; and it requires great effort to close it, for the lion is free, and it is very much exhausted by manual labor.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not succeed, a small amount of blood will open on the back of the foot towards the little toe, and be careful not to tighten the nail; and make sure that the inflammation is as dry as possible, then loosen the bandage, place cotton and tighten it; now the wound is healed.
des sainies de ventouse	from the suction of the cupping glass
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cupping glasses are made of horn, or iron, or glass; and cupping is performed in two ways: either by piercing and drawing blood, or without piercing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	This non-piercing cupping is performed in two ways: either at full heat or without heat; and the cups placed on the body are as follows: twelve on the torso, with one at the top of the head, others along the neck, two on each side of the neck, one under the chin, two on each shoulder, two on each leg, two on each ankle, and two on each wrist. The procedure does not involve drawing blood; it is merely about opening small veins scattered across the body, so as not to weaken any part of the body, much like with vein cupping. It should not be applied to any condition arising from a full stomach, until the entire body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if by necessity of illness or custom, it is necessary to purge, we should do so each hour at the beginning and end of the month, and every day; for there are such who, when they need to purge, have a heavy head; and some who experience fullness and redness in their faces, heads, necks, and darkness; and those who feel a drop of blood in their mouths, and their tongues are swollen, and they cough up blood; and there are those who dream and see blackness, pain, death, and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially in the middle of the month, we order purging after three hours during the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The doctor of the museum helps with the pain in the head ... which comes from the joints, and it is not appropriate to do this after evacuating all the body; and this treatment is for the museum of the cephalic, and it is not appropriate for those with a cold complexion, or those who have scabs, because it does them much harm; and for this reason, the old should not use it, nor those who suffer from cold headaches.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who heal themselves often become obstinate, and for this reason, a suction cup should be placed slightly lower, out of doubt of obstruction.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The ventilation of the chest is beneficial for the health of the heart and basil (organs), and therefore it helps to tighten the muscles, open the channel of the penis, and relieve pressure; however, it should be done with caution, as holding it too tightly can cause discomfort or damage to the stomach and body.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The ventilation of the chest between the ribs provides relief from headaches, eye pain, migraines, choking, and root tooth pain, and is beneficial for the health of the heart and basil (organs). It is important that the patient directs their breath without pressing on the arteries to avoid any complications with blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	The inflammation of the gums is beneficial for mouth diseases, and for the corruption of gums, and similar ailments in the mouth; it is found in the health of both lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The inflammation of the shoulders is beneficial for diseases that arise from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The inflammation of the veins is just as beneficial as three veins in the arm, as it draws blood from these large veins; and instructs the patient not to press too hard, for the flesh is devoid of color, and knows how to heal nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The vacuum that is on the thigh is as dangerous as bloodlets from the depths, and to diseases below, and it is necessary that the vacuum be large, and of iron, that it may need to be pulled well; and by chance, if it were too fine, it would break; and it causes great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The ventouses on the legs tighten strongly, as they draw blood from throughout the body, and are as painful as ancient pains in the rain, and in the back, and in the bladder, and cause inflammation; and they affect the joints of the two thighs, and the two ankles, and nevertheless, after long use, they weaken the body and bring more pain.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of applying the cup is such that you first place it on the skin while it is still empty, and suck gently, then apply it firmly and move it equally, not ceasing this until you see the red color and heat of the blood, and open the pores; then remove it, and be mindful of the condition of the skin, for there are some who have thick and others who have thin pores: it is only necessary to strike once, and make wide incisions, and somewhat deep; suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the vein is thick, it is necessary to strike twice: first to open the path for the thick blood flow.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the pain is very intense, it is necessary to strike the third time; and when we want to draw out blood little by little, we suffice once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want a lot of blood, we must do it often; and if the pain is intense, striking with precision until the veins burst, which is good for those with thick and hard skin, and who have hairy legs, one should apply oil to the suction cups, either stimulating or dissolving: it can be violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil; and if it's in ivy, watercress oil, or chamomile oil, or other similar herbs.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is thick and cold, take amber oil, or balsam, or donkey oil, and similar substances.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if anyone has a tender, wide-open wound, it is not appropriate to apply oil, but instead, wash it after the application of rosewater, or cold water, or morelle water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or any similar liquid.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those with excessive moisture should rise from it using myrrh water, sumac water, and similar substances.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have excessive superfluities should rise from old wine, or holy water, or decoction of nettle or chamomile, or other similar things; and one should not use a cupping glass before the bath or after, but an hour or two after the bath; and one should not sleep after cupping, and it is necessary that he washes himself, when it is time to cup and when he has been cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And beware that the patient with a hot temper does not become too agitated and inflamed; it is necessary for him to press cold things, such as pomegranates, endive, lettuce, and similar things; and eat little, and porridge, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And he who has a cold complexion, should take syrup of honey, and moderate wine that is neither too old nor too new, and eat little, and enjoy raisins and small birds; and on the day that he takes fresh air, he must drink more than he eats; and it is appropriate to give any man triacle or musk before or after ventilation to strengthen his principal members; but it is not advisable for those who are hot to consume it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The cups that are placed without causing harm are those placed on the liver, and on the spleen, and gout, and on the belly and the bowels and the kidneys and the hips, for these members do not tolerate being pricked, and they are only used to draw blood from one member to another, as we place cups on the mammary glands when the nipples are healthy; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we place cups on the belly and bowels to reduce the member; and it removes pain, when there is congestion or a stone, so it may perhaps attract the congestion, or abandon the stone from its place; and it does so when placed on the liver and spleen when there is retained windiness, and these cups are emptied to suck only; and they are never heated with fire, nor filled with cold water, as in cases of tears that flow freely, and in this manner one fills the cup with hot water mixed with herbs suitable for it.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the suction cup applied with fire is this:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	It should have a width of two and a half palm lengths, and on one side near the middle, it should have a small hole, as if to fit an needle, and be made of iron or steel, so that it does not pierce the patient when placed on the body; and in the middle, there should be a crossbar of iron or steel, to hold a cloth, and their sizes vary according to the illness and age of those who use them; for the suction cups for children are different from those for adults, and thinner than the fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one should place this suction cup over the affected member: take the wax or linen cloth and place it through the hole in the suction cup, so that the clarity is at the bottom of the cup to prevent burning the patient; then place it on the member, and your fingers should be on the opening we have mentioned, so that when you want, the vapour goes out, and remove the suction cup; and use the linen cloth as before, and repeat often if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the case of the suction cup used for pleurisy, or any other acute condition, it has no hole or opening, and should only be applied when the surface is dry, and placed on the affected member only once; this is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Without any bonds or constraints that would prevent them from moving, only in members such as lips and gums, and similar areas, are tourniquets applied; and in cases where the skin is stripped of hair, like on the face, hands, or other places; if the quality of the wound allows it, immediately apply a tourniquet to these areas. Soak them in sweet water until they become soft and then clean the wound with a vein and tourniquet, after ensuring there is nothing in their stomachs; subsequently, wash the member with a vein and tourniquet, rub it until it turns red, and reapply the tourniquets; when they stop bleeding, bind them again, if it is possible to do so.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If the lion rises from its sleep and then from water, it feels much better and is refreshed; and if the joints are too stiff after the body's heat, moisten them with cold linen and place it on top until they are relaxed; and if the stiffness increases, apply vitriol or gall or similar substances until they are relaxed; or you can put half-peel peas on the lion, leaving them until they adhere to the joint, which will now relax; and if you need more, take other lions.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the lions do not want to be taken, rub fresh blood on them or insert an needle into the stiff joint until it releases, then apply it and soon as they feel the blood, they will relax; and when you see that they start to move, sprinkle some aloe and silk powder or ash, and they will stop.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	We begin the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it restores fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know this, dear reader, that the foolish eyes cast aside this chapter, which they have never seen nor read in any ancient books; and for this reason the science is strange to our land, for I have never found it good, except through the knowledge of ancient books, on which I have studied so much that I have treated the science both by experiment and by the habits of my life. And I have described to you in this chapter what is contained, and abridged it at the end, and clearly shown the forms of the instruments used, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we recite at the beginning of this book the summa of its words and the chapters where the wise men place their understanding, pausing over truth, so that those who are tested know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	When a fracture, dislocation, or twist occurs in any part of the body, it is necessary to hasten to heal the patient on both sides. If none of these remedies are effective, such as weakness of the body, illness, or old age; or if the temperature is too hot or too cold; and he avoids cold things like ice, raw meat, and goose fat, and does not drink wine, nor consume any fatty foods, and does not overeat meats that clog the veins, until you have no doubt of an abscess forming, or spreading of material in the member; then the patient will return to his former state as if he had never been ill.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that one alleviate the patient from foods that cause excessive flatulence, or have a viscous consistency, such as cooked wheat in water, and laughter, and talking, and pressure, and eating rich food, and drinking, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For excessive flatulence can return and even worsen the fracture.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that bones broken in the elderly or those with decrepitude cannot heal well and solidify according to their nature due to the fragility of the members, nor can those that are too tender, such as the bones of young children; however, do not be discouraged, hold fast to the broken bone with firm grips that join the member together, as it was before, and do not restrict its movement entirely, and for this reason, it is necessary to alleviate them from heavy foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the foot, and in this chapter, I will tell you all manners of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	Because there is a fracture that goes to the bone, and another when sharpening, like the blade of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with a wound, and the fracture is just a tiny crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each type of dislocation has its own mechanism and specific tool for restoration, according to the memory that comes to mind in its place; and the fracture of the bone is known because the joint is twisted, widely opened from the outside, and sounds when pressed by the hand; and when there is no curvature or imperfection upon touching, and the patient does not feel great pain, there is no fracture; but it can have curvature, a fissure, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	You should not move it with the hand; instead, apply medications that will be described later, and then gently tighten it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the fracture which goes up in the air, and the two parts are disjoined, it is now necessary to set them equal, so that the abscesses come there; and if hot abscesses come, let him leave them no day until the abscesses are healed; then put them equal in movement that you can gently and effectively, and know that the restoration of them is lighter than the restorations of those where they have broken off; then tighten it as necessary afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if a bone is broken into two parts, whether it is in the foot or hand, or one of the smaller members, or at two joints, or at one joint and in your hand, place the member according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken member are aligned, all the additions in their places be equalized by your work, and beware that through your handling no further injury or pain comes to the patient; and adjust well the two joints of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And it will feel good to the touch if it seems not well: if it is dressed nicely, and not pulled too hard, not pressed as those who cause a hot abscess and contraction in the member with their own work, as we have often wanted.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the member is at its limit, it is wise to be gentle with the patient so he does not move it, neither awake nor asleep, nor by turning or any other means; and take good care that the member is completely secure so as not to feel any pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when he feels no pain, except that it is not yet completely healed, it is necessary to put him in a position where he feels no pain; and be careful that he is correctly aligned, so that any curvature does not come back as he recovers; and the quality of the damaged member will depend on what I have told you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	You know that broken members are diverse in size and shape and strength.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For some members are small, like arms and hands, and others large, like thighs and legs; therefore, it is necessary to wrap soft and thin linen around them. For the small ones, use narrow bands, three or four times around the member, and tighten your hand a little on each band, then go above the fracture and loosen it slightly, so that the fracture moves a little away from it; then soften the band little by little until you press strongly into the healthy part below. Then take another band and wrap it around again from the opposite side over the broken member; then return to the under-part of the fracture and tighten it moderately, neither too tightly nor too loosely, as we have said in the first part above; then place soft bands or linen strips between the bands, so that they are all even, then tie everything with a bandage, and put your well-made splints on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is a swelling or abscess, apply to it a hot soothing paste that removes the swelling and leave it for no days; then bind your stars tightly, and make them of half a broad cane cut sharply, or of wood used to make splints, or of palm fronds, according to this figure.
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the star placed on the break be a little thicker and wider than the others; and also as long as it should be for the member, whether small or large; then bind the stars just as you did with the first layer, and tie a thin thread over them, just as in the first layer over the fracture; tighter now, less later; and the thread must be medium, neither too thick nor too thin, and of soft flax; for if the thread is thick, it's like the works of foolish men who make their bands from twisted flax threads, and that's a great error, because the band cannot be even if it's too delicate, and it does not suit that there be less than two threads between each star.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is troubled by the roots of the stars after dislocating them in their joints, he should place soft cloth or any other dressing over them so that they do not get hurt.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is accompanied by fracture, and the blood vessels are broken, I will describe the treatment below.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not appropriate to dislocate all the stars of the fractured members on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the members are large, it is not appropriate to put stars (possibly referring to splints or bandages) until after 5 or 7 days, or more according to your judgment of the heat of the sore; and here you will see the ancient method of using plasters to restore fractures, dislocations, and torsions: take flour that clings to the walls of the mill, mix it with plenty of egg, and make this preparation, not too clear or too thick, and use it. This is the common method of using a plaster to restore fractures in various positions, especially for women and small children, as it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of plaster for restoring fracture and dislocation and torsion: take wolfsbane and nettle and hemlock and pestle and gum arabic and myrrh, each 3 parts; add mirror and aloe, each 5 parts; ales (alum) 7 parts; make it into powder and mix with egg white; if the man's body temperature is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and it restores broken bones severely, and it benefits many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another plaster method for torsion: take myrrh and wormwood, each 3 parts; mirror and aloe, each 7 parts; acacia 6 parts; Armenian bole 10 parts; grind well and mix with water or egg white, and apply.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another method of splinting joints and setting bones out of their place, to soothe the pain that comes from it, and use a saw on the bone, and the break: take a fresh cloth, and moisten it with hot water and oil, and lay it over the joint.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Cyst splints do not restore, but they are good for soothing hot abscesses, and properly extracting bones to relieve pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of splinting that restores broken bones: take dry fig leaves and earth poppy leaves, crush them together, and make a paste.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method of plastering for the restoration of a broken bone and to soften the return of the abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take the root of chamomile, camomille, violet flowers, and meal, from each part in equal measure; grind them and mix with wine, and apply to the affected member, heating it. Alternatively, mix with fresh coriander water or water, and use as needed.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another stronger method of plastering when a hard abscess forms during the restoration of the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of chamomile, and seeds of flax, balsam, melilot, and fennel, and flowers of violet and chamomile, from all these plants a portion; and grind them, and preserve with vinegar, or sweet water, or wine, according to the warmth of the member and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates writes in his book that to restore a broken member, one should apply a mixture of wax and oil, and nothing else, stating it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that Galen suggests applying dry, slightly warm substances to a broken member in order to restore it, such as myrrh and aloe, incense, and similar things, as we have mentioned.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another method of plastering that is effective against pain and injury: take the skin and feathers of a bird that has been skinned, or the quills of an eagle, and grind them equally fine, and make a plaster from it and bind it to the affected area.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then, after a little while, take care that the patient does not feel any pain, nor do the bones move from their place; if, however, the pain returns or itching appears, or swelling, act quickly, and remove the plaster immediately, and take a light cloth, and a moist sponge, and dip it in water, and apply it to the affected area, until the itching stops and the pain is soothed; then let the member rest for an hour, and place a dry cloth, moistened with water or rose oil, on top, and bind it with a nut, as long as you are certain of the warmth of the abscess. And thus relieve the inflammation of the affected limb, and remove the pain, and then continue the treatment with a delicate touch and a little plaster, not pulling too hard as before; gently until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is closed, red, painful and swollen, you have used hot compresses and binding, but it returns again as it did at first, then you must do it again just as you did before.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	If the limb shows no improvement after what we have said, do not dislocate it again until after three, four, five or seven days; and under no circumstances leave it for twenty days, as long as the fracture is open and the adjustment of the bone to the socket is progressing; then tighten it more than before and thicken the flesh, as I mentioned earlier. And if you see that the limb is drying out more than necessary, know that healing cannot take place; so raise the temperature with warm water each time you dislocate it, every third day, and loosen the bandage slightly. By this means, the healing of the limb will be improved, and do not underestimate the danger that these actions pose; I see nothing else but to let it rest and do it correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of various ways of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many ways of fracture, each with distinct forms and causes; for there are fractures caused by the impact of a sword, where the bone is completely shattered down to its marrow, as with a hatchet or axe; this type of fracture is therefore called "haichure" (axing).
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Or, the sword may cut through the bone without piercing it, and this is called "absolute" fracture; and the wound from these two types of fractures can be large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a sensation of pounding, or a cut, or a wound from a stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a recent fracture that approaches the skin just beneath or on the bone, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound that has healed is as subtle as a hair, and the fracture is small, this is called a "capillary" fracture; and if the wound was caused by a stone, or a blow, or a similar thing, and the bone fragment enters beneath the skin, and the limb becomes stiff like the blacksmith's arm when he works on the forge, then it is trapped between the bones.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this occurs more often in those with moist shoulders, as in an infant's shoulder; and it happens in all these ways of breakage that small fragments are dislocated, just as they are. And I will speak of it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all the ways of breakage through retraction upon them, and inquiry at close range, and through corrupt fat which is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of hair is known because when the bone is discovered and rubbed hard, it opens the break and reveals the black fragment.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, be cautious regarding complications with the patient's condition, and if you notice any adverse events such as vomiting, loss of consciousness, stiffness, pallor, fever, or other similar symptoms in various combinations, then recovery is unlikely without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any alarming symptoms, but still hope for a recovery, then commence the treatment.
