Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the fracture presents itself first, and it is in winter, then it is advisable to remove the bone before the fourteenth day after the injury.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if this happens, if you hurry to remove the bone on the seventh day, when the tissue under the bone is corrupted, then come the accidents that we have mentioned.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the fracture of the bone extends to the tissue that covers the brain, then you must split the broken part in this way: press down firmly on the patient's head to relieve the pain, and expose the bone in all ways possible, and tenderly uncover the wound, as much as you can, and if blood oozes upon exposing the bone, or pus comes from a wound, or an abscess forms at the site of exposure, then use this aid, and fill the cavity with moist, rose-colored cloth; then rest the wound until any abscesses are calmed and you are assured of no further discharge. Then begin removing the bone, and it is done according to two methods: one method is that you cut tightly before, and this is its form...
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then take another treatment even greater than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	The second method is that you have many different treatments, some narrow and others wide, and they are sharp and made of iron indelible; and perform them gently so as not to damage the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and strong, it is necessary that you make a cut around it, so as to administer treatments with caution, so that they do not go through the bone too deeply, and there should be a margin or a circle on top of the point, which does not allow the point to pass through the bone; and you need many of them, so that each one comes in its place according to the thickness of the bone, so that you have cautery for all parts; and this is the form of the three types of cautery:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality to discover the fracture of a bone is that you place pressure on it and return to your original position until you know the bone is broken; then, put pressure elsewhere a little later, and do this all around, then cut with incisions the space between the cracks in the bone, and do so as precisely as possible, gently, while still holding the bone in your hand or with any of the tools you have, such as pincers or pliers, and be careful not to touch the brain or the spinal cord.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have broken the bone and treated it, it is necessary to remove the tension that remains from the bone to all other tools similar to an incision tool, but it should be more precise and subtler than any other incision tool; and if it holds onto small bones or scales, gently lift them with the appropriate instrument; then dress the wound with bandages and remedies as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another method of treatment is that which Galen says, which is safer; it is very powerful, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is first necessary that you expose a part of the bone, either by opening the fracture widely, so that when you have exposed this part, you will place the tip of this curved knife beneath it, whose form is as follows:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side, but expose the acute part on this side, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then strike gently with a small mallet all around the bone, and be very careful of the tissue beneath; if it is away from the bone, gently pull it, for otherwise you will extract it with great pain and fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not reach down to the flesh, and the bone is only cut from above, leaving small fragments, then it is necessary to remove these rough edges with a fine scalpel, having various quantities of them at hand, in order to render each part as convenient as possible, according to the severity and shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you encounter great difficulty with razors, and then more subtle ones, never cease to do this until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other haircuts and subtle fractures, it is necessary to render them according to their location; and this is a matter that cannot be fully answered by anyone who has studied this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if it pleases him to be uncovered, then you should press the linen drape according to the size of the wound, moisten it with rose oil, and place it over the wound; then take another double drape in two or three layers, moisten it with wine and rose oil, and lay it over the first drape; do this as lightly as possible so as not to harm the patient, then apply a second bandage and do not tighten it too much until the wound is only covered; leave it like that for one or two days until the abscess has subsided, then loosen it and administer medicines such as fennel roots, flour of times (spices), incense powder, aristologus (a herb), and similar things; make a powder from these substances and apply it to the wound, and also give unmixed foreign medicines without burning; be sure that the wound is always clean, do not leave any dressing on it, nor allow bowing (scarring) to form, because when bowing occurs on the skin of the head, it corrots and destroys it, and does great harm to the patient; for when a sharp substance is placed over the syphilis, it hurts from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care then, if no bad accident comes to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if darkness comes not from the medicine that has been placed upon it, but to show its virtue, then you must apply a mixture of one part honey and three parts rose oil, and wrap it in a cloth; then cure the wound in the manner of cures that are appropriate, until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	You know that the two parts of the bone should never be broken, either together or separately, for they are two bones; and this inner part is cartilage, and does not break, but only bends or twists, then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, it is necessary that you insert your small finger or a pointed tool between the joints, and put this fracture back into place with your index finger and thumb, until the joint returns to its natural position; do this gently, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain due to your actions.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the upper part of the joint and the fingers cannot be moved to their original position, it is necessary that you place a slightly thicker ruler at the top of the joint.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the fracture is in both parts, do as you did before, and hurry to restore it on the first day if possible; if not, wait until the seventh or fifth day (after the abscess has subsided), then gently insert a thin piece of linen between the joints if the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or turn to another part, if it is broken; and make the splints so thick that they fill the openings of the bones.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they say that no restoration is required; one must soften the splints with butter, and change them each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	I do not think that is good enough, but it is advisable to soften them with egg yolk and flour powder; then remove the splints, as long as the bones are hard and the cartilage stiff.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And never should one burn the feathers of a goose in place of others, and if it pricks the patient around, and holds the wound closed, and blows air into it; do as you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses form at the new wound while you are working on it, apply a compress or cotton moistened in rose oil or in a poultice of dye.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If no abscess forms, apply a plaster made of flour, incense powder, confited with egg albumen, then place light bandages and do not tie the wound; and if the rupture at the wound is small and broken into small pieces, extract it with suitable instruments, then clean the cut, and treat the resulting charred and infected areas with appropriate plasters and dressings until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	from the dislocation of the mandible
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the mandible is dislocated, and there is no external wound, and the fracture is only slightly out of place, and not broken in two, but only shifted inside, then if you know it lightly, you can reset it.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the fracture is in the right side, you should push your index finger of the left hand into the mouth of the patient; and if the fracture is on the left mandible, then push your index finger of the right hand inside gently, and pull the fracture out with the other hand, making it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jaw is severe in two places, you should administer an extension to both parts, as long as they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the movement of the teeth occurs, or rupture, by applying tension with a golden or silver thread or silk, then place on the broken jaw cerate and cover with a double cloth; and on this cloth place a large well-made star or a piece of leather equal in length and width to the mandible, secure it to the muscles as best you can, and command the patient to rest and eat light meats.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	If you notice that the shape changes on the third day, remove the bandage and then reassess what has changed; apply a paste made of fine powder with egg or flour, after removing the cerate, and place a thin layer of this paste over the affected area. If the bandages become tight, do not change their position as long as the patient's condition does not change for the worse; in many cases, healing occurs within three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess appears, it is necessary to do as we have said many times before.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is both a fracture and a wound together, no part of the bone that is broken should be removed; it is necessary to carefully extract the suitable instruments.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, it should be widened with fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and it does not delay any longer, if the wound is wide, close it with suitable bandages to prevent infection, until it is healed.
de la forcele	of the forceps
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forceps break in many places, towards the shoulder, and the fracture is of three kinds: it may be broken and displaced in two parts, with fragments, and is the easiest to restore; or there may be a fracture with an accompanying wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And for the case where the fracture is without a wound, you shall have two assistants: one holds the aid that is broken; the other stretches the collar towards the affected part. Then, with both hands, set the fracture in its proper place, so that it forms as it should, and there is neither bulge nor deformity.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend it further, place a round spear of cloth or wool under the patient's shoulder, as thick as necessary; then stretch and gently pull on the spear, holding it firmly in your hand, so that you equalize the fracture, as appropriate.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the fracture away from the external side, because it is stuck completely, then the patient should lie on his side with his shoulder supported, and the healers should push the shoulder upwards, until the bone of the fracture is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then address the fracture to your advantage, and if you find any debris, it is appropriate to cut through it; pull the pieces gently, and if the bone cannot join together despite all efforts, use the instrument under the fracture to ensure the desired result.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and it should look like a spoon, and is not too small, and is as wide as necessary, according to the size of the bone and the ability of the work; and it has two parts, as you see, one wider, and the other narrower, just as the wound's rupture that you made when you treated the bones; and when you are certain of the hot abscess, if you cut the wound deeply, or if its rupture is small, then you doubt a hot abscess, if you cover the wound with cloth and bandages, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if hot abscesses occur, then moisten the cloth with rose oil and silk and wine, and place it on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The binding of the bone, when it feels wounds or cuts, is to place plaster made from fine flour and egg white on it, and add light stoppers below, and insert a spike under the armpit if necessary; then take a very wide bandage one palm in width, place two layers of cloth over the stoppers and plaster, then wrap the narrow strip around it, ensuring the top of the bandage is hanging down; place the thin piece of wood on the fracture, and turn the bandage back over the collarbone, removing it from the healthy armpit and the injured one; rearrange each part, and when you see that the binding holds the fracture well, and clearly see that the wood does not move over the broken bone, rewarding each day, and when the stitches loosen, tighten them again; put the patient on his back, and place a small pillow under the armpit while he sleeps, to raise the dislocated joint; if the fracture is relieved by aligning the shoulder, or you tie the arm to the collarbone, and no further accidents occur, leave it for 20 days; then repeat the plastering if needed, tighten it, and leave it thus until it is healed; healing usually occurs within 28 days, and in some cases sooner.
de la brisure de l’espaule	from the dislocation of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	If the shoulder is dislocated, it does not move in any way except through touch; if you put it back according to the shape of the dislocation and restore it to its natural state in every way that you can, then sprinkle a little fine powder on it, apply light bandages, and cover with a double cloth. Then place a wide and thin plate over it, slightly larger than the shoulder, and secure it firmly with straps so that the plate does not move from its place; check it each day. Whenever it tries to move, tighten the straps and return the plate to its correct position if it has moved. Lie the patient on his side, and be sure of it, for it is not a bone that can be easily put back in place.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone protrudes and is not removed from the inside, it causes inflammation in the abscess hotly, and the bone, and does as we have said in the calming of the heat of the abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	from the fracture of the worst
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The bone is never broken in the middle, but that happens rarely; but it often breaks at the extremities.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it declines to one side, and the patient feels great pain, and lack of strength, and sometimes bleeds, and opens up the wound in the broken bone, and feels much better.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies on their back, and puts a cushion between their shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and aligns the ribs with both hands, and subtly adjusts it in every way that you can, so long as the bone figure is as it should be; then apply poultices and compresses over the delicate salt or other light bandage, wrap it in a cloth, and secure it to the broken bone, so that it does not move; and return the ligament to its natural state on the back, tighten it properly, and check the wound every hour, and if it softens, tighten it; if it needs to be released due to decay or itching that arises at the site, or pain or abscess, act quickly, release it, remove the poultice, and address what has come about in terms of treatment; then reapply the poultice and tighten it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	from the fracture of ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	You know that the fracture of ribs only occurs in the upper back and at the top, and they do not bend except because they are broken; and anyone can feel it well with their hands.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is such that you put the fracture back in place as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply the plaster, and tighten it with a board, if you have such need.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the fracture of the ribs is declining inward, the patient feels great pain and stabbing, as if from crying out, because the bone pierces the skin; also it weakens the hands, and causes them to shake, and vomit much blood, which is a sign of grave illness, and ancient physicians have put much effort into it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And for those who say that it is necessary to administer foods that cause bloating in the stomach to expel the fracture outward.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make the mistake of thinking that an abscess will not come if it did not previously exist.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it comes, if the healthy one.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say that none of you should apply cupping glasses over the joint to draw out blood, for it seems reasonable; nevertheless, there is doubt that the cupping glass may attract excess fluids to the joint due to weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that none of you should cover the joint with moist wool in hot oil, and place tents between the ribs to evenly distribute the heat around it, then cure the pleurisy, the flesh, and with medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot endure through the bone where the fracture is, then doubt arises in the patient, and it is necessary to split open the broken rib, and place an instrument to hold it steady; and then one must cut the bone, pull gently, and sew together the two edges of the wound if it is large, and treat it with plasters until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses form, place moist, oil-soaked rags over them and on the affected area; treat it while the abscess is present, keeping the patient lying on their side where needed, until they heal.
de la brisure dou col	From the rupture of the collarbone.
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	No rupture occurs to the bone of the collarbone unless it rains; and also in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will recover, be on guard if you notice their hands becoming soft, swollen, and numb, and they cannot move or extend them, and if you prick them with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is deadly in many ways, and if they are motionless and feel well when you press them and there is no pain, know that the joint of the bone is safe, and the patient will be cured if proper treatment is given.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if similar things occur in the spine, you must know if there is health or sickness, if you see that the feet are limp and the accidents are in the hands, and the winds and emissions on the back without will; and when you remember it on the belly, it also does the same.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it is remembered on the back and it wants to attack, it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Knowing that it is deadly, one must not labor in its treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not happen, then it is a lighter matter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is as follows: if there is an abscess that is hot to the touch, apply warm rose oil or egg-white oil to it until it is soothed; then place a comforting and drying plaster on it and secure it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; and do not sleep on the affected area while it heals.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is separated, it should be covered with a bandage; then the bone is removed, and the wound's edges are sutured if they are large, using stitches, and treated with an ointment to promote healing; and if the fragment of bone is broken off, which is called the "fragment of the break," you press it back into place with your left hand, equalizing it with the other hand, then apply a plaster and a splint, if necessary; then tighten it, and if there are any further separated bones, reduce them and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	from the fracture of the bone in the shoulder blade
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	If the bone in the shoulder blade breaks, and there is not even a slight reduction in the pain at first; it causes long-term discomfort, declining towards one side, and brings to the patient pain, stabbing, and swelling where it breaks.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand above, as long as you are over the break; and know what the break is and its form; and if the break is only at the top, then put it back equally, as much as it was in its natural form.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long, it inclines inward, then make the patient lie on his stomach until the restoration of that fracture becomes visible.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have made it even, place a splint over it, then put a piece of wood or hard material on top and tighten the fracture so that it does not move; and keep the limb under the ribs until the ribcage is level.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	Instruct the patient to sleep on his healthy side or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if the abscess becomes closed and it is not touched, until the abscess beneath is calmed, apply what we have said above; then return to reduction, drawing it tight as appropriate, if there is no adverse event, this is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	dislocation of the shoulder joint
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The aid (or joint) is located between the shoulder blade and the top of the shoulder, and if it is dislocated, it must be reduced according to one of two methods: one is to take a wooden stick of medium thickness, in this shape:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And hold the two feet, pull them up, and place the patient on a seat; then break one of his arms over the thigh until it is dislocated, and put a piece of wood between his legs, then pull down any heavy object or have the assistant stretch it back into place; then arrange the broken arm so that the dislocation is even with both hands together, until the break returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And another method is that we place the patient on his side, and bind his hand to his neck, then instruct the assistants to grasp what is over the broken arm at his hands, and the others grasp each joint, and stretch them as best they can.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that extraction is too forceful, tighten the ligature around the rupture, and on the rupture, extend each of the assistants to their respective sides.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the rupture is near the shoulder joint, it is necessary to place a ligature halfway beneath the acromion and another towards the collarbone below the rupture; and likewise, if the rupture is on the side of the collarbone, it is appropriate to apply a slight ligature without strain, as long as the rupture remains balanced on the bone, then set the dislocation correctly and tighten it gently if there are no complications.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if an abscess appears, do not extract it for seven days; and put a moist cloth dipped in rose oil on the abscess until it is calmed; then extract it, and the manner of extracting it is that you place the plaster on the fracture, then reassemble the arm to the shoulder or breast, and cover with a drape, then extract from the joint and the arm, so that the arm is straight, unless something prevents it, or if the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	If you doubt that the bone does not move, use a wider and stronger splint than the others, and leave two spaces between each splint, so that each splint is large enough to pass over the fracture by three spaces on either side; then extract the splints as I said at the beginning of this chapter about the fracture, making them stronger and farther apart.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the position of the stars and the tightness, as we have said, when you return the broken member, and you doubt the heat of the abscess, leave it bound for seven days, as we have said; then every three days check the binding, that no swelling or pain comes to the place, or the healing cannot come to the limb because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If it is necessary, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accident happens, and the binding is not removed for three days or more, then have the patient lie on his back and keep his hands on his stomach; place under the dislocated limb a smooth cushion of equal thickness made of wool, and every hour during the day and night watch that the position of the dislocated member does not change, or the binding becomes loose. If it heals by the power of medicine and the patient is given food as we have mentioned above, in such a way that the food is first made fine; then when he begins to regain strength, it will be great.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the aid and leg should be taken in for forty days; and then one must loosen and administer baths and medicated oils to correct the place.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the contraction is severe and tight, it may take up to ten days or two months to loosen.
de la brisure du bras	of the breakage of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "fossa," of which one is small and supports the pouch; and the other is large, and is below the small bone; so it may happen that only the large fossa breaks, or only the small one, or both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small bones are broken, their restoration is light and rapid; but when the large ones are broken, the healing is slow, and more difficult than when they were broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is only the small bones that are broken, they should be gently extended and aligned evenly.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the large bones, they require stronger stretching; place them on a pillow, and position the palm of the hand higher than the others, with the small bones lower, crossing the patient over themselves, and the pillow in front of them higher than the rest, so that the patient feels no pain. Then have one assistant stretch the affected arm towards the joint closer to their body, while another assists above it.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then arrange them equally, according to their best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the fracture, each piece is put back in its place, and if there is no suitable one that grasps the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place by moving and the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the fracture there is a wound, I have spoken of it in the specific chapter; then take the cure.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if at the beginning of restoration there appear abscesses, I apply a bandage made of rosin oil and white wax, not too hard nor too soft; and I wrap it very gently until the abscess is calmed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then remove the plaster, and apply the pouder from the soft mill with plenty of egg, then place the needles, making the needle of the fracture stronger and a little wider than the others; and know that it should have six needles or more on each arm in various positions: whether the fracture is in one bone or two; and tighten more over the fracture than elsewhere, and less away from it, as I said at the beginning of this chapter; and make the cloths lying over the fracture soft and moist, and not hard or rough; and let the thread, from which it is bound, be linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the member and the ligament after no days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if no adverse event comes to the member, such as itching that appears on the member, then it is necessary that you immerse the member in hot water until the itching is soothed; and allow the member not to be tightly rested.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then repeat the process, and if the ligament is loosened and the bone is dislocated or any similar thing, address it accordingly.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the tension cannot be removed from the member because it is too tight, then you should gently loosen it and leave it for a few days until the inflammation subsides, and then tighten it again.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things we have said help the patient, then he should be loosened for up to 20 days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	If uncertain, then bind his hands to his chest, ensuring his collarbones are even, and guard against movement and reaching; let him sleep on his back. And know that this fracture is healed in 30 days or 45, or perhaps in 20 days, depending on the combinations and complexities of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	You know that on the back of the hand and on each finger there are often small fractures, and it brings only pain many times over.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And when the hand plant is broken or bent, it is necessary for the patient to cut a cross into it and place it straight in front of him equally; then he places his hand on a cloth extended on the table, and extends the broken bones with the help of assistants, putting them back in their proper places, as much as possible; and applies a plaster and compresses if an abscess forms, then he wraps it up with a linen cloth according to the size.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the rupture is near the belly of the plant, make a ball of cloth, and instruct the patient to press it onto their bruised limb; then take a long strip of cloth, and wrap it around as tightly as necessary, so that the pain in the heart is also great, like the plant on the hand.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is in the open air, it is necessary that you place a stick above and another under the plant, so that the hand is open and straight, then tie it tightly around the hand, and stop the blood flow between them.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture occurs in either of the fingers, it should be set evenly, as appropriate; and hold it with the plant, and if you see that a small stick needs to be placed to keep the fracture still, do so, and do not move it. And if the fracture is in the other fingers, like the index or any other, set them evenly, and bind them with the healthy finger next to it; or you can hold all of them together, which is better, or place a stick on top, as needed; and be careful during restoration and arrangement near the abscess, and support what comes, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	from the broken hip
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The hip bone is often broken, and one can clearly see it when it returns to its place in front and behind; its restoration is achieved by binding it tightly over the break, and on the other side.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his face, then extends each limb equally to its fullest extent; this is when the break is between the bones.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is near the root of the hip bone, one must bind the limb towards the knee, and the other binds below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And also if it is close to the knee, then loosen the ligaments of the knee, and extend it downward; then place the splint so that the bone is in its natural position, and then apply the plaster and bandage, so that no further injury occurs.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, let it subside, then return to your work and treatment; the bandage is made in this way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap the fracture with a hard bandage, doubling it in two or three layers, and remove the excess, then turn the leg until the heels reach the root of the toe, and insert a long thread between the thigh and the leg below the knee, and around the joint, and bring the end above; then turn back to the leg and thigh, and bandage again. Then place a splint with stars on top of the bone; then use eight layers of soft cloth between the leg and thigh to equalize the compression. Then tie three turns or four over the splint, and as you go higher up the splint, loosen it less; then take the two threads that you inserted between the leg and thigh, and tie three stars above them, and turn again to the top of the foot with the thread, until you reach below the ankle. And tighten it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it like this, so that no abscess or swelling occurs.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens, and the dislocation occurs, and you address what comes, as we have said many times; and if there are fragments of bone that have gripped, it is necessary to do so, if possible; and if it cannot be done, it is necessary to break the joint and pull it out strongly; and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never is the joint broken with such stars as in the aid of the leg or arm; nevertheless, such restoration does not please the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the joint is restored in L days, or a little less or a little more, according to the diversity of dispositions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	from the street of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	You know that in the street of the knee there is little rupture, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it ruptures, even just a crack or an opening, it affects every wound, and without a wound, and this feels very good.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that you put everything back in its place as much as possible; then apply an adhesive, and place a round plaster, if needed, and tighten it appropriately, then follow all the arrangements we have mentioned for other ruptures, such as a hot compress or anything similar; apply whatever is suitable to each case, as long as it heals.
de la brisure de la jambe	from the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	You know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is called "tibula" and the other "fibula"; and a fracture occurs in the same way as it does in the arm, and its restoration is identical to that of the arm; all the work is the same. And if both bones are broken together, the leg returns to its original state from every direction.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the small bones are broken, they turn forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if a large bone is broken, it causes great pain, and one can see it well, and the limb turns pale.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Then apply extension, and set it even, and tie the stars equally; but still, it is important to note that if the break is ugly, and there are several pieces, then the extension should be less and lighter; and align it according to your ability.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your task, take two strips of cloth that cover the leg on both sides, and stretch them from the knee to the ankle; then wrap two bands around it, tying them in the middle, and at this band, the leg cannot bend to the right or left, and so it is well; no one should administer anything along the length of the leg, and if it is made of cloth, place the leg to prevent movement, and make sure that the healing occurs properly at the fracture site or where there is an injury; and move the leg each day to see if there is any pus or other complications; treat it as long as it is healthy.
de la brisure des os dou piet	From the fracture of bones in the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no fracture, but the bones in the foot can be fractured and the joints dislocated, and there are various arrangements where this may occur.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if the bones in the foot are fractured and you see them stacked on top of each other, the patient will cry out with great pain on the affected foot, as if they wanted to go somewhere, and then place your foot on theirs, raising the broken bones, and press gently until they return to their proper place; then apply a splint and wrap it, placing a small wooden board under the belly of the foot, and securing it to the foot that has been treated, and use other things as needed.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three days or four have passed, if he loosens the bandage, for you will find the bones even, either broken or discolored.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if none of the bones are broken, but they are discolored, as we have said about the hand's bones, then place a narrow piece of wood along the length of the bone and make it slightly wider, and put the plank under the foot, applying pressure; and if there are two or three, or more, broken bones, place a piece of wood on each bone according to its quantity, wrapped in a linen cloth, and tighten the plank under the foot, and be sure to keep the end of the board against the belly of the foot.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you should not forget the other things I have said about other fractures, as we have mentioned; and treat each accident as it requires.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	On the fracture of the wrist bone.
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the wrist bone of a woman is fractured and the swelling subsides, then she should lie on her back with her rear end raised; then fill the cavity with cotton and pack it tightly. Afterwards, stand her up and gently press the cotton in and out, repeatedly, until it reaches the entrance of the wound, and the bone returns to its place with the cotton inside. When she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and after she has urinated, replace it, and do this for seven or eight days. If successful, a bladder from a goat will be used, and a straw tied around the gap, then the entire bladder inserted into the wound; blow on the straw until the bladder is completely inflated inside. The fracture will heal, and if you notice any pus, take a new bladder and repeat the process. Then fill it with cotton and leave it like this for as long as it takes to heal.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bones of the hand or foot are broken, restore them as we have said regarding the hip bone; and these breaks are not hidden from one who applies his knowledge and skill, and understands this book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For these breaks indicate various arrangements for the right way of restoration: understand this therefore.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	When the staff (or rod) is broken, take a goose throat and insert it into the break; then wrap cloth around it, and leave it for three or four days, and it will heal naturally.
de brisure avec plaie	from fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	For one who has a fracture with a wound, especially if it is great, such as the bone of the shin or shoulder or similar, it is necessary for him to be healed now, so that the healings we have spoken of bear witness.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, but the stiffness from the plaster remains, and you have no other remedy, then begin to restore the fracture in the same hour or on the same day, if the abscess does not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if the abscess closes again after opening it, allow the healing to continue until the abscess is calmed, and do not touch it for at least a day or a half-day, lest you bring about an ill consequence.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is visible upon exposing the heart, it is necessary that you place it gently in your hands with a slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension does not appear suitable to place equally in your hands, then take this instrument made of iron, with seven or eight fingers long, and adjust its width according to the amount of the wound; and for this purpose, it must be pressed firmly against the member during your work, and thin at the front, thickening towards the middle.
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche," so the dislocated bone must be placed back on top of the visible joint; and hold it in place once, until it returns to its original position and is even on both sides.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle and the instrument cannot properly grasp the bone, you must hold the head of the bone until the instrument has a firm grip.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot bring the bone back as we have said, with a suitable instrument such as a knife or scissors within your power, then remove the portion that is stuck in the bone, cauterizing and trimming any rough edges.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is brought back, and the patient feels great pain afterward, knowing that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you do all that it is in its place, then moisten the cloth with a dry black styptic wine, and arrange it properly; do not put any wax or other substance on the wound, lest it bring decay and corruption. Then administer stars (medicinal herbs) when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound exposed, and cover it around according to the amount of the wound, and be very careful that the wound is not constricted by the break; and often the foolish do this and bring death or corrosion to the patient, and the bindings should be gentler and softer than others.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is deep or large, and you doubt that a bad accident may come of it, as we have said, and you feel pain instead of relief, if it is not suitable to put bandages on it; but cover it with hard cloths, and bind them tightly.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days that the wound is beginning to close, then remove whatever you have put on it, and apply a healing dressing for wounds, such as a four-ingredient ointment or similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you dislocate the limb twice a day, in the morning and evening, as long as it remains swollen and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be separated in such a way that the bow of the joint gently moves downward.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if it is continually re-dislocated and cannot return to its original position, knowing that there are small fragments of bone, then you must clean the wound thoroughly and remove all these misplaced fragments which cause pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula or any other form of decay appears in the place, then it must be treated according to what is said in this chapter above.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when a bone is broken and opened up on a limb, such as the bone of the calf or the shoulder, or other large limbs, do not pull it, for many times death results, but let it heal until it rots; perhaps after 20 days or 30, then treat the wound if you can; if not, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	burns that come from the metal.
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often come after the healing of the burn, especially when it is near a joint, and it is a nasty sight to see the disfigurement of the limb; and in some cases, the member cannot perform its natural functions.
