Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care then, if we must administer medicinal substances that contract, such as aloe, incense, myrrh, sarcocolla, acacia, and similar others, so that you press any of these things, or all together, and conserve them with a contractive wine or with abundance of heat or with cold; and place them on the affected area, tightening it well, and do not loosen it for many days; then loosen it and begin again with another, until the swelling is removed; or you press a piece of good plaster, because the property of plaster is to remove all swellings from the limbs; and if the nodulation has already turned into hardness like stone, it is necessary to remove it, cutting off the excess above, and making the healthy part apparent; or you shave it with any razor, as long as it is removed, and cure it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	The weak member after treatment.
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is healed and the weak and delicate member remains, this can happen for many reasons: sometimes because it was bound too tightly and not properly secured as it should be; or because there are too many bindings and it cannot take on the normal movements of the limb; or due to excessive bleeding; or from too great and untimely movements; or because it has little blood in its body, making it weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and make the body firm, until the strength multiplies within it; then administer baths, give joy and comfort, then apply lead to the member, so that the lead draws on great movements, and often washes it with warm water, until the movement reaches the limb; and it returns to its natural state.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	After health, both members are twisted.
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the members are twisted after restoration and the bones are broken open, and the form of the member is ugly, yet it does not lose its natural function; do not believe the foolish ones who say one must break the member all over again, and many such follies have been done in our land. These actions are to be blamed, and great harm and perhaps death come from them. However, if the contusions and torture are fresh, then they should be raised with hot water, or softening herbs cooked, such as fennel leaves, roots, melilot, and similar things; and prepare a soothing plaster as follows: take the essence of fennel and mix it with goose fat or oil of sesame, and apply the plaster. Or you can use fig seeds ground with fine meal and similar medicines that reduce inflammation.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never should the node be broken because it is rubbed continuously and for a long time with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And allow the limb to move every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the stiffness becomes inflamed and hardened, like stone, it is necessary to break it with iron, if it is convenient to remove it all the way to the bone, with a delicate incision; and apply compression and care in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book on dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocations occur from no joint being in its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs from no cause, it is necessary to bring the limb back to its normal position immediately.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one delays, the limb swells, and by chance if it is reset to its place, it should not be moved at that hour when it is swollen; for this often brings about inflammation and other pains. However, once this occurs, make the patient better, then leave it until the abscesses have healed; then elevate the affected member with hot water and oil, and gently reset it, treating each limb as its cure comes to it in its proper place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on dislocations of the upper limbs from the hip to the toe.
des mandibules	of the jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It is often the case that the jaws become dislocated, and there are two types of dislocation: they may be slightly out of place, a bit bent, or entirely dislocated, hanging down towards the chest, preventing the patient from closing their mouth, holding saliva, and even moving their tongue during speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is minor, it may heal on its own with proper treatment.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is whole and complete, then you must reset it with haste, and not delay; and in such a way that the healers place the head towards the patient's malady, and gently pull the mirror with one of their hands at the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, so that the dislocation is from two parts; and let the other two hands be stretched out equally; and command the patient to soften his jaws and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And let the mirror be adjusted equally until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it returns to its place, especially when both jaws are together, then apply hot water and oil, gently resetting it; do not delay in returning it, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are brought back evenly, and the mouth of the patient is closed well without softening, place moistened cloth strips covered in rose oil and wax on them, then gently tie them with soft bands; and let the patient sleep on their back, with their limbs between two cushions, so that they do not move to the right or left, nor make any effort to increase [the pain], but consume light food as soon as the pain is gone and the jaws are healed; and then eat what they want gently, without opening their mouth to eat or drink until the jaw is completely healed and healthy.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if both jaws cannot be brought back to their original position within an hour and are not restored to their places, then fever and severe pain may occur, and perhaps intestinal ruptures, or vomiting of pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, then know it is a misfortune; and often death comes to him who experiences it, within seven to nine days.
de la forcelle	de la forcelle" translates to "of the fork
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The fork cannot be dislocated from any side within the depth of it, and it is never fully healed, especially when it is damaged, and one feels it greatly.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And its restoration is that the patient lies on his back and extends his arms; then he presses the joint in your palm, and it returns; then he applies the plaster and binds it, and tightens it; and the part which is opposite the shoulder cannot be dislocated; if it tries to, and it does not dislocate even once, then he must put it back in place as we have said; then he applies the plaster and the bandage, and tightens it, and instructs the patient to rest until he is healed; and thus the head of the shoulder is brought back into its place when it has returned to its proper position.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	From the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	You know that the shoulder is dislocated in three ways: one is when it dislocates at the acromion end; and the second is at the part of the scapula; and sometimes it dislocates above, which is rare; and it does not dislocate behind for the shoulder, nor inside for the nerves; and often it dislocates downward towards the acromion, especially in those who have little flesh, because it easily slips there; but in those who have enough flesh, it slightly shifts and returns slightly.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes it happens to no one that they experience a blow or fracture, and the shoulder becomes hot with an abscess, and they think it is dislocated because of that.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It is necessary that you test it, as long as you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And dislocations are known when they lean towards the joint, and make a distinction between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find between them a clear diversity; and you will find at the top of the shoulder a hollow, and by pressing on the shoulder blade, you can feel the top of the shoulder, just as if it were one. The patient cannot bring their hand to their side, nor make any movement; and if it is dislocated upward, unless it is completely hidden, you will find it clearly visible by touch; and this type of dislocation is not always easily reduced, especially when it is new, or the infection is in the joint.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the healer holds the patient's hand above the affected area, then places his palms below the joint, and pulls the joint upward with force; and he releases the hand and extends it upwards, then places it below; this will bring relief.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said, above the hands, after a few days, then it is necessary that the patient be bathed in hot water; and administer gently a mollifying and soothing preparation, such as a decoction of alder and fenugreek and melilot in water, and let him drink; then prepare a cushion with an equal amount of soft and firm wool under the affected area, and place the patient's heel on it, and pull the upper part of the shoulder gently, and treat the hand of the patient; and another healer should hold the head of the patient so that he does not move below; this will cause the shoulder to return immediately, and if you see that it is put in order according to this method: and make sure that you are present a man who is stronger than the patient; and position him straight against the ribcage, and pull the affected shoulder away from the joint, and pull the joint upward towards the chest, and another healer pulls the hand of the patient downward towards the stomach.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, so that anything heavy causes no harm to them, the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And it is also done in another way: take a long stick and insert it into the ground so that the end of it is as bright as a pistol, neither too thick nor too thin; then place it under the patient, but ensure there are soft rags on top, and the patient's arm is stretched downward from the other side, forming an angle; then the joint will return to its original position. If for any reason, out of all that we have said, the dislocation does not want to come back, this treatment should be performed: take a stick of great length and four feet in width, with a sharp point at the top, to be inserted entirely under the collarbone according to this form.
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then place a heavy cloth over the head, so it does not hurt the patient, and put the patient on their side; extend one arm above the head, and tie the limb to the patient's side, then place the arm on the narrow edge of a large wooden board, and let the hand hang down, and leave the body hanging from the other side: the joint will now be realigned.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is aligned in any way, it is necessary to put under the joint a piece of equal wool, then apply the plaster made of fine powder, with incense and egg white, over the entire shoulder and around, then remove the joint carefully, and tighten the bandage on the plaster, and press the hand against the collarbone, and let the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he move slightly, as long as the limb is comfortable, for it will heal faster; and then after a few days or seven, he moves it; and if it remains still and is not softened, it heals.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is out of place due to moisture or any other cause, it is necessary that you apply fire cautery at three openings, as described in the chapter on cautery.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and after seven days the dislocation still does not hold, and he cannot raise his arm high, then know that the nerve at the top of the shoulder is either cut, stretched, or softened; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is towards the worst, and the limbs, or behind, if it occurs through a blow, and stretch of the hands, and is attended by pain, another remedy should be applied; and treat until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And after healing comes cracking in the limb, and delay in movement; if the patient uses it many times, as long as the cracking persists, it will be lightened, and return to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	on the cost of dislocation
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	You know that the jointure in question is misaligned at the tips, and at the tips it returns; if it is misaligned from all sides, especially front and back, and the dislocation is not corrected, because one can clearly see it and feel it; and treats according to each shape.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the affected part with the healthy one, if you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	Because the joint is dislocated, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch the shoulder to anything.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary that you reset it in such a way that the pus forms and comes out, for if the pus forms but does not come out, it will be difficult to bring it back; and perhaps it cannot be brought back entirely, especially when it is at the rear; and it is worse than other dislocations, and causes greater pain, and perhaps death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is possible when it can be brought back, that you stretch his hand with both of yours; and his arms should be spread out, and the hands turned to the side according to the joint around, from inside and outside, and pull the joint together at his wrists or at the base of his palm, until he returns to his original position.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in the front, it returns when he doubles his hand to its original position, and turn the root of the palm towards the joint that is misaligned.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not want to return to its place, apply a strong extension; and have the minister extend the arm, and stretch it tightly so that it does not move during the extension. Then turn the arm in each direction after you have wrapped a double long and wide cloth around it; and when you see the joint aligned with his hand, seal the joint with no oil to soften it, then pull the joint back until it returns to its place. And once it is in place, apply dry plaster with egg white, make it tight, bend the arm towards the patient's chest, and leave it for several days, then release it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, loosen the bandage and leave it; and if you see that the joint is not properly aligned, repeat the plastering and bandaging, and leave it for several days, until it is firmly set; then loosen it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if the patient feels grief after the joint is reset, and it becomes stiff, bathe and gently rub it, applying pressure until it is relieved; or place a grease-soaked woolen compress on the joint, leave it for one day and night, then remove it, and give the patient a bath. And when he has sweated, rub the joint properly, then apply the compress again, and repeat this process two or three times until it is healed; and if you see that it remains stiff, apply a fine moist warm compress with butter, and wrap it up. It will return to its normal state.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The hand joint is misaligned and its return to normal is lighter than that of other joints. Nevertheless, it must be brought back to its original position carefully, immediately after it becomes dislocated, so as to avoid swelling or the formation of a hot abscess.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And when you bring it back, place the patient's hand on a table, extend their fingers, and ensure they are even, so that the palm rests on the joint, holding it until it returns to its normal position. However, you must check if it is in the correct position; then, place the patient on their back on a table, extending and bringing back their hand.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is on the back of the hand, let the patient place the back of his hand on a table, and look to place his hand over the appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, it is well; otherwise, if the strain of soothing embrocations does not cease, and it remains thus without restarting.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot endure it, and you cannot put it back in place after any number of days, then the joint remains twisted; and it does not harm the patient for as long as the hand is soft, and nothing can be drawn from it: then know that a nerve or an artery is cut; unless there is no other mechanism to draw out the case, and perhaps there is nothing else worth trying.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is dislocated, if you place the splint as we have said, then stretch it and hold it for a day, then release it and leave it thus.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is no fracture, then apply warm water moisture, and rub it until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	On the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	The fingers of the hand should never be dislocated at any joint, neither at the back of the palm nor at the base; then they are stretched and the dislocation is reduced in small movements until it returns, then hold the top of the finger, and bend it towards the part where it is separated; leave it for a day, and then reset it as you did before; do not tie it, as we have said, but release it at night, and move it, and relace it firmly; continue this often until it becomes tight, and do likewise if it is dislocated on the palm of the hand, or from any other side, until it heals.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	dislocation of the spine
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the spine or the collarbone is dislocated and there is no cure, the patient risks death due to the hastiness of the condition.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs of this are that the patient's extremities jump involuntarily, and they cannot hold them still, and often a limb becomes weak, or both arms or both legs, and sometimes the spine is bent to four parts; the part that bends backward is called "gypsiness". The cure for this is if the gypsiness originated in childhood: there is no cure or complete healing from it.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from a fall or percussions or similar things, the old ways of treatment speak in great words, without much benefit to him; but I have abbreviated it according to my understanding and formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the stiffness that comes to the penis in front, no one has a cure; and also that which comes directly to either side, and it is only the one properly located at the back that can be cured, as I say; and it is that the patient should be extended on his face equally in the first position, and have a tight hold from below so he does not move; then insert a stick into the head in the ground forming, and another at the anus, and tie a strap across the patient's ass, and one at the hips, and another at the thighs, and another at the knees, and another at the ankles; and these assistants know the straps, one on the head and others on the anus among the sticks; and they should be well fastened, the stick as we have said, and the nurse places her palms on the protruding spine until it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return with this treatment, take a table three feet long, cut through the wall from the inside, position the patient on their side, and turn the head of the table away from the wall; then place the center of the table over the pain; put both feet against the other side of the table, and press firmly until it returns to its place; and if you see fit, do it with a twist that turns towards the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And take two large splints, one for the patient's head from a strong arm, and another two for their feet, and make a space of about a palm length between each; and put in each splint a hole or make it twist correctly, so that they are firmly fixed in place, and do not move; and between these two splints, let there be one more small splint turning, so that the others also turn, and have each of these smaller splints about as long as a palm; to turn the larger splint, tie it towards the head with a string from among the knots attached to the larger splint, and another string towards the feet to the other end of the splint, and let all the assistants twist their respective splints until the pain is completely alleviated.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is even, apply a drying plaster with plenty of heat, then the pads, and then the end of a tablet three fingers long, which should adhere to the area of the gibbosity and the healthy part of the spine, then bind it with a strap, as we have said, and use the patient's subtle relief, until he is healed; and if any occurrence happens at the end of health, then it is appropriate to administer softening and soothing medicines, using the method that we have mentioned above; and never apply a piece of plaster, nor let its appearance appear in the rear spine, and be careful that it is not dislocation; and it is the bone that opens, so one must not have presumption, for perhaps death would come.
des dislocations de la hainche	Of dislocations of the spine
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	You know that the joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder only cause dislocations, unlike the other joints; and the hip joint is misaligned according to four parts: inside and outside, front and back; and more inside, less misaligned in front and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of its dislocation within is such that when you join the affected leg with the healthy one, it becomes longer, and the injured knee opens wider than the healthy one, and the patient cannot bend their knee; and this is due to the muscle that is swollen from an abscess above.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him who experiences this at death, it is that this event is contrary to what has been said before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of him who experiences it beforehand, it is that his leg is healthy according to the condition; nevertheless, do not bend the knee without pain, and if one wants to make them walk, they cannot do so before, and they retain their urine, and the anger swells, and when they look down, it passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him who experiences it afterwards, it is that he cannot extend or bend his knee, and one leg is more twisted than the other, and the anger is softened, and the foot is in a position opposite to the rest of the bones.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	They must reset this appearance of dislocation if it is an old dislocation that persists according to its nature, as there is no cure; and one must not let him have any presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And for the one whose dislocation is fresh, and it's of the four types of dislocation, you must act quickly, reducing the joint to its original position both inward and outward, and ensuring it moves freely to the right and left; then it will likely heal on its own and no other treatment is needed.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it doesn't heal in this manner, you must apply a strong compress and extend the leg with two hands or bind it tightly above the knee; other ministers should place their hands from above in such a way that they press his hands down towards his feet, then pull strongly on a tight ligature placed on the calf; others should hold his head with a strap; and all at once, upwards and downwards, until the patient is completely lifted from the ground and remains still.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common to all four limbs, and if the dislocation returns, as we have said, that is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If the dislocation is in a hidden place, it is necessary to treat it as follows: You must have the patient lie on his healthy side, then tie the tendon at the root of the thigh, and the one beneath the angle; then stretch the ligament towards the angle and towards the force. Then have other assistants grasp the patient's arms, and embrace the large tendon of the affected thigh, and extend it in a direction opposite to its natural position. It will return to its place now; and this method of dislocation is lighter than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot hold it in the manner we have said, then it is necessary that you tie together both feet of the patient with a strong soft ligature on both heels and knees; then let the sick leg be extended two fingers more than the others; then hang it over a post, and let it reach two arms' length above the ground; then command the minister to embrace the top of the thigh, and have other ministers hanging with the patient, who embrace the thigh, for the joints will now come together.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is external, if the patient lies as we have said in the case of the dislocated hip, then tighten the ligature precisely on the sick leg and also on the opposite side; then place two hot coals, one at the top and another at the bottom, and insert a third between the cuisses of the patient along the dislocation. Then surround it with moist cloths so that it does not hurt the patient, and let each minister extend towards him, and they should all place their hands equally on the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, that's good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If it does not return, put it on a table and press it as we have said in the previous section, and lay the patient on their healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is present, it is necessary to stretch the diseased leg forcefully, as I have said; and to alleviate the pain of being on the diseased limb, then press with the other hand and extend it downwards towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is at the outside, it is not necessary to extend the diseased limb downwards or lift it up on the table, but rather it should be placed as if the hip was dislocated in the previous section; and it should be on its face, with the leg extended as we have said before, and pressure applied on the joint against the table; and it will be at the right point when the patient extends their legs and they are even. Then tighten the stockings, apply a plaster, and bind with a bandage so that the hip does not move; and let it rest for three or four days, then remove the bandage and plaster, and make them walk gently until the limb is healed.
de la dislocation dou genoil	From the dislocation of the knee.
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The limb is dislocated in three ways: internally, externally, and posteriorly; but not anteriorly.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are that you command the patient to bend his leg at the knee, and if it does not yield at the knee, you know it is dislocated; and the restoration of all is that you make the patient sit straight, and extend his leg if he can, and place his face on your hands, and rest his foot on yours; then take hold of the thigh with your palms, and draw between your fingers, and bend both sides of the knee joint; and another assistant extends the foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that the leg yields slightly at the knee; and apply a poultice, and raise the leg at the knee and ankle together firmly for three or four days, then release it; and let not the patient move about, until the member is comforted.

de la dislocation dou talon	On the dislocation of the heel.
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heel is neither completely dislocated nor fully reduced, and it remains misplaced both internally and externally.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement. Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when the dislocation is slightly improved, it's important that you make the patient lie straight, and have assistants hold the leg apart from the knee, then grab the foot with your right hand, and with your left hand, twice, stretch the foot towards you; then extend it nicely upwards, and bring the foot back down; do this two times as we said, pinching and stretching the foot; if it comes back, that's good; if not, continue the treatment, for it will come back; and if it cannot return in this way, make the patient lie on their back on the ground, and have assistants firmly insert a stick between the patient's thighs, and bind them tightly so that the patient does not move; then each assistant holds the healthy leg from the ankle, and the dislocation will be re-aligned as they stretch it; then evenly place mirrors on both sides of the dislocation, and another assistant holds the intact leg at the knee, and the dislocation will return to its proper place.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when the swelling has subsided, apply an ointment and bandage, tighten the wrap around the leg, and secure the stirrups behind the ankle, ensuring the bindings are not too tight; then leave it for two or three days, and if the swelling is gone, loosen the bindings; then remove them on the third or fourth day, and the patient must walk for four days; and if he recovers before that, it is not fortunate that he will heal no further.

des dois	From two sources
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the eyes are dislocated, if they need to be nicely extended without strain, it is a light matter.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez. de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	From wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound appears with dislocation and it is desired to restore it, often the patient dies if one is not careful in its treatment; so be not presumptuous in its cure if you are unskilled in the art and have not practiced it for long, and be not hasty, but compassionate and slow. In the beginning, apply hot poultices to the abscess, and leave the patient in God's hands if there is no hope of recovery; but if there is hope, then immediately reposition the limb to its proper place, so that the abscess heats it; and when the limb is in place, administer soothing poultices to the abscess and treat the wound as appropriate, using desiccating herbs; and if with dislocation there are broken bones and small bones are damaged, fracture them and do as we have said for simple ailments; and beware of entering a path of fear, as I have said, for this is your salvation according to your Creator, and for the knowledge of your arm and body.
